201 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Burlington Northern, Inc. v. Superior


Nos. 84-2358, 84-2359, 84-2360, 84-2361


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


131 Wis. 2d 564; 388 N.W.2d 916; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 1898


June 3, 1986, Argued  
June 25, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion For Reconsideration Denied August 15, 1986, with costs. ABRAHAMSON, J., took no part.


PRIOR HISTORY: On certification from court of appeals.

Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Douglas County, Douglas S. Moodie, Reserve Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the circuit court is reversed. The cause is remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff iron dock operators sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Douglas County (Wisconsin), which granted defendant city's motion for summary judgment in the operators' action challenging an occupational tax on iron ore concentrates.


OVERVIEW: The iron dock operators brought an action against the city challenging an occupational tax on iron ore concentrates. The lower court entered judgment in favor of the city. Upon appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the tax exemption found in the tax statute, Wis. Stat. § 70.40, violated the Commerce Clause and that that provision was not severable. The court found that the tax scheme demonstrates a discriminatory effect on interstate commerce. The court held that § 70.40 discriminates against taconite produced in another state by effectively favoring the state produced iron ore concentrates, including taconite pellets, which were exempt from taxation under the dock tax. The court held that the effect of severing the exemption for state mined metallic minerals from the iron ore concentrates dock tax was contrary to the manifest intent of the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment entered in favor of the city.

 

202 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


Nos. 82-377-CR, 82-891-CR, 84-1245-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


131 Wis. 2d 220; 388 N.W.2d 601; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 1900


April 2, 1986, Argued  
June 24, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Originally reported in 113 Wis. 2d 497, 335 N.W.2d 376 (1983). Reversing and remanding 125 Wis. 2d 111, 370 N.W.2d 827 (Ct. App. 1985).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision of the court of appeals reversed; cause remanded to the circuit court for vacation of judgment and further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motions prior to, during, and after his trial for murder concerning evidence and a subsequent confession obtained in a warrantless search and arrest at defendant's home.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the appellate court's decision that affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motions prior to, during, and after his murder trial concerning evidence and a subsequent confession. Upon hearing defendant snoring in his home, police entered without a warrant, arrested defendant, and obtained a confession two hours later. The court reversed the appellate court's decision, and remanded the matter for vacation of judgment and suppression of defendant's confession and any other evidence that was the fruit of an illegal warrantless arrest made without exigent circumstances in violation of constitutional rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11. Despite the illegality of the arrest, the court found that the trial court maintained personal jurisdiction over defendant pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 939.03.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision, and remanded the matter to the trial court for vacation of judgment and suppression of defendant's confession to murder and all other evidence that was the fruit of an illegal arrest.

 

203 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bangert


No. 85-1179-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


131 Wis. 2d 246; 389 N.W.2d 12; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 1892


April 30, 1986, Argued  
June 24, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On bypass of the court of appeals.

Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Eau Claire County, Arthur A. Cirilli, Presiding Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County (Wisconsin) which denied defendant's post-conviction motion to withdraw his plea of no contest to second-degree murder. The court granted the state's petition to bypass the court of appeals under Wis. Stat. § 808.05(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with a police officer's murder. He pled guilty to second degree murder, but moved to withdraw his plea. The motion was denied and he appealed. He argued he should be allowed to withdraw his plea as a matter of right because the plea hearing record was insufficient to show he understood the nature of the charge and the colloquy was facially insufficient. He also argued the state breached the plea bargain agreement and a second change of venue for the trial violated Wis. Stat. § 971.22(3). The court found that although the plea colloquy was insufficient to ascertain defendant's understanding of the nature of the charges against him, the totality of the circumstances, including the record made at the hearing on the motion to withdraw, established the plea was knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently entered. The court found that Fed. R. Crim. P. 11 procedures were not constitutionally incumbent on state courts when accepting guilty pleas. Moreover, any breach of the agreement was neither material nor significant. Finally, defendant waived any venue arguments in his no contest plea and the changes were not, in any case, illegal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision to deny the motion to withdraw the guilty plea.

 

204 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fry


No. 85-0625-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


131 Wis. 2d 153; 388 N.W.2d 565; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 1888


April 30, 1986, Argued  
June 20, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from the court of appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Washington County: James B. Schwalbach, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court for Washington county is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of conviction entered in the Circuit Court for Washington County (Wisconsin) for carrying a concealed weapon, asserting that the trial court erred in refusing to suppress evidence found in an illegal warrantless search of a locked glove compartment in his vehicle. He urged that the search was not incident to an arrest under Wis. Stat. § 968.11; the Wis. Const. art. I, § 11; or the U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of carrying a concealed weapon, Wis. Stat. § 941.23, and was sentenced. The trial court denied his motion for a new trial and he sought review, asserting that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence found in an illegal vehicle search which was not incident to his arrest under Wis. Stat. § 968.11; Wis. Const. art. I, § 11; or U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court accepted the appellate court's certification of the appeal and affirmed. It held that the test for a search incident to arrest under § 968.11 agreed with constitutional standards. "Immediate presence," in § 968.11, describing the area from which a defendant might gain possession of a weapon or destructible evidence, conformed to a constitutional case law test that defined a permissible search incident to arrest to include an arrestee's person and the area "within his immediate control." Wis. Const. art. I, § 11 protections conformed to those in the U.S. Const. amend. IV. The search of a locked glove compartment did not violate the U. S. Const. amend. IV because all closed containers in an automobile, whether locked or unlocked, could be searched incident to an arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for carrying a concealed weapon. The trial court properly admitted evidence found in the search of the glove compartment of defendant's vehicle incident to his arrest. All closed containers in a vehicle could be searched incident to a lawful arrest under the state and federal constitutions.

 

205 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Federated Rural Electric Ins. Co. v. Kessler


No. 84-552


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


131 Wis. 2d 189; 388 N.W.2d 553; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 1890; 40 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P36,350


June 4, 1986, Argued  
June 20, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Reversing 126 Wis. 2d 513, 376 N.W.2d 868 (Ct. App. 1986).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This was a review by writ of certiorari of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which determined that petitioner employer's work policy prohibiting relations with married persons violated respondent city's prohibition against discrimination in Madison, Wis., General Ordinances, 3.23(2)(1). Respondent city equal opportunities commission had held to the same result in finding in favor of respondent employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed a complaint with the commission, alleging he was terminated in violation of the ordinance because the employer terminated him based on his relationship with a married co-worker. The commission upheld the challenge. That decision was re-evaluated by several decisionmakers, and was ultimately upheld by the lower appellate court. The employer brought this appeal by way of a petition for a writ of certiorari. The court found the ordinance did not prohibit the employer's policy. The policy was designed to uphold a viable public policy and the policy did not discriminate against married persons. Since the policy did not discriminate against married persons, the policy did not violate the ordinance. Since the policy did not impermissibly discriminate against the class of married employees, reliance by the employer on its policy in terminating the employee was a permissible action in the employment at will relationship. The lower appellate court conducted a flawed analysis and its decision could not be upheld.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and determined that the employer's policy was not discriminatory.

 

206 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Disciplinary Proceedings against Schalow


No. 84-1709-D


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


131 Wis. 2d 1; 388 N.W.2d 176; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 1829


April 30, 1986, Submitted on briefs  
June 12, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion For Reconsideration Denied July 28, 1986, with Costs. ABRAHAMSON J., took no part.


PRIOR HISTORY: Attorney disciplinary proceeding; attorney's license revoked.



DISPOSITION: IT IS ORDERED that the license of James C. Schalow to practice law in Wisconsin is revoked, effective the date of this order.

IT IS FURTHER ORDERED that within six months of the date of this order James C. Schalow pay to the Board of Attorneys Professional Responsibility the costs of this disciplinary proceeding.

IT IS FURTHER ORDERED that James C. Schalow comply with the provisions of SCR 22.26 concerning the duties of a person whose license to practice law in Wisconsin has been revoked.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of a report of a Wisconsin Board of Attorneys Professional Responsibility referee in which the referee concluded that the attorney had engaged in unprofessional conduct in two matters and recommended that his license to practice law in Wisconsin be revoked.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected the attorney's arguments that the board lacked jurisdiction to commence a disciplinary proceeding against him because he had resigned from the bar and that procedural errors required remand or dismissal of the proceeding. The court further held that it was unnecessary to either plead or prove the torts of conversion or misrepresentation in order to establish that an attorney had violated a rule of professional conduct proscribing attorney conduct involving dishonesty, fraud, deceit or misrepresentation. The court found that the attorney's participation in a venture with investors and their money more closely approximated that of an attorney than merely of a fellow investor, that he encouraged the investors to rely on his position as an attorney, and that he insisted that investment funds be deposited in his attorney trust account. The court concluded that the attorney used his position as an attorney to gain control of the investors' funds and that his subsequent misappropriation of those funds constituted professional misconduct, notwithstanding the absence of an attorney-client relationship between himself and the investors.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the attorney's license to practice law in Wisconsin be revoked, that the attorney pay the costs of the disciplinary proceeding, and that the attorney comply with the provisions of Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 22.26 concerning the duties of a person whose license to practice law in Wisconsin had been revoked.

 

207 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Borello v. U.S. Oil Co.


No. 84-1880


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


130 Wis. 2d 397; 388 N.W.2d 140; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 1823; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P11,009


February 10, 1986, Argued  
June 4, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of an order of the court of appeals.

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision of the court of appeals affirmed and cause remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff victim brought a personal injury action against defendants, the furnace manufacturer, the furnace installer, and the insurer, for injuries which she alleged were caused by the furnace. The Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) reversed the trial court's dismissal of the complaint for being untimely. The installer, the manufacturer, and the insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: Shortly after the furnace was installed, the victim complained of a bad odor. She suffered numerous symptoms, which she attributed to the furnace, but which home tests and doctors' diagnoses did not confirm. Nearly two years after the furnace was installed, a doctor diagnosed her physical condition as the result of metal fume fever caused by the furnace. The victim filed suit within three years of the doctor's diagnosis. The manufacturer, the installer, and the insurer argued that the three year statute of limitations ran before suit was filed. The court disagreed, holding that the victim's cause of action did not accrue until the nature of the injury was or ought to have been known to her. The mere knowledge of the fact of an injury or a lay person's belief or hunch that a defendant was the cause did not trigger the period of limitations. This was not a reinstatement or revival of a cause of action or a retroactive extension of a limitations period. The retroactive application of this discovery rule posed no judicial administration problems as it neither stated a new concept of liability nor defeated the interests of persons who relied upon the former rule.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower appellate court, which reversed the trial court's dismissal of the victim's complaint for being untimely, and remanded for further proceedings.

Milwaukee Brewers Baseball Club v. Wisconsin Dep't of Health & Social Services


No. 85-0855


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


130 Wis. 2d 56; 387 N.W.2d 245; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 1818


November 25, 1985, Argued  
May 12, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On bypass of the court of appeals.

Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order of the circuit court is affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded to the circuit court with directions to remand to the Department for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the Wisconsin Department of Health and Social Services, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted a motion for a temporary injunction filed by petitioners, a baseball club and others, to stay the construction of a prison. The court remanded the case to the Department to take corrective action.


OVERVIEW: The Department planned to build a prison. The entrance to the proposed site was across the street from one of the entrances to a stadium parking lot. Petitioners filed an action against the Department, challenging its Final Environmental Impact Statement (FEIS). Petitioners moved to stay construction of the prison until the Department filed a FEIS in compliance with the Wisconsin Environmental Policy Act. The trial court granted petitioners a temporary injunction. On appeal, the court found that petitioners had standing to challenge the location of the prison. There was a close causal connection between the alleged injuries to petitioners and the building of the prison. It was not the psychological effects on the fans of having prisoners in close proximity to the stadium that concerned petitioners. They alleged that as a result of the prison being constructed, there would be added traffic congestion to already congested highways, and that the prison would be aesthetically displeasing, thereby keeping fans away from the stadium. The court remanded the case with directions to remand to the Department for a contested case hearing on the disputed issues of material fact.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.

 

209 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Milwaukee Brewers Baseball Club v. Wisconsin Dep't of Health & Social Services


No. 85-0164


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


130 Wis. 2d 79; 387 N.W.2d 254; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 1903


November 25, 1985, Argued  
May 12, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Modifying and affirming 126 Wis. 2d 512, 375 N.W.2d 220 (Ct. App. 1985).

Review of an unpublished decision of the Court of Appeals reversing the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Judge Angela Bartell.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is modified, and, as modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a baseball club and restaurant owners, appealed from a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed a judgment and declined to hold as unconstitutional certain statutes relating to the construction of a prison. Cross-Appellant, the Wisconsin Department of Health & Social Services, challenged the order that held the siting provision, Wis. Stat. § 46.05(1o)(a), violated Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18.


OVERVIEW: The state authorized the construction of a number of new prisons. As to one such location, the legislation provided for "expedited" administrative and judicial review procedures applicable to environmental review of the site, and precluded the Department of Health & Social Services from holding a contested case hearing on the final environmental impact statement. The legislation also directed the courts as part of this "expedited" process not to enjoin construction of such a facility due to alleged defects in the environmental impact statement unless any parties who sought the injunction proved, by clear and convincing evidence, that any defects could not be remedied during the construction phase of the project. The court held that these provisions violated state constitutional protections of due process, because there was no rational basis for the differing legislative classification for one area over those others in the state that were afforded the constitutional guarantees. However, the court held that the prison siting provisions were constitutional.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was modified, and, as modified, affirmed. The two provisions which related to special administrative and judicial review procedures violated the Wisconsin Constitution's guarantee of equal protection, and they were therefore stricken. The provision that directed the Department of Health & Social Services to construct a particular prison did not violate the Wisconsin Constitution in either respect.

 

210 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williquette


No. 84-2046-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


129 Wis. 2d 239; 385 N.W.2d 145; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 1807


February 11, 1986, Argued  
April 16, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 125 Wis. 2d 86, 370 N.W.2d 282 (Ct. App. 1985).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a decision from the Wisconsin Court of Appeals, which reversed the decision of a trial court that held petitioner's acts did not constitute parental child abuse within the meaning of Wis. Stat. § 940.201.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, a parent, knowingly allowed her spouse to repeatedly abuse her children physically and sexually. When she was tried for child abuse under Wis. Stat. § 940.201, the court dismissed the case. On appeal, the court of appeals reversed. The court affirmed the court of appeals' decision. The parent, by knowingly permitting another person to abuse the parent's own child, subjected the child to abuse within the meaning of § 940.201. Criminal liability for omissions was not abolished by Wis. Stat. § 939.10. Although a person was generally under no duty to protect another from hazardous situations, the parent was under a duty to protect her children. Wis. Stat. § 48.981(2), which required professionals to report suspected child abuse, did not relieve parents of their common-law duty to protect their children. Section 940.201 was not unconstitutionally vague where applied to parents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of appeals' decision, because petitioner knowingly permitted another person to abuse her child and this conduct fell within the meaning of Wisconsin's statute against child abuse.

 

211 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


North Side Bank v. Gentile


No. 85-0822


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


129 Wis. 2d 208; 385 N.W.2d 133; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 1809


March 4, 1986, Argued  
April 16, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On bypass from the court of appeals.

Appeal from a declaratory judgment of the Circuit Court for Racine County, Honorable Dennis J. Flynn, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order and amended judgment of the circuit court is reversed and rights declared.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dentist sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which held that respondent bankruptcy trustees could pursue funds in a pension trust to satisfy their claims against his bankruptcy estate, and that Wis. Stat. § 815.18(31) (1983-84), exempting employee pension plans from execution, was contrary to Wis. Const. art. I, § 17 because it was unreasonable.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issues were whether (1) all creditors of the dentist were required to be named as parties in a declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of the exemption statute; (2) Wis. Stat. § 815.18(31), which exempted qualified pension plans from seizure by creditors, violate Wis. Const. art. I, § 17, which gave the legislature the power to create laws that exempted a reasonable amount of property from seizure by creditors. Upon review, the court held that the bankruptcy trustees were acting in the interest of the dentist's creditors and could therefore have pursued a declaratory judgment without all of the creditors being named as parties, and that § 815.18(31) was constitutional. Based on the purposes served by exemptions and by pension plans, the legislature conformed to the constitutional mandate by exempting a reasonable amount of property in Wis. Stat. § 815.18(31). A qualified pension plan may have helped provide the dentist and his family with the necessary comforts of life. Section 815.18(31) was constitutional, and the trustees failed to prove it unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The order and amended judgment of the circuit court was reversed.

 

212 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Weber v. Cedarburg


No. 84-965


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


129 Wis. 2d 57; 384 N.W.2d 333; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 1789


February 10, 1986, Argued  
April 2, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 125 Wis. 2d 22, 370 N.W.2d 791 (Ct. App. 1985).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which dismissed the citizen's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against appellees, a city, a police chief, a police sergeant, and his wife. The husband alleged that appellees, acting under the color of state law, directed a pattern of official police surveillance of him without any basis for believing he had committed a crime.


OVERVIEW: The lower court had concluded that the husband failed to adequately plead a cognizable constitutional deprivation because no Fourth Amendment deprivation was alleged. The husband had not pleaded that appellees had search or seized his person, house, papers, or effects. Instead, the husband alleged constitutional violations of his privacy rights on the basis that appellees conducted surveillance upon him while he attended softball games and socialized in taverns. On appeal, the husband contended that he had sufficiently alleged an action pursuant to § 1983 because: (1) the conduct of appellees was committed under color of state law; and (2) such conduct deprived him of rights, privileges, or immunities secured by the United States Constitution. The court held that the husband's claim was without merit as a matter of law because he had failed to alleged that he had been deprived of any constitutionally protected right. It was unreasonable for the husband to allege that he had either a subjective or objective expectation of privacy in his attendance at softball games or in his tavern-going, as both activities were in plain view of the public.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court, which dismissed the husband's action.

 

213 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Kramer v. Horton


No. 84-762


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


128 Wis. 2d 404; 383 N.W.2d 54; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 1658


February 10, 1986, Argued  
March 13, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 125 Wis. 2d 177, 371 N.W.2d 801 (Ct. App. 1985).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant university sought review of the judgment from the court of appeals (Wisconsin), which denied its motion to dismiss and determined that the university had deprived plaintiff employee of a protected liberty interest without due process of law. The employee, a tenured music professor, had filed an action against the university seeking relief under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for the deprivation of his property right and liberty interest.


OVERVIEW: After the employee had been reassigned from rehearsing with a quintet to teaching, the employee filed a grievance petition with the university committee. The university committee informed the employee that the department executive committee was the appropriate forum for review of the reassignment. After the employee had filed an action with the circuit court, he sought review of the reassignment with the department executive committee. The department executive committee affirmed the reassignment. The employee then appealed to the chancellor, who denied the appeal. The circuit court found in favor of the employee and held that exhaustion of administrative remedies was not mandatory in a § 1983 action. Reversing the judgment on appeal, the court held that prior to commencing his § 1983 action, the employee was required to exhaust all of his administrative remedies. The court found that there were adequate administrative remedies available to the employee, but he failed to avail himself of them. The employee should have petitioned the board of regents for review of the chancellor's decision. Further, the court found that the employee failed to prove the inadequacy of the remedies.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's denial of the university's motion to dismiss the employee's action alleging deprivation of a property right and a liberty interest.

 

214 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cissell


No. 84-891-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


127 Wis. 2d 205; 378 N.W.2d 691; 1985 Wisc. LEXIS 2752


October 1, 1985, Argued  
December 23, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 124 Wis.2d 776, 370 N.W.2d 293 (Ct. App. 1985).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed and the cause is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals, which affirmed the decision of the trial court that defendant's constitutional rights to due process and equal protection of the law were violated by charging him with a felony and ordered that the charge against defendant be reduced to the misdemeanor of nonsupport.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with felony abandonment. Wis. Stat. Ann. § 52.05(1), and misdemeanor failure to support, Wis. Stat. Ann. § 52.055(1). Defendant contended that statutes with identical substantive elements but different penalty schemes violated due process and equal protection. Defendant argued that disparate sentencing exposures for crimes with identical elements was irrational and arbitrary. The court held that identical element crimes with different penalties did not violate due process or equal protection. The court also concluded that § 52.05(1), was not void for vagueness because the statute informed a person charged with abandonment that he must have willfully failed to satisfy his duty of support to his spouse or children. The court held that this standard provided adequate notice of the conduct proscribed by the statute to those who must obey it and a defined standard for those who must enforce the law and adjudicate guilt. Accordingly, the court reversed the decision of the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court affirming the trial court's decision reducing the charge against defendant to misdemeanor nonsupport.

 

215 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Disciplinary Proceedings against Haberman


No. 84-1572-D


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


126 Wis. 2d 411; 376 N.W.2d 852; 1985 Wisc. LEXIS 2589


October 29, 1985, Submitted on briefs  
November 26, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for reconsideration pending. This motion was not decided at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of a referee's recommendation, among other things, that his license to practice law be suspended for two years for unprofessional conduct which included neglect of certain legal matters entrusted to him and which included failure to cooperate with investigations by respondent Board of Attorneys Professional Responsibility.


OVERVIEW: The attorney was disciplined for his neglect of seven estate matters in which he acted as attorney or personal representative. He was also disciplined for his failure to cooperate with the Board's investigation into two of those matters. He contended that the court, the Board, and the referee all lacked jurisdiction over the disciplinary proceeding as long as the estate matters were pending in circuit court. The attorney also contended that he had a constitutional right not to testify or produce records to the Board. The court held that (1) it had the inherent power to discipline attorneys and that, despite the attorney's contention to the contrary, a circuit court had no authority enforce the Code of Professional Responsibility or to discipline attorneys appearing before it except by the use of its general contempt power; and (2) an attorney's failure to answer questions, furnish documents, or present relevant information to the Board was misconduct and thus, the attorney had no constitutional right not to testify or produce his records. The court accepted the referee's report and recommendation.


OUTCOME: The court suspended the attorney's license to practice law for two years, it ordered him to turn over certain files to the Board, it ordered him to file a complete accounting with the circuit court, and it ordered him to pay a fine for contempt.

 

216 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wyss


No. 83-818-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


124 Wis. 2d 681; 370 N.W.2d 745; 1985 Wisc. LEXIS 2407


April 3, 1985, Argued  
June 28, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 120 Wis. 2d 677, 356 N.W.2d 495 (Ct. App. 1984).

Review of a decision of the court of appeals reversing a judgment and order of the circuit court for Dane county: P. Charles Jones, Judge.
State v. Wyss, 120 Wis. 2d 677, 356 N.W.2d 495, 1984 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4078 (Wis. Ct. App., 1984)



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision of the court of appeals is reversed and judgment of conviction is reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment convicting him of first-degree murder and from an order denying his postconviction motion. The Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) reversed the judgment and order, finding that, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 752.35, defendant was entitled to a new trial in the interest of justice. Under Wis. Stat. § 808.10, the State petitioned for review to test the propriety of the court of appeals' grant of discretionary reversal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's wife was found lying dead on the floor in the basement recreation room of the marital home. Although there were multiple knife wounds, a pathologist determined that the victim died soon after her throat was slashed from ear to ear down to the vertebra. Based on circumstantial evidence, defendant was convicted of first-degree murder. Noting the lack of any physical evidence and a certain juror's lack of candor, the court of appeals granted defendant a new trial in the interest of justice. The state sought review. The court reversed, holding that the court of appeals erred as a matter of law in granting the new trial without finding a substantial degree of probability that a new trial would produce a different result. The court concluded that the evidence was strong enough for a jury to exclude to a moral certainty every reasonable hypothesis of innocence. Such evidence included defendant's extremely jealous nature, his statement a year previous that someday she would find her throat slit, his distraught statements overheard by his daughter shortly after the victim's body was discovered, "Why did you get drunk? Why did you make me mad at you?"


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals' grant of discretionary reversal. Accordingly, defendant's conviction for first-degree murder was reinstated.

 

217 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Newspapers, Inc. v. Circuit Court for Milwaukee County


No. 85-0461-W


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


124 Wis. 2d 499; 370 N.W.2d 209; 1985 Wisc. LEXIS 2391


April 30, 1985, Argued  
June 26, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for reconsideration pending. This petition was not decided at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for supervisory writ.

Petition for a supervisory writ.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The petition for a supervisory writ is granted. The stay of further proceedings before the circuit judge in Petition of K.M. ordered by this court on March 7, 1985, is vacated. It is ordered that further proceedings in that matter shall be conducted in accordance with this opinion. The petition for review from the court of appeals' decision is dismissed. No costs are awarded to any party.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, various media organizations, requested the issuance of a supervisory writ, pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 809.51 and 809.71, commanding the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) to conduct in public a Wis. Stat. § 968.02(3) hearing that involved the alleged sexual assault of a victim by two famous football players.


OVERVIEW: The underlying criminal episode concerned an alleged sexual assault by two professional football players upon the victim, a female dancer, in the dressing room of a Milwaukee nightclub. The incident received substantial attention in the state media. The football players claimed that the incident was consensual. The victim asserted that there was no consent. After investigating the incident, the district attorney refused to issue a criminal complaint based on his perceived inability to prove guilt at trial, not on the basis of lack of probable cause. The victim then petitioned for the assignment of a judge to issue a complaint under Wis. Stat. § 968.02(3). The trial court, at the Wis. Stat. § 968.02 hearing, ordered closure of the proceedings. The court held that such proceedings were presumptively open to the public and could have only been closed upon a showing of a substantial, compelling reason to do so. The court found that the trial court abused its discretion by concluding that there was such a compelling reason to close the hearing. Therefore the court granted the petition for a supervisory writ.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition for a supervisory writ.

State ex rel. Hennekens v. River Falls Police & Fire Com.


No. 83-1894


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


124 Wis. 2d 413; 369 N.W.2d 670; 1985 Wisc. LEXIS 2394


May 28, 1985, Argued  
June 24, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for reconsideration pending. This petition was not decided at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: 121 Wis. 2d 699, 361 N.W.2d 310 (Ct. App. 1984).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed in part, reversed in part, and the cause is remanded to the circuit court for remand to the police and fire commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent police and fire commission sustained a chief of police's five charges against petitioner police officer and ordered that he be removed from the police department. The officer challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed an order upholding the commission's ruling regarding the second, third, and fourth charges. The commission challenged the judgment reversing the order regarding the fifth charge.


OVERVIEW: The officer was charged with violating the department's rules. The commission sustained the charges. A circuit court upheld the commission's decision. The court of appeals found that the fifth charge failed to give the officer adequate notice of his alleged violation but affirmed the circuit court's order regarding the other charges. The court held that charges two and three were sufficiently detailed to allow the officer to prepare an adequate defense. Charge four was sufficiently specific, but the commission was not proceeding according to law when it sustained charge four. No evidence was presented to support a finding that the officer violated the police department rule against unsavory associations. The facts presented at the suspension hearing did not fulfill the legal standards of the police department's rule against associations. Charge five was devoid of sufficient facts to apprise the officer of his alleged violation. Therefore, the commission failed to act in accordance with due process guarantees with regard to that charge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeal's decision that affirmed the order upholding the commission's ruling sustaining charge four. The court affirmed the decision to reverse the order sustaining the commission's conclusion regarding charge five and to affirm its conclusions regarding the remaining charges. The court remanded the cause to the circuit court for remand to the commission.

 

219 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kramsvogel


No. 84-017-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


124 Wis. 2d 101; 369 N.W.2d 145; 1985 Wisc. LEXIS 2383


January 30, 1985, Argued  
May 29, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 119 Wis. 2d 902, 350 N.W.2d 743 (Ct. App. 1984).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed and the cause remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a circuit court order dismissing a criminal complaint charging defendant with criminal damage to property, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 943.01. The complaint was dismissed on collateral estoppel and double jeopardy grounds, finding that defendant had been convicted in a municipal court for the same acts which formed the basis for the state's charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant plead guilty to violating Town of Pleasant Prairie, Wis., Ordinance § 9.03.1. (1983) for his disorderly conduct. The state filed a criminal complaint charging defendant with criminal damage to property, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 943.01. The criminal complaint was dismissed on double jeopardy and collateral estoppel grounds. The court reversed the dismissal and remanded. The court held that the double jeopardy clause prohibited only multiple criminal punishments. The municipal proceeding against defendant was a civil action. The legislature intended the penalty imposed by the ordinance to be a civil penalty, and there was not clear proof that the forfeiture assessed against defendant was punitive. The court concluded that the municipal civil action did not bar the subsequent criminal prosecution, even though both proceedings concerned the same actions of defendant. The court also held that the doctrine of collateral estoppel was not applicable because defendant plead guilty to the municipal violation and, therefore, no facts were established against the state, and there was a lower burden of proof in civil cases than in criminal actions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals' decision, which had affirmed the dismissal of the state's criminal complaint charging defendant with criminal damage to property, on collateral estoppel and double jeopardy grounds. The prior municipal proceeding against defendant for the same acts was a civil action, and double jeopardy or collateral estoppel did not bar the state's criminal complaint. The cause was remanded for further proceedings.

 

220 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mann


No. 84-044-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


123 Wis. 2d 375; 367 N.W.2d 209; 1985 Wisc. LEXIS 2215; 79 A.L.R.6th 731


April 3, 1985, Argued  
May 9, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 120 Wis. 2d 629, 357 N.W.2d 9 (Ct. App.).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed and the cause is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed defendant's conviction of leaving the scene of an accident. The appeals court ruled that there was no probable cause to find a violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.67(1)(c), because defendant had fulfilled his statutory obligation to remain at the scene of the accident and provided reasonable assistance.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court ruled that there was no probable cause to find a violation of §§ 346.67(1)(a) and (b), because it was futile to give a name, address, and vehicle registration to an unconscious person, as the victim of the accident was in such a condition. The appeals court also ruled that there was no probable cause to find a violation of § 346.67(1)(c), because defendant had fulfilled his statutory obligation to remain at the scene of the accident and provide reasonable assistance by asking a woman to summon help. The court reversed the appeals court decision and remanded the case holding that in examining the face of the amended criminal complaint, the court found facts sufficient to find probable cause, even assuming the inclusion of the facts asserting that defendant asked one woman at the scene to get help. The court held that § 346.67(1)(c) required a person involved in an accident involving injury or death of any person to render such a person "reasonable assistance" and that the trial court erred in concluding as a matter of law that defendant's actions constituted conduct complying with the statutory requirements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appeals court which affirmed the judgment of the trial court that had found no probable cause existed to have arrested defendant for failure to render assistance at an accident scene. The court remanded the case to the trial court.

State v. Douglas


No. 84-453-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


123 Wis. 2d 13; 365 N.W.2d 580; 1985 Wisc. LEXIS 2202


October 31, 1984, Argued  
April 3, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 120 Wis. 2d 673, 353 N.W.2d 844 (Ct. App.).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a pretrial order suppressing the introduction into evidence a note found on defendant's bedroom floor 45 hours subsequent to permissive entry by police into defendant's home.


OVERVIEW: Defendant called 911 to request police assistance after he shot to death his mother and two sisters. He stated he wanted police to meet him in the basement of the home. After arresting him for murder, the police returned the next day, entered defendant's bedroom, and found a written note lying on the bedroom floor. In affirming the suppression of the note, the court found that entry into the home for investigative purposes had not been justified by consent, exigent circumstances, or a warrant. Pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. IV principles, a warrant was required to enter defendant's home approximately 45 hours after the implied consent was given and 22-1/2 hours after other investigative activities in the home had ceased because the continuation rule did not apply. The court held that the passage of time vitiated the initial consent and that the interruption in investigative activities and the subsequent investigation and scene reconstruction factually and analytically separable.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

222 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Bell v. Elkhorn


No. 84-327


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


122 Wis. 2d 558; 364 N.W.2d 144; 1985 Wisc. LEXIS 2191


January 30, 1985, Argued  
February 27, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from the court of appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Walworth County: Robert D. Read, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which denied plaintiffs' request for a declaratory judgment and upheld an amendatory zoning ordinance of defendant city.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs challenged the amendatory zoning ordinance, claiming that the existence of a formal comprehensive plan was a condition precedent to the adoption of a valid zoning ordinance. Plaintiffs additionally argued that the rezoning of certain property constituted illegal spot zoning and that the commercial shopping district portion of the zoning ordinance was unconstitutional for failure to limit the city's legislative discretion. The court held that the ordinance itself was a "comprehensive plan" as required by Wis. Stat. § 62.23(7)(c). No separate comprehensive plan document needed to be adopted by the city as a condition precedent to enacting the amendatory zoning ordinance. The court additionally determined that the amendatory zoning ordinance did not constitute spot zoning. Finally, plaintiffs had not met their burden of overcoming the presumption of validity that the ordinance enjoyed. Because the validity of the commercial-shopping portion of the ordinance was fairly debatable, the ordinance had to be upheld.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying plaintiffs' request for a declaratory judgment.

 

223 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Quinn v. Dodgeville


No. 82-1932


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


122 Wis. 2d 570; 364 N.W.2d 149; 1985 Wisc. LEXIS 2192


January 30, 1985, Argued  
February 27, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 120 Wis. 2d 304, 354 N.W.2d 747 (Ct. App.).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of the trial court granting summary judgment to respondents, a town, three town board members, the county, the county clerk, the county zoning administrator, and the county zoning and planning committee, in his action to have Wis. Stat. § 59.97(5)(e)(6) declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The property owner's property was zoned agricultural and the property owner sought to have it rezoned so that he could open a business on it. The county zoning and planning committee recommended the denial of the property owner's petition. After the county board of supervisors rejected the recommendation of the committee, the committee adopted a resolution vetoing and disapproving the county board of supervisor's action in rezoning the property. Upon review, the court held that the court of appeals correctly affirmed the grant of summary judgment to respondents. Wis. Stat. § 59.97(5)(e)(6) facilitated the responsible development of local county/town land use by a unified county/town board governmental structure. The power to locally zone was shared between town and county governments and that fact accentuated the importance and value in deliberative land use development. As such, the statute violated no constitutional provision. There was no abuse of discretion, excess of power nor error of law by the circuit court or the court of appeals, and the property owner failed to prove the unconstitutionality of § 59.97(5)(e)(6) beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the affirmance of the granting of summary judgment to respondents in the property owner's action to have the statute declared unconstitutional.

 

224 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Caibaiosai


No. 83-2330-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


122 Wis. 2d 587; 363 N.W.2d 574; 1985 Wisc. LEXIS 2193


January 3, 1985, Argued  
February 27, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion For Reconsideration Denied April 30, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: On certification from the court of appeals.

Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County: Earl D. Morton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of violating Wis. Stat. § 940.09(1)(a) by operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, which resulted in the death of another. Defendant filed a post-conviction motion for a new trial, which was denied. Defendant filed a notice of appeal. The court of appeals (Wisconsin) certified the appeal to the Wisconsin Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was intoxicated when he crashed his motorcycle, which killed his passenger. Defendant argued that Wis. Stat. § 940.09(1)(a), which proscribed the crime of homicide by an intoxicated operation of a motor vehicle, was unconstitutional because it did not require a causal connection between the intoxicated condition of the operator and the death of another person. The court disagreed. The court stated that the statute required that the prosecution prove and the jury find beyond a reasonable doubt a causal connection between defendant's unlawful conduct, operation of a motor vehicle while intoxicated, and the victim's death. The statute did not include as an element of the crime a direct causal connection between the fact of defendant's intoxication, conceptualized as an isolated act, and the victim's death. The legislature determined the activity was so inherently dangerous that proof of it need not require causal connection between defendant's intoxication and the death. Accordingly, the court affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

In re Disciplinary Proceedings against Solomon


No. 84-1674-D

February 11, 1985  
February 11, 1985, Filed

State ex rel. Watts v. Combined Community Services Bd.


No. 84-1107


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


122 Wis. 2d 65; 362 N.W.2d 104; 1985 Wisc. LEXIS 2110


November 26, 1984, Argued  
January 31, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion For Reconsideration Denied April 30, 1985, without costs.
Reconsideration denied by State ex rel. Watts v. Combined Cmty. Servs. Bd., 122 Wis. 2d 65, 366 N.W.2d 896, 1985 Wisc. LEXIS 2213 (Wis., 1985)


PRIOR HISTORY: On bypass of the court of appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County. John E. McCormick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In separate cases, petitioners alleged that the state's protective placement scheme set forth in Wis. Stat. § 55 violated constitutional guarantees of due process and equal protection. Except for ordering the release of one petitioner who claimed that she was being illegally confined in an acute psychiatric ward, the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) denied both petitions. Petitioners appealed.


OVERVIEW: At one time or another, petitioners were involuntarily hospitalized pursuant to the state's protective placement scheme set forth in Wis. Stat. § 55. Unlike the state's civil commitment statute, Wis. Stat. § 51, protective placement was allowed to be indefinite in duration even though both laws required treatment in the least restrictive alternative. The state supreme court held that Wis. Stat. § 55 denied protectively placed individuals equal protection of the law by failing to require periodic automatic court review of the individual's need for guardianship and protective placement. Moreover, Wis. Stat. § 55.06(9)(d)-(e) violated equal protection because they allowed involuntary mental hospitalization of protectively placed wards without the requirements of the mental commitment law. In other words, Wis. Stat. § 55.06(9)(d)-(e) denied protectively placed individuals basic procedural protections that were available to other persons facing involuntary hospitalization. In short, there was no "rational basis" for the lack of periodic judicial review of confinement under § 55 and the lack of substantive and procedural safeguards pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 55.06(9)(d)-(e).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

227 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martin


No. 83-1401-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


121 Wis. 2d 670; 360 N.W.2d 43; 1985 Wisc. LEXIS 2106


November 1, 1984, Argued  
January 10, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review of an order of the court of appeals.

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant was convicted of armed robbery and second-degree felony murder, he was sentenced to two consecutive 17-year terms. The trial court vacated the conviction and sentence for armed robbery, as a lesser included crime, but, over defendant's objection, increased the sentence for second-degree felony murder from 17 to 20 years, the statutory maximum. The Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) affirmed, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Contrary to defendant's contention, the trial and appellate courts held, and on appeal, the court agreed, that the trial court had the inherent power to change and modify its sentence even after defendant had commenced serving his sentence. Furthermore, increasing defendant's sentence for second-degree felony murder did not violate his federal double jeopardy protections, because the initial sentence was illegal. This was because, by the interdependent nature of the offenses involved, by attacking the armed robbery conviction defendant in reality attacked both sentences. Defendant having been convicted of and sentenced for two offenses that were in fact the same offense, and the sentences for both offenses had been illegal. Thus, resentencing on the valid conviction was permissible. The court also held that the trial court did not err when it increased the sentence without requiring new objective factors justifying a more severe sentence, because identifying new factors was not required when the initial sentence was illegal. Finally, the trial court at resentencing properly implemented the original dispositional scheme rather than exercise independent discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which vacated defendant's conviction and sentence for armed robbery, and which increased defendant's sentence on his conviction for second-degree felony murder.

State v. Hamilton


No. 83-1539-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


120 Wis. 2d 532; 356 N.W.2d 169; 1984 Wisc. LEXIS 2871


September 6, 1984, Argued  
October 30, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from court of appeals.

Appeal from a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County, William U. Zievers, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of obstructing a police officer contrary to Wis. Stat. § 946.41(1) (1981-82).


OVERVIEW: Defendant refused to provide identifying information to a police officer as he was investigating some windows that had been shot out at a residence. Defendant was convicted of obstructing a police officer contrary to § 946.41(1). The trial court denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and held that there was insufficient evidence to prove that defendant obstructed the police officer. The court ruled that no reasonable trier of fact could be convinced beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant hindered, delayed, impeded, frustrated, or prevented the police officer from performing his duties in violation of § 946.41(1). The court held that the only reasonable inference to be drawn was that defendant's refusal to furnish information did not affect the investigation. The court ruled that the legislature had not stated that a refusal to furnish identifying information was deemed to be an obstruction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

State ex rel. Palleon v. Musolf


No. 82-1487


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


120 Wis. 2d 545; 356 N.W.2d 487; 1984 Wisc. LEXIS 2872


October 1, 1984, Argued  
October 30, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 117 Wis. 2d 469, 345 N.W.2d 73 (Ct. App.).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent lodge members appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision that they were not entitled to tax exemptions in an action brought by petitioners, the Wisconsin Department of Revenue, the Wisconsin Tax Appeals Commission, and others, after an applicant for membership complained that the members had rejected his application because he was black.


OVERVIEW: The Department received a letter complaining that an applicant had been rejected for membership in a lodge because he was black. He requested that the Department investigate the tax exempt status of the lodge. The lodge had no black members, no black had applied for membership before the applicant, and his was the only application to be rejected in a five-year period. According to the admission procedure, the applicant was sponsored by two members, he was given a favorable report by the investigative team, and the lodge's board recommended him for membership. In spite of all that favorable reporting, he was rejected. The Department found that he was rejected because of racial discrimination, and it removed the lodge's tax exempt status. The decision was reversed by the trial court, but the appellate court affirmed the Department's decision. The members sought review. The court affirmed, holding that the only reasonable explanation for the applicant's rejection was his race, and that discrimination eliminated the organization from preferential tax treatment and exemptions by the government. An organization that received tax exemptions could not discriminate because of race.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Department's decision that the lodge was guilty of racial discrimination in its membership.

 

230 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rodgers


No. 82-1930-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


119 Wis. 2d 102; 349 N.W.2d 453; 1984 Wisc. LEXIS 2589


March 29, 1984, Argued  
June 12, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 115 Wis. 2d 118, 339 N.W.2d 605 (Ct. App.).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State of Wisconsin, challenged the order of Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the order of the circuit court that had dismissed the false imprisonment charges against defendant because the warrantless arrest of defendant in his home was unconstitutional because the consent to enter the home was obtained from the defendant's mother by deception.


OVERVIEW: Two deputies went to defendant's home to arrest him without a warrant for battery and false imprisonment. Defendant's mother answered the door and the deputies asked for permission to enter the home to talk to defendant. The deputies entered the home and arrested defendant. Defendant gave a verbal and written statement. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss. The circuit court granted the motion, which was upheld by the appellate court. The State appealed. The court reversed and found that the mother had voluntarily consented to the entry into her home. The deputies identification of themselves and request to enter to speak with defendant was all the information the mother required to make a decision. The proper test for voluntariness of consent under U.S. Const. amend. IV was whether under the totality of the circumstances the consent was coerced. Defendant was not entitled to a presumption that the consent was involuntary and coerced. There was nothing in Wis. Stat. § 968.07 or Wis. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 11 that required application of a different standard.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the appellate court, which had affirmed the order of the circuit court that dismissed the charges against defendant.
