In re Grady


No. 82-2234-J


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


118 Wis. 2d 762; 348 N.W.2d 559; 1984 Wisc. LEXIS 2583


January 4, 1984, Argued  
May 30, 1984, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This matter was before the court to review the findings of facts, conclusions of law, and recommendation of the judicial conduct panel in a judicial disciplinary proceeding brought by petitioner Judicial Commission against respondent judge.


OVERVIEW: The Judicial Commission instituted disciplinary proceedings against the judge for his willful or persistent failure to perform his official duties. The panel recommended that the judge be reprimanded for his persistent failure to be prompt in the performance of his official duties, to organize his court for the prompt disposition of judicial business, to decide matters within the time period provided by Wis. Stat. § 757.025, and to file affidavits pursuant to that statute accurately reporting the status of undecided cases. The court held that § 757.025 was an unconstitutional intrusion by the legislature into the area of judicial decision-making, as the setting and enforcement of time periods for judges to decide cases was an area of authority exclusively reposed in the judicial branch of government. As such, the judge could not be punished for violating the statute; however, the judge was reprimanded for his failure to perform his official duties by promptly disposing of cases, his failure to organize his court for the prompt disposition of judicial business, and for knowingly making a false statement regarding his caseload.


OUTCOME: The court reprimanded the judge for his persistent failure to perform his official duties and for making false statements concerning his caseload.

 

233 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Field


No. 82-1330-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


118 Wis. 2d 269; 347 N.W.2d 365; 1984 Wisc. LEXIS 2453


February 2, 1984, Argued  
May 2, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from court of appeals.

Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Calumet County: Hugh F. Nelson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a commitment order of the Circuit Court for Calumet County (Wisconsin), which was issued after the third phase of his trial, at which he was found to be presently mentally ill and a danger to others. Defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder after the first phase of his trial and not guilty by reason of mental disease after the second phase.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed the trial court's order to the court of appeals, which certified the case to the court. The court framed the issue for review as whether Wis. Stat. § 971.17(1) (1981-82), which allowed the automatic commitment of a defendant found not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect, violated the Due Process Clause or the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution, or Wis. Const. art. I, § 1. The court overruled State ex rel. Kovach v. Schubert, 64 Wis. 2d 612, 219 N.W.2d 341 (1974) and affirmed the commitment order. Defendant argued that the trial court denied him due process and equal protection of the laws by finding him presently mentally ill and dangerous without taking testimony at the third phase hearing. Based on a decision of the United States Supreme Court, the court ruled that there was no constitutional requirement for a hearing after defendant was found not guilty by reason of mental disease, or for a finding that he was presently mentally ill and in need of institutionalized treatment. The commitment order was allowed to stand regardless of any error that might have occurred during the trial's third phase.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which committed defendant for institutionalized treatment after he was held not guilty of first-degree murder by reason of mental disease or defect.

 

234 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Enright v. Board of School Directors


No. 82-2158


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


118 Wis. 2d 236; 346 N.W.2d 771; 1984 Wisc. LEXIS 2449


March 28, 1984, Argued  
April 24, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion For Reconsideration Denied, with Costs, June 5, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: 114 Wis. 2d 124, 338 N.W.2d 114 (Ct. App.).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, administrator of a deceased child's estate and his parents and siblings, challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed an order of the trial court dismissing plaintiffs' civil rights claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, filed as part of a wrongful death action against defendants, a school board, a school secretary, an insurer, and others alleging that the secretary's negligence led to the child's death.


OVERVIEW: A child was strangled by a man who had been reported to the school's secretary as suspiciously watching the children on the playground. The secretary admitted that she forgot to report the incident, remembering the call only after the child was discovered dead near the school. The administrator of the child's estate and his parents and siblings filed a wrongful death action that included a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim. A police captain gave testimony that if the man's behavior had been reported to the police, they would have investigated, because the man could have been arrested for loitering or taken into custody for a psychiatric evaluation. The § 1983 claim was dismissed on the basis that because the wrongful death statute provided a satisfactory means of redress for the child's family, they did not suffer a deprivation of any constitutional right in connection with his death. On appeal the court affirmed, finding that, although mere negligence on the part of a state actor did not preclude an action under § 1983, the state remedy afforded the family to compensate it for the tragic death of the child was adequate to satisfy the requirements of due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals that affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing plaintiffs' civil rights action against the school board, the secretary, an insurer, and others, for negligently contributing to the death of a child.

 

235 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burroughs


No. 82-1238-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


117 Wis. 2d 293; 344 N.W.2d 149; 1984 Wisc. LEXIS 2302


January 4, 1984, Argued  
February 28, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from court of appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County: Richard G. Harvey, Reserve Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of second-degree assault in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(a) and sentenced him to an indeterminate term of not more than eight years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of second-degree assault in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(a) and was sentenced to an indeterminate term of not more than eight years. Defendant sought review and contended that his counsel ineffectively represented him by failing to file a notice of alibi pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 971.23(8). The court found that § 971.23(8) required notice of alibi even when the alibi consisted of nothing more than defendant's uncorroborated testimony that he was elsewhere at the time of the offense. The court held that evidence of alibi included any testimony placing defendant somewhere else at the time of the crime. The court determined that a mistaken interpretation of the requirements of the statute or even total lack of awareness of the existence of the statute was insufficient to constitute "good cause." The court held that the trial court properly excluded defendant's offered testimony regarding his alibi. The court further held that the failure to allow such testimony had not violated defendant's right to testify. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of second-degree assault and sentenced him to an indefinite term of not more than eight years.

 

236 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re R.W.L.


No. 82-1093


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


116 Wis. 2d 150; 341 N.W.2d 682; 1984 Wisc. LEXIS 2274


November 30, 1983, Argued  
January 4, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from court of appeals.

Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Menominee and Shawano Counties: Michael G. Eberlein, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, alleged father, challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Menominee and Shawano Counties (Wisconsin), which denied the alleged father's motion to dismiss a paternity action commenced by respondent, a guardian ad litem for a minor.


OVERVIEW: The minor, through the guardian ad litem, commenced a paternity action against the alleged father. The trial court denied the alleged father's motion to dismiss the action as barred. The court affirmed the order, holding that the action was not barred. The court overruled J.M.S. v. Benton, 98 Wis. 2d 406, 297 N.W.2d 18 (1980) and held that the pre-1981 paternity statutes did not provide an exclusive remedy or forum for a child to establish paternity. Thus, prior to the 1981 statute, the minor had a right to bring a declaratory judgment action to establish paternity independent from the Wis. Stat. ch. 52 procedure commenced by the district attorney. Before the adoption of the 1981 statute there apparently was no statute of limitations applicable to the minor's commencement of a paternity action. Thus, as of the commencement of this action, the minor had a cause of action to establish parentage and for paternal support which was not barred by any statute of limitations. Accordingly the action was brought timely and should not be dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying the motion to dismiss and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

237 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Beno


No. 82-387


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


116 Wis. 2d 122; 341 N.W.2d 668; 1984 Wisc. LEXIS 2273


October 4, 1983, Argued  
January 4, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 110 Wis. 2d 40, 327 N.W.2d 712 (Ct. App.).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, state legislator and aide, sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) that held that the aide was not protected by legislative privilege pursuant to Wis. Const. art. IV, §§ 15, 16 and reversed a circuit court order quashing a subpoena issued to the aide by defendant wife of a taxpayer in an action to compel the wife to comply with an audit of the taxpayer by plaintiff State of Wisconsin Department of Revenue.


OVERVIEW: After a previous appeal and remand, the wife learned that the aide had stated during a settlement conference in another case that the taxpayer was about to be indicted for tax fraud. Alleging that the department had abandoned its civil tax purpose, the wife subpoenaed the aide. The court held that the aide was protected by a constitutional legislative privilege. The wife's subpoena to the aide was within the definition of "civil process" in Wis. Const. art. IV, § 15, but the privilege created by § 15 could be invoked only by the legislator. It was not available to the aide because the legislator had not been subpoenaed. The legislative privilege created by Wis. Const. art. IV, § 16, however, protected the aide because its objectives were implicated when a legislator was called to testify as a witness in a judicial proceeding, the legislative activities in question were within the regular course of the legislative process, and the legislator could invoke the privilege created by § 16 because the aide was acting as an alter ego. The privilege was not waived by the aide's divulgence of the information because its purpose was to prevent questioning of the legislator.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals that had held that the aide was not protected by a constitutional legislative privilege and had reversed the circuit court order quashing the subpoena issued by the wife to the aide in the department's action to compel the wife to comply with its audit of the taxpayer. The circuit court orders were affirmed.

 

238 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Midland Financial Corp. v. Wisconsin Dep't of Revenue


No. 82-396


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


116 Wis. 2d 40; 341 N.W.2d 397; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 3221


October 31, 1983, Argued  
December 29, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 110 Wis. 2d 261, 328 N.W.2d 866 (Ct. App.).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Wisconsin Department of Revenue challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which upheld the reversal of the Department's decision and held that dividends were not other items of income under Wis. Stat. § 71.06 (1971) and did not reduce the business loss carry forward for 1971 of respondent corporate taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: In 1971 and 1972, the taxpayer, a Wisconsin corporation, operated as a bank holding company. It owned a controlling interest in four banks through an ownership interest in two other corporations. In 1971, the taxpayer received dividend income from its subsidiaries, which it included as gross income. It then deducted that dividend income from its gross income under Wis. Stat. § 71.04(4) (1971) and reported a net loss in 1971. This amount was carried forward as a loss and used as a deduction in 1972. After an audit, the Department reduced the 1971 loss of dividend income received in 1971 under Wis. Stat. § 71.06 (1971) and regarded the dividends received by the taxpayer as "other items of income," which reduced the taxpayer's 1972 loss carry forward and increased its 1972 taxable income. The court held that the Department erred when it reduced the taxpayer's loss carry forward and that dividends were not includable in calculating the business loss carry forward under § 71.06. The court further held that the taxpayer met the requirements of Wis. Stat. § 180.787 (1971) by filing its petition appealing the Department's decision a year before the taxpayer's dissolution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

239 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State Public Intervenor v. Wisconsin Dep't of Natural Resources


No. 82-111


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


115 Wis. 2d 28; 339 N.W.2d 324; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 3201


September 7, 1983, Argued  
November 1, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Richard W. Bardwell, Judge. On certification from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court for Dane county is modified and as modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State of Wisconsin Public Intervenor sought review of a judgment entered in the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which held constitutional an administrative code adopted by respondents, Wisconsin Department of Natural Resources and Natural Resources Board, pertaining to the removal of material from the beds of waterways. Respondents cross-appealed from the trial court's decision that the public intervenor had standing.


OVERVIEW: The public intervenor brought a declaratory judgment action, claiming that the code improperly failed to give notice and an opportunity for a hearing to the public intervenor and public in Wis. Stat. § 30.20 permit proceedings and requesting the circuit court to declare the code invalid. The circuit court found that the public intervenor had standing to challenge the code, but held that the code was a valid exercise of rulemaking authority. On appeal, the court held that the public intervenor had no standing to file a declaratory judgment action to challenge the code. The court determined that the enabling legislation for the public intervenor, Wis. Stat. § 165.07, gave the public intervenor the right only to intervene in proceedings and to appeal from administrative rulings in those proceedings and did not give him authority to initiate an action to challenge a code. The court further ruled that the public trust doctrine, which established standing for the state or any person suing in the name of the state for the purpose of vindicating the public trust, did not confer an affirmative right of action upon the public intervenor because the public intervenor was not the state.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the public intervenor did not have standing to challenge the validity of the administrative code and did not reach the issue of whether the code was constitutional.

 

240 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bohacheff


No. 83-130-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


114 Wis. 2d 402; 338 N.W.2d 466; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 3195


September 7, 1983, Argued  
October 4, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County: Ness Flores, Circuit Judge. On bypass from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed; cause remanded for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which dismissed with prejudice the second count of a two-count criminal complaint against defendant under Wis. Stat. § 940.25(1)(a) (1981) and Wis. Stat. § 940.25(1)(b) (1981).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a single drunk driving accident and was charged by indictment with two counts under Wis. Stat. § 940.25(1)(a) (1981) and Wis. Stat. § 940.25(1)(b) (1981). The trial court dismissed with prejudice the second count under § 940.25(1)(b) upon defendant's motion. Upon review the court reversed the dismissal order, holding that charging both counts did not violate the double jeopardy provisions of the federal or Wisconsin constitutions. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 940.25 (1981) subjected defendant to only one conviction and one punishment. The court held that in enacting Wis. Stat. § 940.25(1)(a) (1981) and Wis. Stat. § 940.25(1)(b) (1981) the legislature only intended to provide two different tests for determining whether a person was guilty of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order which had dismissed with prejudice the second count of a two-count indictment against defendant and remanded for further proceedings.

 

241 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. La Follette v. Stitt


No. 83-1502-OA


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


114 Wis. 2d 358; 338 N.W.2d 684; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 3190


September 9, 1983, Argued  
September 27, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Action for declaratory judgment.



DISPOSITION: Rights Declared.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Wisconsin Attorney General, brought an action seeking a declaratory judgment that the State of Wisconsin Operating Notes of 1983 when issued, sold and delivered in the manner provided by the Authorizing Resolution issued by the State Building Commission pursuant to 1983 Wisconsin Act 3, were valid enforceable contractual obligations of the State of Wisconsin.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, two members of the legislature, asked the court to declare Act 3 invalid because it was not properly enacted and because it authorized a state debt in violation of the state constitution. The two issues raised were: (1) Was 1983 Wisconsin Act 3 invalid because the legislature did not follow specified statutory procedures in enacting the legislation?; and (2) Were the operating notes "public debt" within the meaning of Wis. Const. art. VIII, § 4 which prohibited the state from contracting "public debt" except in certain situations not applicable in the instant case? The court held that the proposed 1983 operating notes did not contravene the constitutional prohibition against creating public debt because such notes, issued in the manner provided by the authorizing resolution adopted by the state building commission pursuant to 1983 Wis. Act 3, were to be repaid within the current fiscal year from current revenues, and thus were not public debts. If the legislature failed to follow self-adopted procedural rules in enacting legislation, and such rules were not mandated by the constitution, the court would not intervene to declare the legislation invalid.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the notes issued pursuant to the authority of 1983 Wisconsin Act 3, were evidence of a valid enforceable obligation of the State of Wisconsin.

Pleasant Prairie v. Department of Local Affairs & Dev.


No. 81-1118


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


113 Wis. 2d 327; 334 N.W.2d 893; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2910


March 29, 1983, Argued  
July 1, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming 108 Wis. 2d 465, 322 N.W.2d 486 (Ct. App.).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner town sought review a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed an order that dismissed the town's petition for incorporation as a village after respondent Department of Local Affairs and Development (Department) determined that the town did not meet the criteria for incorporation as a village as set forth in Wis. Stat. §§ 66.013 to 66.018.


OVERVIEW: The Department determined that, in respect to Wis. Stat. § 66.016(1)(a), although the town's external boundaries were compact, its patterns of land use, urban development, transportation facilities, population distribution, and shopping and social customs were neither compact nor homogeneous. The town did not challenge any of the findings of fact and conceded that the specific findings were supported by substantial evidence. It challenged the Department's interpretation of § 66.016(1), which concluded that in circumstances where an adjacent city had offered to annex the territory, the purpose of the Legislature was to make an independent incorporation substantially impossible. The dismissal of the town's petition was affirmed. The court held that the petition for incorporation was appropriately dismissed under the standards of § 66.016(1)(a). The court found that the standards were appropriately and reasonably interpreted in a manner that comported with the legislative intent to effectuate homogeneity in populated areas.


OUTCOME: The lower appellate court's decision, which affirmed the dismissal of the town's petition for incorporation as a village, was affirmed.

 

243 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williamson


No. 81-1961-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


113 Wis. 2d 389; 335 N.W.2d 814; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2914


March 31, 1983, Argued  
July 1, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming in part and reversing in part 109 Wis. 2d 83, 325 N.W.2d 360 (Ct. App.).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision of the court of appeals is affirmed in part and reversed in part; judgment of conviction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and the State challenged an order from the Court of Appeals of Wisconsin which affirmed the trial court's judgment that the complaint filed by the State was sufficient pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 968.01 (1979-80), but reversed defendant's conviction upon the appellate court's finding that the stop and frisk of defendant failed to meet statutory and constitutional standards.


OVERVIEW: Police officers were parked in a lot of a closed bar. Two men were in the bar's parking lot and, when they saw the police, they acted peculiarly. Defendant was waived over to the police car. An officer asked defendant whether he had ever been convicted of a crime. Defendant admitted to having been convicted of weapons violations in the past. The police officers frisked defendant and found a concealed weapon. Defendant argued that the complaint filed by the state was insufficient as it was based upon unconstitutionally seized evidence. Defendant also argued that the stop and frisk was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court concluded that the complaint was sufficient in that it complied with the requirements of Wis. Stat. § 968.01 and that the validity of the complaint was unaffected by the character of the evidence considered. The court held that the stop and frisk of defendant met the statutory standards in Wis. Stat. §§ 968.24, 968.25 and the constitutional standards because the officer acted as a reasonable man of caution would have in possession of the same facts available to the officer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate and trial court's judgment that the complaint against defendant was sufficient. The court reversed the appellate court's judgment that the stop and frisk of defendant failed to meet constitutional and statutory standards and affirmed defendant's conviction.

In Interest of Baby Girl K.


No. 82-087


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


113 Wis. 2d 429; 335 N.W.2d 846; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2917


April 27, 1983, Argued  
July 1, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming 108 Wis. 2d 785, 324 N.W.2d 833 (Ct. App.).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a circuit court judgment terminating his parental rights to his minor child under the provisions of Wis. Stat. § 48.415(6)(a)2, (b) (1981-82).


OVERVIEW: The father was incarcerated from the fifth month of respondent mother's pregnancy. The child was born out of wedlock and placed in a foster home. Both the circuit and appellate court determined that the father had had an opportunity prior to his incarceration to develop a substantial relationship with the child, and had failed to do so. The court found that the mere fact of the father's incarceration did not preclude the termination of his parental rights because the opportunity to exercise responsibility for the care and protection of a child began before the child's birth. The court held that the father's parental rights were properly terminated under the provisions of Wis. Stat. § 48.415(6)(a)2 (1981-82) because there was evidence to support the circuit court's findings that the father had asked the mother to smuggle marijuana to him in prison, had physically assaulted her, had neglected to provide care or support to her during the pregnancy, and had failed to contact the child. Termination was allowed without a specific finding of parental unfitness because the father had failed to establish a parental relationship with the child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that terminated the father's parental rights.

Noranda Exploration, Inc. v. Ostrom


No. 81-236


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


113 Wis. 2d 612; 335 N.W.2d 596; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2924; 77 Oil & Gas Rep. 380


February 28, 1983, Argued  
July 1, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on September 19, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing 107 Wis. 2d 205, 320 N.W.2d 530 (Ct. App.).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a mineral exploration company, challenged a decision from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed a judgment of the trial court declaring Wis. Stat. 107.15, which required public disclosure of the results of mineral exploration, unconstitutional as a taking without just compensation. The court of appeals found that the statute was a valid exercise of the State's police power.


OVERVIEW: The mineral exploration company brought a complaint challenging the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 107.15 on the ground that the provisions requiring the disclosure of the results of its mineral explorations constituted a taking of the company's property without just compensation in violation of U.S. Const. amend V and Wis. Const. art. I, § 13. The company alleged that it had a vested title to the information and that the information was of extreme value to the company. The trial court declared § 107.15 to be unconstitutional and ordered the State to be permanently enjoined from enforcing the statute. The court of appeals reversed, concluding that the statute was a valid exercise of the State's police power and that it did not take property without due process of law. The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals, concluding that the requirement of public disclosure under § 107.15 constituted an unconstitutional taking without just compensation. The court concluded that the statute was not a valid exercise of the State's police power because the statute did not have a reasonable and rational relationship to the furtherance of a proper legislative purpose.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals that the statutory provisions for disclosure to the public of confidential mining exploration data and core samples was a valid exercise of the State's police power and that the disclosure provisions did not constitute a "taking" without just compensation.

Brockmeyer v. Dun & Bradstreet


No. 81-2024


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


113 Wis. 2d 561; 335 N.W.2d 834; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2928; 115 L.R.R.M. 4484; 98 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P55,398


June 1, 1983, Argued  
July 1, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming 109 Wis. 2d 44, 325 N.W.2d 70 (Ct. App.).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee challenged the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the employee in his action against defendant employer for wrongful discharge.


OVERVIEW: An employee held a management position as a district manager of credit services for an investment firm, and he had no contract of employment. After the employer settled a sex discrimination suit filed by the employee's former secretary, with whom he allegedly had an affair, the employer fired the employee. The court held that it was appropriate to create a public policy exception to the employment-at-will doctrine for cases where a termination clearly violated a well-defined public policy as evidenced by existing law. While the employer's actions may have constituted bad faith, its actions did not contravene the policies of any statute or constitutional provision. As the employee failed to prove that his discharge violated fundamental public policy, the decision for the employer was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court in favor of the employer.

In re Disciplinary Proceedings against Glasschroeder


No. 81-2055


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


113 Wis. 2d 672; 335 N.W.2d 621; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2921


June 2, 1983, Submitted on Briefs  
July 1, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, with $ 50 Costs, on August 9, 1983.



DISPOSITION: Attorney disciplinary proceeding; attorney's license revoked.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of a referee's recommendation that the attorney's license to practice law be revoked for having appropriated for his own use monies belonging to a client and for having uttered as genuine a forged check.


OVERVIEW: The attorney did not deny that he had misappropriated the money or that he had forged the check. His assertion was that disbarment was too harsh a penalty. He claimed that at the time he committed the acts he was charged with, he was suffering from the effects of alcoholism and drug use, and that his conduct was also caused in part by coercion and threats against his family by third persons. Testimony at the attorney's disciplinary hearing indicated that he had been involved in rehabilitation and that he had made significant progress in overcoming his alcoholism and drug dependency. The court disbarred the attorney. The referee's recommendation was based on the attorney's actions in misappropriating a large sum of money and his commission of a crime. None of the evidence presented during the disciplinary hearing indicated that the attorney's drug or alcohol dependence had impaired the attorney's judgment leading his misconduct. Furthermore, there was nothing in the record to substantiate the attorney's claim of coercion.


OUTCOME: The court acted on the referee's recommendation and revoked the attorney's license to practice law.

 

248 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Zinn v. State


No. 81-1772


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


112 Wis. 2d 417; 334 N.W.2d 67; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2906


April 27, 1983, Argued  
June 1, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Consideration Denied, without Costs, on August 9, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing and remanding 108 Wis. 2d 783, 324 N.W.2d 831 (Ct. App.).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed and cause remanded to the trial court for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the trial court's decision to deny defendant State's motion to dismiss the landowner's action for damages under Wis. Const. art. I, § 13 for the temporary taking of property by the State.


OVERVIEW: The landowner owned property surrounding a lake. However, upon the petition of a neighbor, the State initially declared the lake to be navigable waters and, thus, owned by the State pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 30.10(1). The State retracted this decision, but the landowner filed an action for damages arising from a temporary taking. The State sought dismissal of the case based upon failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted and sovereign immunity. The trial court refused to dismiss the case, but the lower court disagreed. The court reversed the lower court's decision in favor of dismissal because (1) the pleadings stated a claim upon which the relief of damages could be granted, (2) sovereign immunity did not apply to a taking, and (3) as there was no statute under which the landowner could proceed, she could rely directly upon Wis. Const. art. I, § 13 as the basis for her claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's decision in favor of the State against the landowner, and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

249 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Bilder v. Delavan


No. 81-2182


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


112 Wis. 2d 539; 334 N.W.2d 252; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2899; 9 Media L. Rep. 2294


March 28, 1983, Argued  
June 1, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Walworth County, Robert H. Gollmar, Reserve Circuit Judge. On certification from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police chief sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which granted intervenor newspapers' motion to intervene and rescinded its earlier order that sealed documents from public examination in the police chief's action against appellees, city and city employees, that alleged he was wrongfully suspended.


OVERVIEW: The police chief appealed the newspapers' intervention, alleging that the newspapers did not have an interest relating to the property or transaction which was the subject of the action. Specifically, he contended that the subject of the action was whether the city's investigation and disciplinary proceedings against him were lawful and that the newspapers' claimed right of access to the court file was only a collateral issue that was too remote from the subject of the action to create a right of intervention. The court disagreed and held that the newspapers' interest in opening the court file was a legally protected interest under Wis. Stat. § 59.14. Although the issue of the sealing or opening of the file was not the main objective of the police chief's action, he made the issue important when he moved to seal the court file on the day he filed his action and when he made the permanent sealing of the file a condition of the stipulation dismissing the lawsuit. On the merits, the court found that the sealing of the court file would have been improper because the contents of the file were records that the legislature intended to come under the provisions of § 59.14(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which granted the newspapers' motion to intervene and rescinded an order to seal documents.

 

250 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burns


No. 82-210-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


112 Wis. 2d 131; 332 N.W.2d 757; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2869


February 4, 1983, Argued  
April 26, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County. On certification from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a trial in the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), defendant was convicted of first-degree sexual assault, endangering safety by conduct regardless of life, kidnapping, robbery, and verbally threatening to injure another. Defendant appealed on the ground that the trial court violated his constitutional right to confrontation by permitting a transcript of the victim's preliminary hearing testimony to be read at trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant abducted, severely beat, and sexually assaulted the victim. The victim testified at a preliminary hearing and was extensively cross-examined by defense counsel. As the trial date approached, and after learning that the victim was hospitalized because of the incident, the prosecutor filed a motion to declare the victim unavailable for trial. At the motion hearing, a specialist in forensic psychiatry testified that the victim became a catatonic schizophrenic, and that if she was forced to testify at trial her symptoms would worsen. The trial judge declared her unavailable and permitted her former testimony to be read into evidence. In affirming the convictions, the court held that (1) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in ruling that the victim was unavailable to testify at trial, and (2) there was no Confrontation Clause violation. The court stated that it was a legitimate interest of the criminal trial process to protect a victim of crime from needlessly repeating testimony where the victim was diagnosed as being severely mentally ill and where the act of testifying again had a significant probability of worsening the condition.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for first-degree sexual assault, endangering safety by conduct regardless of life, kidnapping, robbery, and verbally threatening to injure another were affirmed.

State v. White


No. 81-1895-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


112 Wis. 2d 178; 332 N.W.2d 756; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2871

DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision of the court of appeals reversed; judgment of the circuit court reversed; cause remanded to the circuit court to dismiss the complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review from a decision by the court of appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a judgment convicting defendants pursuant Wisconsin's compulsory school attendance law, Wis. Stat. § 118.15(1)(a) (1981-2).


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a plea agreement that preserved their rights to appeal, defendants were convicted of violating Wisconsin's compulsory school attendance law, Wis. Stat. § 118.15(1)(a) (1981-2), by failing to make their minor child attend school regularly. The appellate court affirmed the conviction. On appeal, defendants argued that § 118.15(1)(a) was unconstitutionally vague. The court reversed the conviction, noting that new precedent established that § 118.15(1)(a) was unconstitutionally vague as applied to private schools. Therefore, even if defendants did not properly preserve the constitutionality of § 118.15(1)(a) for appeal, the court would hold afford defendants' the opportunity to withdraw their pleas because they were based upon an erroneous understanding of their legal rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's affirmance of the trial court's judgment convicting defendants for not making their child go to school.

State v. Popanz


No. 81-1493-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


112 Wis. 2d 166; 332 N.W.2d 750; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2872


March 2, 1983, Submitted on Briefs  
April 26, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Iowa County, James P. Fiedler, Circuit Judge. On certification from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment of the circuit court reversed; cause remanded with directions to dismiss the complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Iowa County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of two counts of violating Wisconsin's compulsory school attendance law, Wis. Stat. § 118.15(1)(a) (1981-82). The court of appeals certified the case to the court.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented on certification was whether the phrase "private school" as used in § 118.15(1)(a) was impermissibly vague and, as applied to prosecutions involving "private schools," violated the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution and Wis. Const. art. I, § 8. The charges concerned two of defendant's daughters who attended the Free Thinker School. Defendant requested the children's school records along with recommendations regarding curriculum and asked the district school administrator to inform the school attendance officer about the matter so that he could be informed of anything they needed to do to be in compliance with the law. The local administrator required a listing of the school in a State directory, and requested prosecution without visiting the school. The circuit court found defendant guilty, and he appealed. The court reversed the judgment of conviction because it found that there was no statutory definition of "private schools" and that the statute as it applied to private schools was invalidated on the grounds of vagueness. There were no statutory standards of culpability, which posed the danger of arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction and remanded the cause to the circuit court with directions to dismiss the complaint.

 

253 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Cannon v. Moran


No. 81-420


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


111 Wis. 2d 544; 331 N.W.2d 369; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2639


February 4, 1983, Argued  
March 29, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing 107 Wis. 2d 669, 321 N.W.2d 550 (Ct. App.).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, current or former circuit court judges, appealed a decision from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), in favor of defendant state of Wisconsin, which held that Wis. Stat. Ann. § 40.91, operating to reduce plaintiffs' salaries by the amount of pension benefits they received from prior judicial service in Milwaukee County, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: After the conversion of county courts to state circuit courts and the creation of the court of appeals, retirement benefits were provided exclusively by the state except for certain circuit court judges, including plaintiffs, who elected to receive a portion from the state and a balance from the county. Then, § 40.91 was passed, which reduced plaintiffs' state retirement benefits by an amount received from the county. Plaintiffs argued that § 40.91 unconstitutionally impaired their retirement benefit contracts and deprived them of property without due process of law. The court agreed. The lower court erred in holding that the law did not impair the contracts because the amounts paid were reduced, not eliminated. Such a distinction was illusory. Using a higher degree of scrutiny for a severe impairment, the court concluded that § 40.91 did not, as retroactively applied to plaintiffs, reasonably or appropriately safeguard a vital interest of the people. Furthermore, the salary set off was inherently inequitable and the class of employees affected was extremely narrow.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, holding that the challenged law was unconstitutional.

 

254 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Holland Plastics Co.


No. 82-024


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


111 Wis. 2d 497; 331 N.W.2d 320; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2642


February 28, 1983, Argued  
March 29, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on May 3, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County. On certification from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, builders and building material suppliers, appealed from the trial court's denial of their summary judgment motion, in a suit by plaintiff, the State of Wisconsin (State), alleging breach of contract and negligent construction of a university building. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals certified the case to the court pursuant to Wis. R. Civ. P., Wis. Stat. § 809.61. The certification request was granted and the appeal was accepted.


OVERVIEW: The State filed suit, alleging that the roof of a university building was defectively constructed. The suit alleged that the building suppliers were negligent in supplying certain materials and that one builder was negligent in using the wrong type of asphalt for the roof. The action also claimed that two builders negligently constructed the roof and that both breached their contracts with the state involving the building's construction. Defendants filed a summary judgment motion, alleging that the suit was barred by the statute of limitations. On appeal from the denial of the motion, the court reversed and remanded, concluding that the action was governed by the six year limitations in Wis. Stat. §§ 893.19(5) and 893.19(3). Wis. Stat. § 893.18(6), the 10-year statute of limitations for actions by the State, was inapplicable because this section only governed actions that were not covered any other statute of limitations. Further, § 893.19(3), barred the breach of contract claims. On remand, the trial court was to determine whether the negligent construction claim was barred by § 893.19(5).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision to deny defendant's motion for summary judgment and remanded for further proceedings.

 

255 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re B.


No. 81-2020


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


111 Wis. 2d 175; 330 N.W.2d 584; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2626


February 4, 1978, Argued  
March 1, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on April 5, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing 109 Wis. 2d 1, 325 N.W.2d 64 (Ct App).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment by the appellate court (Wisconsin), which reversed the judgment of the trial court. The trial court found defendant, a juvenile, guilty of two counts of burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of two counts of burglary. The appellate court vacated the trial court's decision, stating that it was error under Wis. Stat. § 805.13(4) and Wis. Stat. § 972.10(5) for the trial court to refuse to provide the jury with a written copy of a burden of proof and presumption of innocence instruction. On appeal the court reversed the appellate court's decision. The court held that if the legislature intended to mandate automatic reversal for a violation of Wis. Stat. § 805.13(4) or Wis. Stat. § 972.10(5) then such action amounted to an unconstitutional exercise of legislative authority under the doctrine of separation of powers. Because neither section expressly mandated reversal upon noncompliance the court found that the statutes required the submission of instructions on substantive law to the jury in written form while at the same time leaving the determination of whether an error was reversible to the courts. The court concluded that the concepts of burden of proof and presumption of innocence fell within the realm of procedure. Therefore the trial court did not commit reversible error by not submitting a written copy of the instructions to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court.

Tri-State Home Improv. Co. v. Labor & Industry Review Com.


No. 81-1731


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


111 Wis. 2d 103; 330 N.W.2d 186; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2630


November 30, 1982, Argued  
March 1, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming 107 Wis. 2d 748, 322 N.W.2d 700 (Ct App).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff aluminum siding company sought review the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the circuit court order and held in favor of defendant Labor & Industry Review Commission, and affirmed the Commission's original determination that the company's salesmen were employees under the Unemployment Compensation Act.


OVERVIEW: The Commission concluded that the salesmen for the company were not free from the company's control or direction over the performance of their services; therefore they were employees for unemployment compensation purposes. The court examined whether the company was liable for payments to the Unemployment Compensation Fund pursuant to the criteria set forth in Wis. Stat. § 108.02(3)(a) and (b). The company claimed that the exemptions under § 108.02(3)(b)1 and 2 were applicable because the salesmen were not under its control, either by contract or in fact, and because the salesmen had independently established businesses. The court affirmed the appellate court judgment, and held that the employees were not free from the company's control or direction over the performance of their services. The court stated that whatever independence the salesmen had was hedged with controls which could be invoked at the will of the company. The court held that there was sufficient evidence of control in the record to support the legal conclusion of the commission that the exemption under § 108.02(3)(b)1 was not applicable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals, which had affirmed the order of the Commission concluding that the company's salesmen were employees under the Unemployment Compensation Act and were not exempt. The circuit court order was overruled.

In re All-Star Ins. Corp.


Nos. 81-1349, 81-1350


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


110 Wis. 2d 72; 327 N.W.2d 648; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2594


December 1, 1982, Argued  
January 5, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from judgments of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: William A. Jennaro, Circuit Judge. On certification from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Case No. 81-1349 is remanded to the court of appeals for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion. Judgment affirmed in Case No. 81-1350.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurance agencies appealed judgments from the circuit court, which granted plaintiff special deputy commissioner's motion for summary judgment in an action to recover sums allegedly due to an insurance corporation that was brought by the commissioner in his capacity of overseeing the corporation's liquidation. The Court of Appeals certified the appeal to the court.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner was appointed to oversee the liquidation of the insurance corporation and filed suit to recover sums due under separate contracts with two independent agencies, asserting jurisdiction over the foreign companies pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 645.04(5)(a). The cases were consolidated and the trial court granted the commissioner's motion for summary judgment. Both agencies asserted that the trial court lacked personal jurisdiction and that jurisdiction pursuant to the statute was unconstitutional, and one agency also appealed the determination on the merits. The court affirmed one judgment and remanded the other for further proceedings on the challenge to the determination on the merits, holding that assertion of jurisdiction pursuant to § 645.04(5)(a) did not violate due process because the agencies were linked to the forum state by virtue of their contract with the insurance corporation, the cause of action was incident to their contracts, and the burden upon the agencies to defend within the forum state was not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's holding that it had personal jurisdiction over the agencies, remanded the judgment that was challenged on jurisdictional grounds and on the merits to the court of appeals for further proceedings, and affirmed the judgment that was challenged only on jurisdictional grounds.

259 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sharlow


No. 81-207-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


110 Wis. 2d 226; 327 N.W.2d 692; 1983 Wisc. LEXIS 2598


November 2, 1982, Argued  
January 5, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming 106 Wis. 2d 440, 317 N.W.2d 150 (Ct App).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the circuit court's order granting him a new trial, following his conviction for first-degree murder, party to a crime, under Wis. Stat. § 939.05 and § 940.01 (1971).


OVERVIEW: In his motion for post-conviction relief pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.06, defendant contended that he had been denied the constitutional right to call witnesses in his own defense. The trial court granted a new trial, and the Court of Appeals reversed. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that hearsay testimony which incriminated a codefendant was properly excluded. The fact that the codefendant may have told the proffered witness that he shot the victim would not have exculpated defendant as he was charged with being a party to the crime of murder. Under those circumstances, the statements were not so critical to his defense that their exclusion denied him a fair trial. The codefendant's statement that he shot the victim did not bear persuasive assurances of trustworthiness. Defendant's contention that under § 939.05 only a conspirator or a solicitor could be held liable for a crime other than the intended crime was rejected, as the statute required that the actor "knowingly" render aid in the commission of the crime.


OUTCOME: The judgment reversing the granting of defendant's motion for a new trial was affirmed.

S.D.R. v. State (In re S.D.R.)


No. 81-914


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


109 Wis. 2d 567; 326 N.W.2d 762; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2932


November 3, 1982, Argued  
December 2, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming 106 Wis. 2d 772, 318 N.W.2d 26 (Ct. App.).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed an order extending a juvenile dispositional order against him for 30 days pending a full hearing on the extension, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.365(6). The action was brought by respondent State seeking to continue custody of the minor.


OVERVIEW: The minor was in custody of the State, and six days prior to the expiration of the dispositional order against him, the State petitioned for an extension based on a social worker's report that the minor needed to continue in a structured and supervised atmosphere. The minor contested the extension and requested that a hearing on the merits be held prior to the expiration of the order to prevent a violation of his right to liberty. The trial court extended the order for 30 days pending a full hearing. At the hearing, the minor filed a motion to dismiss, but it was denied, and custody was extended. The decision was affirmed on appeal. The minor sought review, arguing that he was deprived of liberty without due process. The court affirmed, holding that there was no violation of due process because no liberty interest was violated until 30 days after termination of a dispositional order. The minor was adjudicated delinquent in a proceeding where he was accorded full due process protection, and he had no legitimate expectation of release at the expiration of the order because juveniles were not automatically released; they were subject to a system of annual review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision extending the minor's custody by the State.

State v. Welsh


No. 80-1686


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


108 Wis. 2d 319; 321 N.W.2d 245; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2729


March 1, 1982, Argued  
July 2, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing 102 Wis. 2d 727, 308 N.W.2d 772.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which vacated an order of the trial court that revoked defendant driver's motor vehicle operator's license for 60 days because he unreasonably refused to submit to a breathalyzer test, as required by Wis. Stat. § 343.305(2)(a) (1977), after being issued a citation for the operation of a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant under Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1) (1977).


OVERVIEW: A witness saw the driver driving erratically before he ran off the road into a field. The driver left the scene before the police arrived, but the witness stated that he was staggering and his speech was slurred, which provided probable cause to believe that the driver was intoxicated. When the police ran a check on his car, an officer remembered arresting the owner in an earlier alcohol-related disturbance, which provided additional probable cause. The officers went to the driver's home, where his relatives gave consent to enter. The driver challenged his warrantless arrest in his residence as violating the Fourth Amendment and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11. The trial court upheld the arrest, concluding that probable cause to believe that the driver had been operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, coupled with the existence of exigent circumstances, justified the officers' entry into the driver's residence. A single judge of the court of appeals reversed, but the court reversed again, holding that there was ample evidence supporting the trial court's ruling that the co-existence of probable cause and exigent circumstances justified the warrantless arrest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment that vacated the trial court's order, and the court affirmed the trial court's findings.

State v. Chosa


No. 80-1903-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


108 Wis. 2d 392; 321 N.W.2d 280; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2730


June 2, 1982, Argued  
July 2, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing 104 Wis. 2d 743, 314 N.W.2d 362.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed and the case is remanded to the trial court for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Vilas County (Wisconsin) that convicted defendant of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a Native American, was convicted of committing a murder on an Indian reservation. In affirming defendant's conviction, the court of appeals found in part that the trial court did not violate defendant's rights to equal protection of the law by excusing for cause all Native Americans from the jury panel without objection by defense counsel. The trial court judge excused all of the Native Americans from jury service after questioning only three of them. The state claimed that defendant waived any challenge because he failed to object. On appeal, the court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for a new trial. The court found that excluding all of the Native Americans from service as potential jurors without any established reason stigmatized the entire class and was an abuse of discretion because (1) no voir dire was conducted of six of the nine Native Americans, and (2) even the responses elicited from the three who were questioned provided an insufficient basis for exclusion for cause. The court concluded that defendant's substantial rights were affected and that the appropriate remedy, under Wis. Stat. § 805.18(2), was reversal and a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals, which affirmed defendant's conviction of first-degree murder, and remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial.

Oddsen v. Board of Fire & Police Comm'rs


Nos. 80-1726, 81-684


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


108 Wis. 2d 143; 321 N.W.2d 161; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2753


June 2, 1982, Argued  
July 2, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of decisions of the Court of Appeals. Reversing and remanding 103 Wis. 2d 689, 309 N.W.2d 889 [Case No. 80-1726], and 105 Wis. 2d 764, 318 N.W.2d 23 [Case No. 81-684].



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decisions reversed and the causes are remanded to the respective circuit courts, with directions that the officers be reinstated without prejudice as provided by the statutes and for the computation of wages due.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner police officers appealed the judgments by the Wisconsin Court of Appeals, which affirmed the judgment of one Circuit Court for Milwaukee County which had affirmed the judgment of Respondent Board of Fire and Police Commissioners for the City of Milwaukee discharging one officer, and reversed the judgment of another trial court, which had reversed the Board's decision to discharge the other officer.


OVERVIEW: The female officer's estranged husband found the officers in bed together and called the police, and said that an officer was down. Police and ambulance personnel showed up, attracting media attention. The officers were taken to the station. Although the female officer was vomiting blood, she was told that if she left to go to the doctor she would be discharged and that she could not leave the station until she gave a truthful statement. The officer finally admitted to a sexual relationship. After 14 hours, she was taken home. The male officer's request for an attorney was denied and he was also told that if he left, he would be subject to further discipline. After 13 hours of interrogation and no food, the male officer admitted to the relationship. Both officers were discharged, and the Board affirmed the discharges. The trial court affirmed the Board's judgment as to the male officer, but reversed as to the female. The appellate court affirmed as to the male officer, but reversed as to the female officer. The officers appealed. The court reversed. The court held that the confessions were involuntary because they were the result of coercion and the denial of due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgments, which had affirmed the judgment of one trial court affirming the board's dismissal of one of the officers, and which had reversed the judgment of another trial court, which had reversed the board's dismissal of the other officer.

 

264 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Bence v. Milwaukee


Nos. 80-1815, 81-1574


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


107 Wis. 2d 469; 320 N.W.2d 199; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2562


March 30, 1982, Argued; April 1, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
June 2, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Case No. 80-1815: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.

Case No. 81-1574: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: John E. McCormick, Circuit Judge. Reversing and remanding 103 Wis. 2d 679, 309 N.W.2d 883. On by-pass from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court -- Case No. 80-1815. The decision of the court of appeals is reversed and the cause remanded to the trial court with directions to issue a declaratory judgment that Charter Ordinance 410 does not violate plaintiffs' constitutional rights. Case No. 81-1574. The decision and order of the trial court is reversed and the cause remanded with directions to issue a declaratory judgment that Charter Ordinance 378 does not violate plaintiffs' constitutional rights.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city, in consolidated appeals, challenged the judgments of the appellate court and the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which declared Milwaukee, Wis., Charter Ordinances 378 and 410 unconstitutional in violation of the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The suits were brought by plaintiff retired city employees.


OVERVIEW: The retired city employees challenged the ordinances, which incorporated terms of collective bargaining agreements regarding two pension plans. The ordinances provided for greater benefits for employees who retired after a certain date. The lower courts held certain provisions unconstitutional. The court reversed and held that there was a rational basis for the ordinances. The court held that the pensions were properly arrived at according to the procedure mandated by Wis. Stat. § 111.70, and the provisions were then enacted as charter ordinances, as required by law, and went into effect according to Wis. Stat. § 66.01. The purpose of the ordinances was to effectuate the collective bargaining agreements and to provide pension benefits. Harmonious labor relations and provision of pension benefits were valid public purposes; therefore, the ordinances served valid public purposes. The classification was rationally related to the purposes of the ordinances. The classifications, while determined by employment status on a date pertaining to the collective bargaining period, did not discriminate unwarrantably in favor of persons existing or engaged in an occupation as of a certain date.


OUTCOME: The decisions of the lower courts were reversed and the causes were remanded with directions to issue declaratory judgments that stated that the ordinances did not violate the retired city employee's constitutional rights.

 

265 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Funmaker v. Klamm


No. 81-650-W


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


106 Wis. 2d 624; 317 N.W.2d 458; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2529


March 1, 1982, Argued  
March 30, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming 102 Wis. 2d 724, 308 N.W.2d 421.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Petitioner contended that there was insufficient evidence at the preliminary hearing to establish probable cause for a bindover, that the examining judge erred by viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the State, and that petitioner was denied a constitutional right to make a closing argument.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that there was insufficient evidence at the preliminary hearing to bind him over for trial. The victim was initially uncertain in his identification of petitioner as his assailant because petitioner and his brother were similar in appearance. A second witness identified a different man as the attacker. The court determined that there was sufficient evidence to establish probable cause that petitioner was the victim's attacker. The victim's identification of petitioner was competent evidence for the examining judge to act on in finding probable cause. Weaknesses in the identification that affected the weight and credibility of the victim's testimony were issues for trial, not the preliminary hearing. All that was required was a plausible account of petitioner's commission of a felony to support bindover for trial. The court also determined that the decision of whether to allow closing argument at the preliminary hearing rested within the sound discretion of the examining judge. Petitioner was not denied a constitutional right when his counsel was not allowed to give a closing argument. The court affirmed the court of appeals' denial of a writ of habeas corpus.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals denying petitioner a writ of habeas corpus.

 

266 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Denny v. Mertz


No. 80-436


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


106 Wis. 2d 636; 318 N.W.2d 141; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2532; 8 Media L. Rep. 1369


November 3, 1981, Argued  
March 30, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming 100 Wis. 2d 332, 302 N.W.2d 503.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed and the case is remanded to the circuit court for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant publisher, and former chairman of a corporation (the alleged source of a defamation), sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), that reversed a grant of summary judgment in their favor from the trial court, in plaintiff dissident shareholder's action for libel. In reversing the trial court, the lower court held that the shareholder was not a public figure, and remanded for a trial on the merits.


OVERVIEW: The corporation had employed the shareholder as an attorney until he resigned to go into private practice. After he left, the value of the corporation's stock dropped. He sought to oust the chairman of the board, who later resigned. When a publisher sought information on the controversy, the chairman allegedly stated that the shareholder had been "fired" from his position. The shareholder brought an action for libel. At issue was whether the shareholder was a "public figure" for the purpose of maintaining an action for libel. The court concluded that he was not, because the shareholder disputes did not have an impact outside of those immediately interested in the corporation. Also in issue were the constitutional protections of the publisher of the libel. The court concluded that the shareholder must prove that the publisher was negligent in publishing the libel in order to recover actual damages. "Presumed" or punitive damages might only be awarded upon proof that the publisher acted with "actual malice." The court further concluded that the alleged source of the defamation published did not enjoy the same constitutional protections as the media publisher.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court and overturned the summary judgment granted to the publisher and to the source of the defamation. The court remanded for a trial on the merits.

 

267 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Milwaukee Alliance Against Racist & Political Repression v. Elections Bd. of Wisconsin


No. 81-2193


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


106 Wis. 2d 593; 317 N.W.2d 420; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2524


March 4, 1982, Argued  
March 26, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County. P. Charles Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a political group, challenged the validity of an amendment to the state constitution revising the right to bail. Wis. Const. art. I, § 8. The Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) granted defendant state elections board's motion for summary judgment and directed certification of the election results, and the political group appealed.


OVERVIEW: The amendment to the constitution revised the right to bail and authorized the circuit courts to deny release on bail for a limited period to certain accused persons. The political group argued that the amendment was submitted to the voters in violation of Wis. Const. art. XII, § 1, which required that if more than one amendment was submitted to the voters, the amendments must be capable of being voted for or against separately. The political group argued that the issues of conditional release and anti-monetary bail should have been submitted to the voters as separate questions. Affirming the circuit court, the court rejected this argument as unrealistic. The purpose of the amendment was to provide a comprehensive plan for conditional release. A single amendment could cover several propositions, all tending to effect and carry out one general object or purpose, and all connected with one subject. The question as submitted met all constitutional and statutory requirements as to content and form necessary to adequately inform the public on the purpose of the amendment upon which it was voting.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court.

 

268 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Callaway


No. 80-1333-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


106 Wis. 2d 503; 317 N.W.2d 428; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2527


February 3, 1982, Argued  
March 26, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing and remanding 103 Wis. 2d 389, 308 N.W.2d 897.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed and remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of a court of appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed an order of the circuit court that granted defendant's motion to suppress the physical evidence seized in a warrantless inventory search of an automobile.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court found that both the impoundment of the vehicle and the subsequent inventory search of the car, including the glove compartment, were unreasonable and violated defendant's Fourth Amendment rights. The appellate court affirmed, agreeing with the circuit court that the impounding of the vehicle was unreasonable and further holding that the State had waived any right to raise the issue of defendant's standing. The court noted that the relevant standard to have been applied to the search and seizure was whether the search was reasonable. The court held that it was reasonable for the police to have impounded the vehicle. Defendant had been informed that the car would have been impounded if he could not suggest another driver the police could contact and he consented to the impoundment of the vehicle and voluntarily surrendered his keys to the police officer. The impoundment was not a mere pretext for searching the car. The court also decided that the inventory search was both reasonable and necessary to protect both the owner's property and the police from claims of lost property. Finally, the court concluded the State did not waive the issue of defendant's standing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and remanded for further proceedings.

Taylor v. Conta


No. 80-2221


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


106 Wis. 2d 321; 316 N.W.2d 814; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2512


January 5, 1982, Argued  
March 2, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: William D. Byrne, Circuit Judge, on certification of the Court of Appeals. On certification from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment for appellee secretaries of Wisconsin Department of Revenue, in the taxpayers' action for declaratory relief challenging the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. §§ 71.05(1)(a)5 and 71.05(1)(a)7.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers contended that taxation of their gains and denial of their deductions of moving expenses constituted impermissible discrimination against non-residents. The court rejected the taxpayers' contention that under the precedence of a prior case, the court was required to declare a state tax statute void under the privileges and immunities clause if the challenger showed that there was no substantial equality of treatment for the citizens of the taxing state and nonresident taxpayers, holding that the taxpayers misconstrued the prior case. The court held that because the tax statutes could disadvantage non-citizens and did involve a fundamental right, the court was required to determine whether the state's discriminatory treatment of non-citizens was within or outside the bounds set by the constitution. The court affirmed the constitutionality, holding that the statute bore a substantial relation to a legitimate state objective. The court held that the differential treatment of new residences inside or outside the state had a substantial relation to the legitimate state objective of raising revenue and to the state's power to tax and to achieve equality among taxpayers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, in favor of the secretaries, in the taxpayers' action for declaratory relief challenging the constitutionality of two state tax statutes.
