Wisconsin Professional Police Asso. (WPPA) v. County of Dane


No. 81-023


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


106 Wis. 2d 303; 316 N.W.2d 656; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2513; 114 L.R.R.M. 2153


November 3, 1981, Argued  
March 2, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: P. Charles Jones, Circuit Judge. On by-pass from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order of the circuit court is reversed and the cause is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sheriff challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), that found that the sheriff was bound by an arbitrator's award directing that the court officer work be returned to a member of the nonsupervisory bargaining unit.


OVERVIEW: The sheriff appointed a deputy sheriff who was a member of the supervisory, rather than the nonsupervisory bargaining unit as a court officer. The duties had previously been performed by a member of the nonsupervisory bargaining unit. Respondent union filed a grievance, and arbitration proceedings were conducted between the union and respondent county. The lower court affirmed, and the sheriff appealed. The issue on appeal was whether the duties performed by the court officer were among the principal and important duties which characterized the office of sheriff so that the sheriff may not be restricted as to whom he appointed to perform the function. The court reversed, concluding that attending on the courts was one of the duties preserved for the sheriff by the state constitution. The court was, however, unable to determine whether the position at issue fell within the abovementioned powers of the sheriff.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter for determination of the duties of a court officer and whether those duties were among those preserved to the sheriff by the state constitution.

 

271 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Holmes


Nos. 81-1669-CR, 81-1774-W


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


106 Wis. 2d 31; 315 N.W.2d 703; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2504


December 3, 1981, Argued  
February 2, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Polk County: Robert O. Weisel, Circuit Judge.

Petition for a supervisory writ to the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Ralph Adam Fine, Circuit Judge. Case No. 81-1669-CR on certification from Court of Appeals. Case No. 81-1774-W on by-pass from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order of the circuit court for Polk county is reversed; a writ of prohibition is issued directing the circuit court for Milwaukee county, Ralph Adam Fine, circuit judge, to refrain from taking any further action in the above-captioned matter; and the causes are remanded to the respective circuit courts for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals from judgments of respondents, the Circuit Courts of Polk and Milwaukee Counties (Wisconsin), each criminal defendant sought review of a denial of substitution of judge pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 971.20. Each circuit court held that § 971.20 was an unconstitutional legislative interference with the judicial branch in violation of the Wisconsin Constitution. The state intervened, asserting that § 971.20 was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the circuit courts had the power to raise and decide the constitutionality of § 971.20 and exercised that power in a fair and proper manner. As to the merits, the court noted that § 971.20 permitted a defendant to request a substitution of judge without giving any reason or requiring proof of any grounds. Nevertheless, there was no showing beyond a reasonable doubt that § 971.20 materially impaired or practically defeated the circuit court's exercise of jurisdiction and power or the proper functioning of the judicial system so as to constitute a violation of the doctrine of separation of powers. The legislature's elimination of the requirement of an affidavit of prejudice was merely a change in the method of assuring a fair trial. Statistics did not provide quantitative evidence that substitution requests materially impaired or practically defeated the ability of the judicial system to dispose of cases. That § 971.20 could be abused was not controlling. Although the wisdom of § 971.20 was being seriously challenged in the legislature, the court could not conclude that the statute violated the constitutional doctrine of separation of powers.


OUTCOME: The order of the Circuit Court for Polk County denying the request for substitution of judge was reversed, and a writ of prohibition was issued directing the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County to refrain from taking any further action in the case. Both causes were remanded to the respective circuit courts for further proceedings.

 

272 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Marshfield Clinic v. Discher


No. 81-214


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


105 Wis. 2d 506; 314 N.W.2d 326; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2496


November 30, 1981, Argued  
January 18, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Portage County: James H. Levi, Judge. On certification from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Reversed and remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff clinic sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin) that dismissed the clinic's complaint on the ground that no cause of action existed to hold a wife liable for the necessary medical expenses of her husband. The clinic had filed an action against defendant wife seeking reimbursement for the husband's medical expenses.


OVERVIEW: The clinic had provided medical services to the husband prior to his death. The clinic alleged that it had not been paid for these services, but it did not allege that any attempts had been made to collect from the estate of the husband. The trial court dismissed the action. At issue on appeal was whether a wife was liable for medical expenses incurred by her deceased husband on his own behalf in the absence of her agreement to accept responsibility for the expenses. In reversing, the court held that a wife shares with her husband a limited legal duty of support of the family. Thus, if the clinic had proven that it had attempted to collect from the husband's estate, but had been unable to do so, the wife would have been liable. However, because no such showing was made or even attempted, the court remanded to give the clinic an opportunity to prove that it either attempted to collect from the husband's estate but was unable to do so, or that any collection attempts would have been futile. The court held that the Stromsted rule only applied in the absence of an express agreement by the parties.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment from the trial court.

State ex rel. Grand Bazaar Liquors, Inc. v. Milwaukee


No. 79-1712


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


105 Wis. 2d 203; 313 N.W.2d 805; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2484


December 1, 1981, Argued  
January 5, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing 102 Wis. 2d 208, 306 N.W.2d 255.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed the judgment by the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment by the Milwaukee County Circuit Court, which had, in plaintiff grocery store's declaratory judgment action, entered a judgment that the city's liquor licensing ordinance was constitutional. The store filed a cross-appeal.


OVERVIEW: The store filed an application with the city for a liquor license. While the application was pending, the city passed a new ordinance which required a licensee to receive at least 50 percent of its income from liquor sales, and that stores which had their license at the time the ordinance was passed were not required to comply with it. Milwaukee, Wis., Code § 90-25.1(2), (3). The store filed a second application, which was denied. The store filed an action for a declaratory judgment that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The trial court found the ordinance constitutional. The appellate court reversed as to the grandfather clause, and otherwise affirmed. Both parties appealed. The court reversed. The court held that there was no rational basis for the 50 percent requirement and the effect of the ordinance would be to protect small liquor stores from competition. The court held that the ordinance was not rationally related to the goal of limiting liquor sellers. The court held that the grandfather provision violated the Equal Protection Clause because the distinction was arbitrary, not germane to the purpose of the law, and was based on existing circumstances only.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment, which had affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's judgment declaring that the city's liquor licensing ordinance was constitutional.

Swanson Furniture Co. v. Advance Transformer Co.


No. 81-470


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


105 Wis. 2d 321; 313 N.W.2d 840; 1982 Wisc. LEXIS 2488; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P9145


December 3, 1981, Submitted on Briefs  
January 5, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Wood County, Fred A. Fink, Judge. On by-pass from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court is reversed and the case is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a furniture company, its owner, and its insurer, sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Wood County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent manufacturers in a products liability suit after finding that respondents were within the protections of Wis. Stat. § 893.155 (1977).


OVERVIEW: Appellants alleged that respondents were liable to them under a product liability theory, both strictly and in negligence, for fire damages caused by defective light fixtures installed in their furniture store's basement when it was built. The evidence was that no respondent dealt directly with appellants in the construction, and that the fixtures were manufactured with no particular project in mind. Respondents obtained summary judgment based on trial court findings that § 893.155 applied to the claims because respondents were suppliers of material to improve real property. Appellants argued that § 893.155 was unconstitutional and that respondents were not in the protected class. On review, the court found that no respondent was within the protected class because there was no proof the light fixture in question was designed for the construction or even in contemplation of the construction, and that summary judgment was improper because § 893.155 governed only the statutorily identifiable services or materials deliberately directed towards or chosen for a particular real property improvement project.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court granting summary judgment in favor of respondents and remanded the case for further proceedings consistent with its opinion.

Basinas v. State


No. 79-1552


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


104 Wis. 2d 539; 312 N.W.2d 483; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 3044


October 5, 1981, Argued  
December 1, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing and remanding 99 Wis. 2d 412, 299 N.W.2d 295.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions to remand to the personnel commission for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a career executive employee, sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a trial court's judgment. The trial court affirmed respondent State Personnel Commission's finding that under Wis. Stat. § 230.44(1)(c) (1977) and Wis. Admin. Code § PERS 30.10 (1975), it did not have subject matter jurisdiction to hear the employee's appeal regarding his reassignment to a job with a lower pay range.


OVERVIEW: The employee alleged that his reassignment was for disciplinary purposes and constituted an improper and unreasonable exercise of the appointing authority's discretion. The lower courts determined that Wis. Admin. Code § PERS 30.10(1) deprived the Commission of jurisdiction because it stated that reassignment of a career executive employee did not constitute a demotion that was appealable under Wis. Stat. § 230.44(1)(c), which provided appeals for demotions. On appeal, the court interpreted Wis. Admin. Code § PERS 30.10 as a definition of demotion. Wis. Admin. Code § PERS 30.10(1) stated that reassignments to jobs in lower pay ranges were not demotions, but then § PERS 30.10(2) and (5) declared that reassignments for disciplinary purposes, or reassignments that constituted an unreasonable and improper exercise of discretion, were demotions appealable to the Commission. Wis. Stat. § 230.44(1)(c) and Wis. Admin. Code § PERS 30.10 gave the Commission jurisdiction over the employee's appeal of a reassignment to a job in a lower pay range because the appeal alleged that the reassignment was an unreasonable and improper exercise of discretion or was for disciplinary purposes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that held that the Commission lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the employee's appeal and remanded the case with directions to remand the case to the Commission for proceedings.

December 1, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing and remanding 102 Wis. 2d 723, 308 N.W.2d 421.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decisions of the court of appeals and the trial court are reversed and cause remanded for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State appealed from a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed an order for default judgment entered in a lower court in an action against defendant for drunken driving violations.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of drunken driving on two occasions during a three-month period. On both occasions, a civil forfeiture penalty was entered on his record pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 346.65(2)(a)(1). However, the Judicial Court Commissioner (Commissioner) was later advised that the court was obligated, upon the second occasion, to impose criminal penalties. The state appealed from the appellate court's affirmance of the trial court's holding that § 346.65(2) must have been construed like general repeater statutes, and therefore, the penalty enhancing provisions were inapplicable. Since defendant's second violation was a criminal proceeding, the Commissioner's entry of judgment was a nullity because he was without subject matter jurisdiction. The court also held that the lower courts had erred. It concluded that the criminal penalties of § 346.65(2)(a) were applicable to violations of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1) committed prior to conviction for a first offense within a five-year period. The judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments below in the State's action against defendant for drunken driving violations.

State v. Vick


No. 80-1046


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


104 Wis. 2d 678; 312 N.W.2d 489; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 3055


November 2, 1981, Argued  
December 1, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing 101 Wis. 2d 735, 306 N.W.2d 308.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed, and the judgment of the trial court is reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals, which reversed defendant's conviction for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of DUI. On review, the appellate court reversed based on an ambiguous jury instruction. On further review, the court reversed and reinstated the conviction. The court found that the instruction did not set forth a mandatory presumption. The jurors could have rationally inferred that defendant, who had a blood alcohol level of 0.13 plus percent at the time of testing, was under the influence of an intoxicant at the time of operation of his vehicle. Under the test for a permissive inference, the court upheld the trial court's discretion in concluding that the inferred fact of driving while intoxicated flowed more likely than not from the proven fact of the breathalyzer results based upon all the evidence. Furthermore, the qualifying instruction regarding the legal effect of the presumption that stated "But, you should so find only if " was sufficient to overcome any infirmities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court and reinstated defendant's conviction by the trial court of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant.

Office of State Public Defender v. Circuit Court for Dodge County


No. 79-1431


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


104 Wis. 2d 579; 312 N.W.2d 767; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 3056


April 1, 1981, Argued  
December 1, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing 99 Wis. 2d 806, 310 N.W.2d 461.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision of the court of appeals reversed; order of the circuit court vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff public defender's office appealed the judgment and order of a Wisconsin the Court of Appeals, which affirmed the appointment of the public defender's office by respondents, a circuit court and a judge, over the public defender's office's objection, to represent a prisoner who had filed a pro se conditions-of-confinement claim.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner filed a complaint alleging that his disciplinary transfer from one correctional facility to another without an opportunity to refute the charges brought against him violated his rights to equal protection and due process. The public defender's office participated in an unsuccessful informal attempt at settlement. When the prisoner filed a pro se motion for summary judgment, the circuit court ordered the public defender's office to represent him. The circuit court ruled that Wis. Stat. § 977.05(4) required the public defender's office to represent the prisoner. The appeals court affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed and held that although the circuit court had inherent authority to appoint counsel for the prisoner, in the interest of orderly administration of justice and in the exercise of the court's superintending and administrative authority pursuant to Wis. Const. art. VII, § 3, the trial court should not have ordered the public defender's office to act as counsel for when it had declined to representation. When it refused to represent the inmate, the circuit court should have appointed counsel for the inmate other than the public defender's office.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appeals court's order requiring the public defender's office to represent the prisoner and vacated the order of the circuit court.

 

281 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Kollasch v. Adamany


No. 79-1579


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


104 Wis. 2d 552; 313 N.W.2d 47; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 3045


September 8, 1981, Argued  
December 1, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing and remanding 99 Wis. 2d 533, 299 N.W.2d 891.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions that the circuit court enter judgment declaring that plaintiffs are not liable for sales tax for meals served at the center and they they are not required to obtain a seller's permit.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sisters of a religious community filed suit against defendant Secretary of the Department of Revenue for a declaratory judgment that they were not liable for sales tax for the sale of meals to their guests. The sisters sought to enjoin the Secretary from penalizing them for failure to obtain a sales tax permit. The sisters challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which held that the sale of the meals was taxable.


OVERVIEW: The sisters, under their religious direction, offered a center on church grounds as a meeting place. The sisters provided simple meals to the guests of the center, utilizing produce from the center garden. Guests who were able to pay for food and lodging did so, while those who could not pay worked around the center. All guests were invited to help with clean up after meals. The court held that the sisters were not retailers under Wis. Stat. § 77.51(7) and were therefore not liable for the sales tax imposed by Wis. Stat. § 77.52. The court found that: (1) the sisters presented extensive evidence in support of their position that the meals they served and ate with their guests were in furtherance of their religious beliefs; (2) all guests were welcome; (3) food and lodging was equally provided to guests who were unable to pay; (4) financial records of the center revealed a loss of money; (5) evidence indicated that the sisters' serving of meals was not a means of supporting their ministry, but an integral part of their ministry.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and remanded to the trial court with directions to enter judgment declaring that the sisters were not liable for sales tax for the meals and that they were not required to obtain a seller's permit.

 

282 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Jankowski v. Milwaukee County


No. 79-1896


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


104 Wis. 2d 431; 312 N.W.2d 45; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 3038


September 9, 1981, Argued  
November 3, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing 99 Wis. 2d 803, 300 N.W.2d 82.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed. Rights declared.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff class, whose members had been involuntarily committed, sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which upheld a decision requiring the class to reimburse defendant county for the commitment costs pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 46.10. The class claimed that it was not liable for the commitment costs because the commitment procedures had violated the class's due process rights.


OVERVIEW: The class, whose members had been involuntarily committed, was released because the commitment procedures had violated the class's due process rights. Following the class's release, the county sought to recover the commitment costs from the class pursuant to § 46.10. Thereafter, the class brought a declaratory judgment action against the county, and after the appeals court upheld a decision for the county, the class sought review. Upon review, the court held that § 46.10 applied only to due process commitments.Specifically, the court held that because the proceedings had not been adequate to sustain a finding that the class needed care and treatment, there had not been a valid commitment order; thus the class could not be considered "committed" under § 46.10. The court also held that the class could not be required to pay for the commitment costs because: (1) such a requirement was an absurd interpretation of § 46.10; and (2) the principles of equal protection forbid such a requirement. Finally, the court held that rendering the class liable for the commitment costs would deprive the class of its property because the illegal commitments had deprived the class of its liberty.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment which upheld a decision requiring the class, whose members had been involuntarily committed, to reimburse the county for the commitment costs.

 

283 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


County of Portage v. Steinpreis


Nos. 80-037, 80-038


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


104 Wis. 2d 466; 312 N.W.2d 731; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 3041


September 10, 1981, Submitted on Briefs  
November 3, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing 98 Wis. 2d 748, 297 N.W.2d 515.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the circuit court's decision and held that Wis. Stat. § 299.21 (1977) was unconstitutional in requiring prepayment of the jury fee and violated the equal protection clauses of both the federal and state constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged Wis. Stat. § 299.21 (1977), which required prepayment of a jury fee and costs upon the filing of a demand for a jury trial in a small claims action. He contended that the statute violated the equal protection clauses of both the federal and state constitutions. The trial court held that the statute was constitutional, but the court of appeals reversed. The court reversed, holding that the requirement that small claims litigants pay a fee upon demand for a jury trial did not violate the right to a jury trial under the constitution. It also did not violate the equal protection clause of either the federal or state constitutions because (1) there was a rational basis for classifying small claims litigants differently from those proceeding under Wis. Stat. chs. 801-807, under which an action was meant to be summary in nature; (2) the statutory fee assessed was reasonable when one considered the actual cost of the courtroom proceedings; (3) when a jury trial was demanded in a small claims action, more court time was needed, therefore, costs were increased; and (4) assessing such costs helped to insure the sincerity of the litigant's jury demand.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals.

285 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Grobarchik v. State


No. 80-808-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


102 Wis. 2d 461; 307 N.W.2d 170; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 2770


June 3, 1981, Argued  
June 30, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing 99 Wis.2d 805, 300 N.W.2d 84.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed and the modified judgment filed July 15, 1977, is reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) that vacated the trial court's amended sentence against him and ordered the reinstatement of his original sentence.


OVERVIEW: As punishment for defendant's two counts of armed robbery, the trial court adjudged imprisonment for no more than 15 years, to be followed by five years of probation, its term to begin upon defendant's release from prison. Defendant secured post-trial modification of this sentence under Wis. Stat. § 57.01 (1965). Defendant then appealed the modification, with the result that the lower court remanded the action to the trial court with instructions to reinstate the original sentence. Defendant appealed. A trial court's authority to fashion a sentence derived from statute, not the trial court's inherent authority. "Sentence" was a term of art in the criminal law, meaning the judgment by which a trial court imposed a punishment or penalty provided by statute for a particular offense. A defendant's term of confinement was not equivalent to the duration of his sentence. Under § 57.01, a sentence of imprisonment was a term of incarceration or supervision on parole which continued until defendant was finally discharged.The statute did not authorize the imposition of probation upon release from prison on parole. The trial court properly corrected its error by resentencing defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court and reinstated the trial court's modified sentence against defendant.

State v. Mosley

In re Estate of Safran


No. 80-108


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


102 Wis. 2d 79; 306 N.W.2d 27; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 2758; 25 A.L.R.4th 766


March 2, 1981, Argued  
June 2, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on July 6, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Walter T. Norlin, Reserve Judge, presiding. On certification from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- That part of the order of the trial court disposing of property jointly held by Bernard Safran and Mrs. Safran is affirmed. That part of the order disposing of the remainder of the estate is reversed and the cause remanded to the circuit court for Milwaukee county for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In probate proceedings, the court accepted certification from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) to review the challenges of appellant alternate beneficiaries and cross-appellant son of the testator to an order of the trial court that disqualified the son from inheritance due to his conviction for the reckless homicide of the testator and ordered the decedent's estate held in trust for the benefit of any issue born to the son.


OVERVIEW: The testator's son, the principal beneficiary of her will, was convicted of causing the testator's death by reckless conduct pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 940.06 (1975). The trial court held that the son was conclusively disqualified from his inheritance by the conviction. On appeal, the court noted that under earlier cases only an intentional killer was disqualified from inheritance. Because the legislature had not modified this standard, the court inferred a legislative intent to limit disqualification to intentional killers. Thus, the court held that the criminal offense of reckless homicide did not by itself disqualify the son from his inheritance because the intent to kill was not an essential element of the crime. The court further held that a conviction for that offense was not admissible to show disqualification in the subsequent probate proceeding. The court directed that the son was to be disqualified from his inheritance only if it was proven in civil proceedings, by clear and convincing evidence, that he unlawfully and intentionally killed his mother. If proof of disqualification was made, a constructive trust was to be imposed for the benefit of the alternate beneficiaries.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the order of the trial court that disposed of property jointly held by the decedent and the son by dividing it equally between the son and the decedent's estate. That part of the trial court's order disposing of the remainder of the estate was reversed and the cause was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings to determine whether the son intentionally killed his mother.

In Interest of W.


No. 80-2191


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


102 Wis. 2d 118; 306 N.W.2d 46; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 2760


April 1, 1981, Argued  
June 2, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on July 6, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order and a Judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Ralph Adam Fine, Circuit Judge. On by-pass from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The orders and judgment of the trial court terminating the parental rights of Mrs. R. to J.L.W. and granting guardianship to Mr. and Mrs. B. are reversed. J.L.W. is to be returned to Mrs. R.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On a by-pass from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), the court accepted review of an appeal filed by appellant mother from an order and judgment of the circuit court, which permanently terminated the mother's parental rights to her son and granted guardianship to respondents, the child's aunt and uncle.


OVERVIEW: The mother became pregnant outside of wedlock and asked her sister and her husband to raise the child. After the birth, the mother changed her mind about permitting the adoption, but because of financial difficulties, she allowed the child to remain with its aunt and uncle. Later, the aunt and uncle petitioned for guardianship of the child pursuant Wis. Stat. §§ 48.14, 880.03, 880.15 (1977). The trial court terminated the mother's parental rights upon the jury's findings that the mother had abandoned and neglected to provide for her child. However, the court reversed the termination on appeal. Recognizing the constitutional protection of liberty afforded to parental interest in a child, the court held that, except under unusual circumstances, the due process protections of the state and federal constitutions prohibited the termination of a natural parent's rights, unless the parent was unfit. The court found that the record did not support a finding that the mother was unfit. The court noted that at all times the mother was concerned for the child and had permitted the child to live with its aunt and uncle only until she could re-establish her career and a home for her children.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders and judgment of the trial court that terminated the mother's parental rights and granted guardianship to the child's aunt and uncle. The court directed that the child be returned to the mother.

In re Rabideau


No. 80-453-D


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


102 Wis. 2d 16; 306 N.W.2d 1; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 2756


March 3, 1981, Argued  
June 2, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a report and disciplinary order of Rodney L. Young, Referee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney challenged a report and disciplinary order of a referee (Wisconsin), which found, inter alia, that the attorney was subject to discipline for professional misconduct due to a violation of a criminal statute involving moral turpitude. The referee ordered that the attorney's license to practice law be revoked and imposed the costs of the proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The attorney provided marijuana to a former client who was a juvenile. The attorney was convicted of contributing to the delinquency of a minor and possession of a controlled substance. The referee ordered that his license to practice law be revoked and imposed costs of the proceeding. The court modified the referee's order by directing, instead of revocation, suspension for three years. The court held that the attorney's convictions adequately showed moral turpitude, and Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 21.05(1) (1980) adequately informed the attorney as to the definition of "moral turpitude. The court held that a responsible attorney should have had no cognitive problem recognizing that criminal actions of different sorts may have struck a factfinding tribunal as more or less morally reprehensible, and should have been able to tailor his own behavior accordingly. The court held that whether a person's conduct indicated moral turpitude depended upon the circumstances of each case. Whatever ancillary punitive effects attached in a practical sense to an attorney's civil disciplinary proceeding did not violate the state constitutional proscription against double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order of the referee by directing, instead of revocation of the attorney's license, suspension for three years. The court sustained the imposition of costs and the requirement that they be paid prior to reinstatement in the bar. The court reversed that part of the referee's disposition ordering that payment of fines, penalties, and costs imposed in the criminal prosecution be made a condition of reinstatement.

Law Enforcement Standards Bd. v. Lyndon Station


No. 78-456


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


101 Wis. 2d 472; 305 N.W.2d 89; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 2741


March 4, 1981, Argued  
April 29, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motions for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on June 8, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming 98 Wis.2d 229, 295 N.W.2d 818.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a village and others, challenged the judgment of a court of appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the grant of a peremptory writ of mandamus upholding the position of respondent, the Wisconsin Law Enforcement Standards Board (LESB). The LESB directed the removal of the village chief of police and deemed the chief ineligible pursuant to Wis. Admin. Code § 2.01(1) (Feb. 1981).


OVERVIEW: The village, aware of the police chief's convictions, hired him believing that the chief's violation constituted a misdemeanor rather than a felony. The LESB denied certification. The court affirmed and held that village acted in violation of Wis. Admin. Code § 2.01(1)(d), which had the force and effect of law and was superior to any conflicting action of the village. Wis. Stat. § 111.32(5)(h) prohibited discrimination in employment on the basis of arrest or conviction unless the subject of conviction was substantially related to the ability of the person to perform the job. The court held that § 111.32(5)(h) modified § 2.01(1)(d) and that the two were not in conflict. The chief was convicted of misconduct in public office on 26 felony counts of falsifying uniform traffic citations. As a police officer for the village, he was charged with enforcing traffic laws. His conviction for falsifying traffic tickets had a substantial relationship to the duties of a police officer called upon to issue traffic citations. The court held that the chief was barred from holding a law enforcement position in Wisconsin. The writ of mandamus was properly issued to compel an urgent need.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment upholding the grant of a writ of mandamus.

Martino v. McDonald's Corp.


No. 80-085


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


101 Wis. 2d 612; 304 N.W.2d 780; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 2735


March 2, 1981, Argued  
April 29, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming 98 Wis.2d 755, 300 N.W.2d 80.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff franchisee sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed a decision by the circuit court finding that defendant franchisor had failed to give the franchisee notice or an opportunity to cure any deficiencies in the franchise agreement as required by law.


OVERVIEW: The franchisee operated a restaurant under a franchise agreement with the franchisor. The franchisor terminated the relationship without notice. The franchisee filed suit in circuit court alleging that the franchisor had failed to comply with Wis. Stat. § 135.04, requiring 90 days' prior written notice of termination or cancellation for any reason and 10 days' written notice in the event of nonpayment of sums due under the dealership. The circuit court agreed that proper notice under this provision, enacted after the franchise began, had not been complied with. The court of appeals reversed, holding that the provisions of § 135.04 were to applied prospectively only, and that since the franchisor had complied with the nonrenewal and cancellation policies in its original contract, the franchisee had no cause of action. The court affirmed, holding that § 135.04 was to be applied prospectively only, lest it be an unconstitutional violation of the obligation of contracts in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1, which provides that no state shall pass any law impairing the obligation of contracts. Here, the contract between the parties had been complied with.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of appeals, which held that the circuit court erred in retroactively applying law requiring greater notice to franchisee of termination of franchise agreement than that provided for in original franchise agreement.

Wipperfurth v. U-Haul Co. of Western Wisconsin, Inc.


No. 80-144


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


101 Wis. 2d 586; 304 N.W.2d 767; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 2736


March 2, 1981, Argued  
April 29, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming 98 Wis.2d 516, 297 N.W.2d 65.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dealer sought review of the judgment from the court of appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the trial court's finding that the Wisconsin Fair Dealership Law, Wis. Stat. § 135, was retroactive and constitutional. The dealer had filed an action against defendant grantor, who had terminated the dealership.


OVERVIEW: Due to a change in circumstances, the grantor terminated the dealership with the dealer. As provided for in the written contract, the grantor gave the dealer 30 days written notice. The dealer instituted an action, alleging that § 135 gave him additional protections that were not present in the contract, that § 135 was retroactive, and that § 135 was a reasonable exercise of state police power. On appeal, the court held that retroactive application of § 135 was unconstitutional because it violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. The court found that the predecessor to Wis. Stat. § 135 clearly stated that the statute would have prospective application. The revised § 135, however, removed the prospective application clause and stated that the statute was to be liberally construed to promote its underlying purposes of protecting dealers. The court found that the legislative history and the language indicated an intent to apply § 135 both prospectively and retroactively. However, the court held that such retroactive application violated the Contracts Clause because § 135 substantially impaired the rights and remedies of the contract by unnecessarily using police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment finding that the Wisconsin Fair Dealership Law was prospective only.

Soo Line R. Co. v. Department of Transp., Div. of Highways


No. 80-2087


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


101 Wis. 2d 64; 303 N.W.2d 626; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 2713


March 4, 1981, Argued  
March 31, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: William F. Eich, Circuit Judge. On certification from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff railroad company brought an action against defendant, the Wisconsin Department of Transportation, seeking a declaration that 1977 Wis. Laws 418, § 923(48)(a) violated Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18 and a judgment enjoining the Department from enforcing its terms. The Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) granted the company's motion for summary judgment. The Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Department had petitioned the Wisconsin Public Service Commission for approval of an at-grade railroad crossing where a highway crossed the company's tracks. The Commission determined that an at-grade crossing would endanger public safety. The Department appealed to a circuit court, which affirmed the Commission's order. The Department did not appeal. Thereafter, as part of what was known as the budget review bill, 1977 Wis. Laws 418, § 923(48)(a) was enacted specifically to direct the company and the Department to establish an at-grade crossing at the same location. The court held that the enactment of 1977 Wis. Laws 418, § 923(48)(a) violated Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18. It was a private or local law that embraced more than one subject, and the subject was not expressed in the title of 1977 Wis. Laws ch. 418. 1977 Wis. Laws 418, § 923(48)(a) was a legislative response to a unique problem that affected only the company, reversing the Commission's decision regarding that unique problem, which was affirmed by a circuit court. It was constitutionally infirm as it was included in a bill that embraced many subjects, and the title did not provide the full scope of its provisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Aetna Life Ins. Co. v. Mitchell


No. 80-518


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


101 Wis. 2d 90; 303 N.W.2d 639; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 2718


January 7, 1981, Argued  
March 31, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on May 4, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: W. L. Jackman, Reserve Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Commissioner of Insurance appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County declaring Wis. Admin. Code § 2.14(3)(a) to be invalid because it directed insurance agents to disseminate misleading information in violation of Wis. Stat. § 628.34(1)(a) and enjoining defendant from enforcing the administrative rule.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff insurance companies sought a temporary and a permanent injunction enjoining defendant Commissioner of Insurance from enforcing Wis. Admin. Code § 2.14(3) and sought a declaration that the rule was invalid. The rule required insurance agents to distribute a buyer's guide and policy summary to all prospective purchasers. The lower court found the rule to be invalid and issued an injunction. Defendant appealed. The supreme court affirmed because the information contained in the guide and policy summary failed to accurately predict the least costly policy under all circumstances and other calculations provided more accurate measures of the relative cost of whole life policies terminated by death. Thus, defendant failed to provide reasonable grounds for the rule and the enactment of the rule exceeded the defendant's rule-making powers because the rule mandated that insurance agents distribute misleading information in violation of Wis. Stat. § 628.34(1).


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because defendant's buyer's guide and policy summary were misleading because they contained incomplete information; thus, defendant did not demonstrate reasonable grounds for rule requiring dissemination of this information by insurance agents, and rule was beyond scope of defendant's rule-making powers because it mandated a violation of § 628.34(1)(a).

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted appellant creditor's petition for review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the judgment of the circuit court denying the creditor's claim filed against respondent estate. The estate's personal representative objected to the allowance of demand as an untimely claim barred by the operation of Wis. Stat. § 859.01. The claim was dismissed and the judgment was affirmed on appeal. The court modified and affirmed the judgment of the appellate court. The court first noted that there was no dispute that the attorney general was not given notice that the creditor planned to challenge the constitutionality of § 859.01. The court concluded that lack of compliance with the rule did not preclude review. The court then determined that the creditor's probate claim was cut off by operation of the statute of limitation. The court noted that it was the creditor's own fault that he did not keep in close enough contact with the decedent to know that he had died. The court rejected the creditor's contention that the denial of its claim violated the commerce clause.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the appellate court, and as modified, it affirmed.

 

296 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Briggs & Stratton Corp. v. Noll


No. 80-1098-OA


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


100 Wis. 2d 650; 302 N.W.2d 487; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 2707


January 6, 1981, Argued  
March 3, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Action for declaratory judgment.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- It is adjudged and declared that sec. 29m, ch. 278, Laws of 1979, is unconstitutional and void and that the increase in maximum benefits authorized by sec. 6 of that chapter shall apply to claims arising out of injuries occurring on or after May 13, 1980, and not to claims arising out of injuries occurring before that date.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employers filed an original action for declaratory judgment with the court to determine the effective date for a statutory increased in worker's compensation benefits and to determine the constitutionality of that statute. Respondent state officials argued that the statute that was effective May 13 was retroactive to January 1.


OVERVIEW: The legislature intended for a bill to implement increased worker's compensation benefits effective January 1st, but procedural delays did not put it into effect until May 13; an amendment added to the bill on February 12 specifically stated that the bill was to be effective retroactively to January 1st. The employers argued that retroactive application of the law to injuries arising from January 1 to May 12 meant recalculating benefits on about 10,000 cases. They argued that the law had to be applied only prospectively or else it was unconstitutional. The court agreed, holding that worker's compensation benefits vested as of the day of the injury and that retroactive application of the statute to those vested rights violated due process and equal protection under both the state and federal constitutions. The court held that the bill had to be interpreted in a manner that would find it constitutional if at all possible, and that meant that the law could only be applied prospectively to injuries arising on or after May 13. The court struck the February 12th amendment as void and affirmed the rest of the bill as constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court struck as void and unconstitutional the amendment to the legislation that directed the bill's retroactive application to January 1. The court held that the rest of the bill, applied prospectively as of the bill's effective date of May 13 was constitutional and affected worker's compensation benefits only as of that date.

State v. Kummer


No. 80-892-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


100 Wis. 2d 220; 301 N.W.2d 240; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 2683


January 7, 1981, Argued  
February 2, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Wood County: Fred A. Fink, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Wood County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of second-degree sexual assault of a person over the age of 12 years and under the age of 15 years in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 940.225(2)(e) and 940.225(4) (1977). Defendant asserted that the statutes under which he was convicted were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of having sexual intercourse with a young woman who was 14 years and 10 months old at the time. He defended his actions on the fact that the young woman consented and that they loved each other and were planning to marry. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the information based on the fact that the statute was unconstitutional. The motion was denied. The jury was instructed that under state law, a person under the age of 15 was not competent to consent to sexual contact. Defendant appealed, asserting that the statute's definition of consent was unconstitutional because it established a conclusive presumption of non-consent when the victim was under the age of 15. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that the existing statute was constitutionally valid even though it was cosmetically defective. The court concluded that consent was not an element of the offense of second-degree sexual consent if the victim was under the age of 15 and, therefore, defendant's reliance upon consent as a defense was misplaced.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for sexual assault of a person over the age of 12 years and under the age of 15 years.

 

298 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Omernick v. Department of Natural Resources


Nos. 77-557, 77-558


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


100 Wis. 2d 234; 301 N.W.2d 437; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 2684


November 24, 1980, Argued  
February 2, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motions for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on April 6, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming 94 Wis.2d 309, 287 N.W.2d 841.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowners sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the circuit court's order reversing the order of cross-petitioner Department of Natural Resources (DNR). DNR directed the landowners to remove certain obstructions from two river beds located on their property, and the circuit court reversed and remanded to the DNR for further proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The DNR directed the landowners to remove obstructions from two river beds on their property. The hearing examiner found that the obstructions had been constructed in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 30.12, 31.05, 31.06 (1973), that no permits had been issued for them, and that the waterways involved were navigable. The examiner concluded that the obstructions were nuisances under Wis. Stat. §§ 30.15(4), 31.25 (1973). The circuit court remanded the proceeding to the DNR, concluding that there was not substantial evidence to support the finding of navigability, and that the search warrant was issued without probable cause. On the DNR's appeal, the court of appeals reversed, concluding that substantial evidence supported the examiner's findings and that the issue of the search warrant's legality was improperly considered in the circuit court. The court affirmed, holding that the search warrant issue was not preserved before the hearing examiner, that a reasonable man could have concluded that the streams were navigable, and that the DNR did not have to show that penalties were inadequate to protect the public interest as a prerequisite to proceeding under Wis. Stat. § 30.03(4)(a) (1973).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of appeals decision reversing the circuit court's order.

 

299 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Mannino v. Davenport


No. 79-1140


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


99 Wis. 2d 602; 299 N.W.2d 823; 1981 Wisc. LEXIS 2679


November 25, 1980, Argued  
January 6, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from judgments of the Circuit Court for Dane County: William D. Byrne, Circuit Judge. On certification from Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a husband and a wife, appealed the judgments of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment to defendants, a supervising doctor and a resident, in a medical malpractice suit.


OVERVIEW: In the suit, the husband and wife claimed that the wife was injured after the resident negligently performed cosmetic surgery and that the supervising doctor negligently failed to supervise the resident. When the trial court granted summary judgment to the doctors, the couple appealed. Affirming, the court concluded that the affidavits of the opposing parties raised no issue of material fact and that summary judgment was not inappropriate. The court did not doubt that the wife perceived the supervising doctor to be acting in a private capacity after he quoted to her a $ 1,000 fee. Wis. Stat. § 895.45 provided that no suit could have been brought against a state employee for any act committed in the discharge of duties. The statute did not create an exception for plaintiffs with a mistaken belief about a defendant's status as a state employee. The suit had to be dismissed for failure to comply with § 895.45(1). The husband and wife were not under any physical or legal disabilities after the operation. They should have known that they were dealing with state employees. Compliance with § 895.45 was not unreasonable so as to offend their due process rights or their right to recovery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments, which granted summary judgment to the supervising doctor and the resident in the medical malpractice suit.

Sharpe Furniture, Inc. v. Buckstaff


No. 79-277


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


99 Wis. 2d 114; 299 N.W.2d 219; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2816; 19 A.L.R.4th 421


September 29, 1980, Argued  
November 25, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, with Costs, on January 13, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals which affirmed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County: William E. Crane, Circuit Judge. Affirming 92 Wis.2d 912, 286 N.W.2d 647.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, debtor's husband, sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) in favor of respondent retailer in respondent's action against appellant and debtor to recover the cost of a sofa purchased on credit by debtor.


OVERVIEW: Wife purchased a sofa from respondent on credit. Wife did not represent that she was acting on behalf of appellant, and appellant had previously written a letter to the local credit bureau service stating that he would not be responsible for any credit extended to wife. Wife and appellant failed to pay for the sofa, and respondent sued both appellant and wife. The district court held that wife was liable for the amount due on the sofa pursuant to her contract and that appellant was also liable under the doctrine of necessaries. The appellate court affirmed the judgment. The supreme court also affirmed the judgment because the doctrine remained viable, the sofa was a reasonable and proper item for appellant and wife's household, and there was an inference of reasonable need.


OUTCOME: Judgment in favor of respondent was affirmed because the doctrine of necessaries was applicable and the sofa was reasonable and necessary.

 

301 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Maynard v. Port Publications, Inc.


No. 78-602


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


98 Wis. 2d 555; 297 N.W.2d 500; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2808; 16 A.L.R.4th 1361; 6 Media L. Rep. 2239


September 29, 1980, Argued  
October 28, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals affirming a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: P. Charles Jones, Circuit Judge. Affirming 91 Wis.2d 850, 284 N.W.2d 121.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner victim sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals affirming an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted respondent printer's motion for summary judgment in her defamation action.


OVERVIEW: The printer contracted with said newspaper for the printing of its newspaper. The newspaper published a picture of the victim's face imposed on a nude figure of another accompanied by what the victim claimed was a defamatory article. The victim thereafter brought an action against the newspaper and the printer based on defamation. The trial court granted the printer's motion for summary judgment and the court of appeals affirmed. The state supreme court granted review of the victim's petition and affirmed the order. The printer's affidavits stated it had no knowledge of the content of the issue of the newspaper in question because no employee read the photographic negatives prior to the making of the photographic plates and the victim offered no opposing proof. Further, as a contract printer, independent from and exercising no control over the publication, it had no duty to inspect for libelous content the material it contracted to print. To be held libel for defamation because of their role in the publication process, the printer had to know or have reason to know of the existence of the libel. The printer had no such knowledge; hence summary judgment was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The order granting summary judgment in the printer's favor in the victim's defamation action was affirmed.

 

302 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Guardianship of Nelson


No. 79-997


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


98 Wis. 2d 261; 296 N.W.2d 736; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2751


September 3, 1980, Argued  
September 30, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Door County: Edwin C. Stephan, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a guardian of an incompetent, sought review from an order of the Circuit Court for Door County (Wisconsin), which ordered the guardian to pay to respondent, the Department of Health and Social Services, all funds available from the guardianship assets for the cost of care and maintenance of the incompetent.


OVERVIEW: An order was entered requiring the guardian of the estate of an incompetent to pay the Department all funds available from the guardianship assets in excess of a certain amount. The order was issued under the authority of Wis. Stat. § 46.10(2). On appeal, the court held that § 46.10(2) and (2m), which authorized the collection of the cost of care and maintenance from persons admitted or committed to a state institution but which exempted persons in prisons from a similar liability, did not violate the equal protection clause of the federal or state constitutions. Persons transferred to mental health facilities under Wis. Stat. § 51.37(5) after conviction and during the term of their sentence were exempt from § 46.10(2) liability and this was not violative the equal protection rights of the guardian's ward. Amendments to § 46.10(2) did not constitute an ex post facto law when applied to the ward, who was found not guilty by reason of mental disease prior to the amendments. The ex post facto doctrine did not apply because liability of the ward's estate was unrelated to criminal proceedings and because a charge for services did not constitute punishment and was not a penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

303 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Midcontinent Broadcasting Co. v. Wisconsin Dep't of Revenue


No. 78-203


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


98 Wis. 2d 379; 297 N.W.2d 191; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2760


September 4, 1980, Argued  
September 30, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing 91 Wis.2d 579, 284 N.W.2d 112.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed; judgment of the circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Wisconsin Department of Revenue appealed from a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the decision of the trial court and held that the sale of tangible personal property, broadcasting equipment, by appellant broadcasting company was an "occasional sale" that was exempt from sales tax pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 77.54(7), 77.51(10)(a) (1969).


OVERVIEW: The broadcasting company claimed that its sale of broadcasting equipment and other assets was exempt from state sales tax pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 77.54(7) (1969), which exempted "occasional sales" from taxation. The company argued that the sale came within the statutory definition of occasional sales, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 77.51(10)(a) (1969), because the sale of assets was isolated and infrequent in relation to its broadcasting business, which generated revenues through the sale of advertising. However, because the company held a seller's permit to sell phonograph records, the court held on appeal that the company fell within an exception to the "occasional sales" tax exemption. The court explained that Wis. Stat. § 77.51(10)(a) (1969) specifically provided that no sale of any tangible personal property was considered an occasional sale if at the time of such sale the seller held a seller's permit. The court reasoned that the fact that the company's sales permit was intended only for record sales was irrelevant because the permits were general in nature. The court further held that the tax was rational and did not violate the commerce clause, due process, or equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the Department of Revenue.

305 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Rabe v. Ferris


No. 80-327-W


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


97 Wis. 2d 63; 293 N.W.2d 151; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2615


June 2, 1980, Argued  
June 27, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Action. Habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner accused brought an action for a writ of habeas corpus seeking release from a county jail pending his trial on four counts of homicide by intoxicated use of a motor vehicle contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.08.


OVERVIEW: The accused, unable to post bail, was jailed awaiting trial and filed a demand for a speedy trial. A substantial delay resulted from the State's appeal of an order by the trial court consolidating four counts of homicide by intoxicated use of a motor vehicle in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.08. Over the accused's objection, the appellate court granted the State's petition for leave to appeal the consolidation order and stayed the trial court proceeding pending the appeal. The trial court ordered a continuance and that the accused not be released. His petition for leave to appeal was denied. In the meantime, the court reversed the consolidation order. The accused then petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus for release from custody because of the delay caused by the State's interlocutory appeal. The court denied the accused's petition, concluding that the stay of proceedings tolled the running of the 90-day period for a speedy trial provided by § 971.10(2)(a), and even had it not, the trial court's continuance order to maintain the status quo rendered the release provisions of § 971.10 inoperative. The court did not find continued pretrial confinement to be a due process violation.


OUTCOME: The court denied the accused's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

306 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Steele v. State


No. 77-061-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


97 Wis. 2d 72; 294 N.W.2d 2; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2618


November 28, 1978 and November 7, 1979, Argued  
June 27, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on August 11, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Writs of Error to review a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Monroe County: Peter G. Pappas, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Monroe County (Wisconsin), which entered a jury verdict that convicted him of the first degree murder of his wife. The trial court had excluded, at the guilt phase of the trial, expert opinion testimony that defendant lacked the capacity to intend to kill his wife. Defendant contended that the exclusion of the testimony deprived him of the right to offer a defense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not dispute the fact that he shot his wife. He claimed that he did not intend to kill her. After a bifurcated jury trial, defendant was convicted of the first-degree murder of his wife. After the court decided in Schimmel v. State, 84 Wis.2d 287, 267 N.W.2d 271 (Wis. 1978) that during the guilt phase of a bifurcated trial, competent psychiatric evidence relevant to defendant's mental state at the time of the crime was admissible, defendant filed a motion for summary reversal, which the trial court denied. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the denial of defendant's motion, overruling that portion of Schimmel v. State. In the guilt phase of defendant's trial, the trial court properly excluded expert opinion evidence in respect to defendant's mental capacity to form an intent to kill his wife. The court did not exclude from admission in the guilt phase of the trial ordinarily admissible evidence that tended to prove a defendant's state of mind, but barred introduction of expert opinion testimony at the guilt phase of a trial that tended to prove or disprove the defendant's capacity to form the requisite criminal intent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of first degree murder and the trial court's order that denied defendant's motion for summary reversal.

 

307 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


May v. State


No. 77-853-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


97 Wis. 2d 175; 293 N.W.2d 478; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2623


June 4, 1980, Argued  
June 27, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals affirming a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Michael B. Torphy, Jr., Circuit Judge. Originally reported in 91 Wis.2d 540, 283 N.W.2d 460.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for the crime of delivering a controlled substance. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in answering questions posed by the jury in the absence of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his live-in accomplice were convicted of delivering a controlled substance to an undercover police officer. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in answering questions posed by the jury in the absence of counsel and that he was denied his right to a unanimous verdict. The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals, holding that although counsel should have been given an opportunity to respond to the jury's question, it was not reversible error because defendant was not prejudice as the question was correctly answered by the judge. The court held that defendant's absence at the time the trial court responded was not a violation of his constitutional rights because the question posed by the jury was a question of law and defendant's right to a fair and just trial was not thwarted by the court's answering outside his presence. The court concluded that the trial court did not err in failing to instruct the jury that they must be unanimous in regard to the manner in which defendant participated in the crime of delivering a controlled substance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals, which affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for the crime of delivering a controlled substance.

Wisconsin Asso. of Food Dealers v. Madison


No. 77-699


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


97 Wis. 2d 426; 293 N.W.2d 540; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2627; 14 ERC (BNA) 1803


June 2, 1980, Argued  
June 27, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals affirming an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Michael B. Torphy, Jr., Circuit Judge. Originally reported in 89 Wis.2d 311, 278 N.W.2d 481.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed and cause remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, milk wholesalers, milk retailers, and milk trade associations, appealed the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which refused to enjoin the enforcement of Madison, Wis., Gen. Ordinances § 23.44(2). Previously, a circuit court had refused to enjoin the enforcement of § 23.44(2). Defendants, a city, its director of public health, and its director of consumer protection, opposed petitioners' appeal.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted § 23.44(2), which required milk retailers that used nonrefillable containers to also provide refillable containers to consumers. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 96.02, it was the declared policy of Wisconsin to promote the orderly and efficient marketing of agricultural commodities. The circuit court denied the petitioners' request for a temporary injunction without considering whether Madison Wis., Gen. Ordinances § 23.44(2) infringed on the spirit or policy of Wisconsin legislation, and the appellate court affirmed the circuit court's decision. The court reversed the appellate court's decision, holding that the circuit court was required to consider statewide policy in considering whether a temporary injunction should have issued. The court ruled that the circuit court's failure to consider statewide policy was an improper failure to consider a factor that was relevant to the circuit court's exercise of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Court of Appeals which held that the circuit court properly denied the milk retailers request for a temporary injunction, and the cause was remanded to the circuit court for proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.
