Hunter v. School Dist.


No. 78-045


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


97 Wis. 2d 435; 293 N.W.2d 515; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2630


June 2, 1980, Argued  
June 27, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals reversing a judgment of the Circuit Court for Trempealeau County: Thomas H. Barland, Circuit Judge. Originally reported in 90 Wis.2d 523, 280 N.W.2d 313.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent builder challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which held that Wis. Stat. § 893.155, which was amended effective June 13, 1976, did not bar a claim for negligence filed by co-appellant wife, a claim for loss of consortium filed by co-appellant husband, and a cross-claim for indemnification or contribution filed by appellant school district.


OVERVIEW: The builder completed an addition to a gymnasium in 1960. In November 1975, the wife sustained injuries when a cement block wall partially fell on her as she tried to retrieve a ball lodged in the wall of the gym. Wis. Stat. § 893.155 (1961) did not allow recovery for injuries against a contractor for damages brought more than six years after the construction of the building. The trial court dismissed the complaint and the cross-complaint holding that there was no cause of action against the builder for negligent construction of the school after 1966. In 1975, the court declared § 893.155 (1961) unconstitutional. The legislature replaced it with § 893.155 (1977), that became effective on July 13, 1976. The latter statute had a new statute of limitations. The court affirmed the appeals court's decision. The court held that: (1) the 1961 statute was unconstitutional; it had no effect; (2) the 1977 statute did not bar the causes of action because the wife's claim accrued prior to the effective date of the statute; (3) the husband's claim was derivative; and (4) the amended statute applied only to a claim for contribution based on injuries that occurred after July 13, 1976.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals.

 

310 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Sambs v. Brookfield


No. 78-599


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


97 Wis. 2d 356; 293 N.W.2d 504; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2635


May 5, 1980, Argued  
June 27, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, with Costs, on August 11, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Originally reported in 95 Wis.2d 1, 289 N.W.2d 308.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed; the judgment of the circuit court is reversed; and the cause is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant City of Brookfield, Wisconsin sought review of a decision from the Wisconsin Court of Appeals, which affirmed a judgment from a circuit court awarding damages to plaintiff for injuries he sustained in a car accident for which the City was found 30 percent causally negligent in failing to properly maintain and repair a highway. The City claimed that plaintiff's recovery was properly limited by Wis. Stat. §§ 81.15 and 895.43(2) (1965).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was awarded in excess of $ 900,000 by the circuit court in his personal injury action against the City. The court of appeals affirmed the circuit court's judgment, holding that the $ 25,000 limitation on the recovery of damages arising from highway defects in Wis. Stat. §§ 81.15 and 895.43(2) (1965) violated the equal protection guarantees of the state and federal constitutions. The City sought further review, and the court reversed, holding that plaintiff did not carry his burden of proving that it was arbitrary or invidious for the legislature to limit the amounts recoverable by a victim of a highway defect from a city. The court determined that in enacting Wis. Stat. §§ 81.15 and 895.43, the legislature could have reasoned that a maximum should be imposed on the amount recoverable in those situations where the burden of unlimited liability might have been substantial, and the danger of disrupting the functioning of local government by requiring payment of substantial damage awards might have been great. The court concluded that plaintiff's constitutional guarantee of equal protection was not violated by his recovery against the City being limited to $ 25,000.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decisions of the court of appeals and the circuit court, which were entered in favor of plaintiff in his action against the City to recover damages for injuries he sustained in a car accident. The court remanded the cause to the circuit court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

311 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Amoco Oil Co.


No. 77-065


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


97 Wis. 2d 226; 293 N.W.2d 487; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2638


September 11, 1979, Argued  
June 27, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: George R. Currie, Reserve Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant oil company sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which enjoined appellant from advertising or representing the sale or furnishing of any property or services combined with or conditioned on the purchase of any other property or services without clearly and conspicuously setting forth the total price or amount in such advertisement or representation.


OVERVIEW: Appellee state succeeded in its action to enjoin appellant oil company from continuing its advertising program offering combination sales, allegedly in violation of Wis. Stat. § 100.18(2), which prohibited the selling or furnishing of any property or services combined with or conditioned on the purchase of any other property or services without setting forth the total price to be paid. Upon appeal the court affirmed, holding that advertisements by appellant that did not include the total price of certain combination offers defeated the purpose of Wis. Stat. § 100.18(2), which was to promote full disclosure to the consumer of reliable data, thereby preventing deceptive pricing and facilitating price comparison. The court found that the statute did not conflict with the Federal Trade Commission Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 45 (a)(1), § 57(a) or § 45, because it was not contradictory in the sense of legislative provisions that cannot coexist. The court found that the effect of the state statute on interstate commerce was incidental and not excessive and therefore did not violate the commerce clause. The court held that the statute did not stifle speech so as to violate U.S. Const. amend. I.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision to enjoin appellant oil company from advertising the sale or furnishing of any property or services combined with or conditioned on the purchase of any other property or services without clearly and conspicuously setting forth the total price or amount in such advertisement because the applicable statute was constitutional and its application to appellant's advertisements was within the scope of the statute.

 

312 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Neely v. State


No. 77-499-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


97 Wis. 2d 38; 292 N.W.2d 859; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2612


May 7, 1980, Argued  
June 9, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on July 21, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals affirming a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County: Earl D. Morton, Circuit Judge. Originally reported in 86 Wis.2d 304, 272 N.W.2d 381.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a judgment of a circuit court that convicted defendant of first-degree murder and imposed a sentence of life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and others were charged with the murder of the victim, who had robbed a co-defendant. At trial, defendant took the stand in his own defense. On direct examination, he testified with respect to his actions on the day the murder was committed. He denied any knowledge of the murder plan and claimed his only involvement was that he was in a car that had transported the victim to the place where the murder took place. On cross-examination, defendant refused to answer the prosecutor's questions on the ground that his answers might tend to incriminate him and persisted in his refusal even after the circuit court ordered him to answer. The court held that: (1) the circuit court correctly ruled the defendant had no right to invoke the Fifth Amendment and avoid responses because the questions propounded during cross-examination concerned matters within the letter and the spirit of the waiver rule; and (2) the court of appeals' creation of a use immunity was incorrect because use immunity was unnecessary and inappropriate where defendant, by taking the stand, waived his privilege against self-incrimination as to the testimony he gave.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court which affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

313 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Princess Cinema of Milwaukee, Inc.


Nos. 78-472-CR, 78-473-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


96 Wis. 2d 646; 292 N.W.2d 807; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2599; 6 Media L. Rep. 1458


May 6, 1980, Argued  
June 3, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals affirming in part and reversing in part a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Marvin C. Holz, Circuit Judge. Originally reported in 90 Wis.2d 543, 280 N.W.2d 323.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals affirming the judgment of conviction on the seventeen counts is reversed, and that part of the decision vacating the judgment on the remaining three counts and remanding to the circuit court is vacated and the complaints are dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered a plea of no contest to each of 20 counts of violating an obscenity statute, Wis. Stat. § 944.21(1)(a), and a judgment of conviction was entered. Defendant's motion to suppress, which asserted that § 944.21(1)(a) was unconstitutional on its face, had previously been denied. The Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), affirmed the judgment of conviction on 17 of the counts and vacated the remaining 3 counts. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant owned an operated a motion picture theater from which 20 motion pictures were seized pursuant to a search warrant. Defendant argued that the unconstitutionality of § 944.21(1)(a) automatically rendered the search and seizure unlawful. The court held that a later determination that a statute was unconstitutional did not render a search and seizure thereunder unlawful. In considering the constitutionality of § 944.21(1)(a), the court applied the three-pronged Miller v. California; the third prong of which considered whether the work, taken as a whole, lacked serious literary, artistic, political, or scientific value. The court had previously held that § 944.21(1)(a) was facially vague and overbroad, but saved it by interpreting the third prong to apply a community standard. That previous holding was clearly erroneous. The third prong required the application of an objective standard, and the application of a community standard introduced subjectivity, thereby providing no clear guidance as to the nature of acts that were subject to punishment. The court refused to judicially modify § 944.21(1)(a), leaving it to the legislature to propose regulatory schemes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court of appeals that affirmed the judgment of conviction as to 17 of the counts. The court also vacated the judgment of the lower court of appeals that vacated the judgment convicting defendant on the remaining 3 counts and remanding to the circuit court, and dismissed the complaints.

 

314 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Milwaukee v. Wilson


No. 77-670


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


96 Wis. 2d 11; 291 N.W.2d 452; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2564


March 31, 1980, Argued  
May 6, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Originally reported in 88 Wis.2d 763, 277 N.W.2d 332.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals affirming the judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a circuit court's judgment affirming a county court's judgment convicting her of loitering with intent to solicit for prostitution contrary to Milwaukee, Wis., Mun. Code § 106.31(1)(g).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged her conviction under Milwaukee, Wis., Mun. Code § 106.31(1)(g) as being unconstitutionally vague and overbroad, and that the evidence at trial was insufficient to sustain the county court's finding that defendant had violated § 106.31(1)(g). The court held that § 106.31(1)(g) represented a constitutionally permissible exercise of the city's police power. The court found that the ordinance was directed only to loitering in a manner and under such a circumstance that manifested an intent to induce, entice, solicit, or procure another to commit an act of prostitution. The court concluded that the ordinance's language sufficiently defined the conduct which the city sought to proscribe such that one inclined to obey the ordinance would have been able to understand what was and was not allowed. The court held that the city was required and did prove its case by clear, satisfactory, and convincing evidence. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction where she was observed on a street corner early in the morning in an area known to have a high rate of prostitution, stopping male pedestrians as they were walking by.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for loitering with intent to solicit for prostitution.

 

315 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Rod v. Farrell


No. 77-681


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


96 Wis. 2d 349; 291 N.W.2d 568; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2566


March 4, 1980, Argued  
May 6, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, with Costs, on June 9, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Originally reported in 86 Wis.2d 760, 273 N.W.2d 386.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former patient sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which, in the patient's medical malpractice claim against defendant physician, reversed a trial court's denial of the physician's motion for summary judgment because the statute of limitations had run.


OVERVIEW: When the patient was four, the physician performed surgery on him to repair a congenital hernia. At the time, apparently no one had any knowledge of any problems with the operation. Twenty years later, the patient underwent exploratory surgery in an attempt to discover the cause of his wife's failure to become pregnant. The operation revealed that portions of his vasa had been surgically removed and he was permanently sterile. The next year, he brought a medical malpractice action against the physician. The trial court denied the physician's motion for summary judgment. The appellate court reversed, concluding that the statute of limitations began to run from the time the act occurred and the injury resulted, not from the date of discovery of the injury. On further appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that while it believed that the three-year limitations period of Wis. Stat. § 893.205 was too short, and that injustice might result from the commencing of the period before a right of action was discovered, it was a matter for the legislature, which had not changed the statute despite the introduction of several bills. The court found no violation of Wis. Const. art. I, § 9.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's reversal of the trial court's denial of summary judgment to the physician in the patient's medical malpractice action.

 

316 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Albright


No. 77-014-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


96 Wis. 2d 122; 291 N.W.2d 487; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2577


September 12, 1979, Argued  
May 6, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the County Court of Waupaca County: A. Don Zwickey, County Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the County Court of Waupaca County (Wisconsin), which dismissed defendant's motion requesting a new trial or release from custody and discharge pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (1976). Defendant claimed that her right to testify, as guaranteed by the United States and Wisconsin Constitutions, was denied during her trial for contributing to the delinquency of a child and for conspiracy to commit burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant also claimed that her attorney's failure to permit defendant to testify constituted ineffective assistance of counsel. On appeal, the court disagreed and affirmed the dismissal of defendant's motion. The court first held that the right to testify was a part of the due process rights afforded to criminal defendants under the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution, such that every criminal defendant was privileged to testify or to refuse to do so. However, that right was not among those fundamental rights that could only be waived in open court on the record by the defendant. Rather, when a defendant accepted counsel to conduct her defense, the exercise or waiver of the right to testify was a decision that was delegated to defense counsel, subject to a defendant's ability to assert that right independent of counsel's advice. In the case at bar, the record revealed that defendant accepted representation and acquiesced to her attorney's decision not to put her on the stand, and that she raised no objection to that decision before the trial court. Consequently, defendant was deemed to have waived her right to testify, and her motion was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying defendant's post-conviction motion.

 

317 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


John v. State


No. 78-596-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


96 Wis. 2d 183; 291 N.W.2d 502; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2581


March 3, 1980, Argued  
May 6, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Originally reported in 89 Wis.2d 214, 278 N.W.2d 235.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) that affirmed her conviction for welfare fraud in violation of Wis. Stat. § 49.12(1) and (9) (1977).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was receiving welfare benefits, but failed to report a change in circumstances that affected her eligibility for such benefits. Defendant was convicted of welfare fraud, and the intermediate appellate court affirmed. Defendant sought review, and the court affirmed. The court held that the statute of limitations requiring felony prosecutions to be commenced within six years after the commission of the offense, § 939.74(1), did not bar defendant's conviction. Defendant did not commit an offense until she failed to report the change in circumstances after seven days from the occurrence of the change. Any benefits received thereafter were the result of defendant's fraud and were to be computed in the determination of the penalty. Therefore, all of the benefits received after the seven-day period constituted part of the fraud, which occurred through years at least until a year before defendant's prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for welfare fraud.

State ex rel. Terry v. Percy


No. 75-503


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


95 Wis. 2d 476; 290 N.W.2d 713; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2536


February 7, 1980, Argued  
April 8, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Remand from the United States Supreme Court. By the Court: State ex rel. Terry v. Percy, 84 Wis.2d 693, 267 N.W.2d 380 (1978), is modified and, as modified, the decision is reinstated. Originally reported in 74 Wis.2d 487, 247 N.W.2d 109 and 84 Wis.2d 693, 267 N.W.2d 380.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the United States Supreme Court, appellant prisoner commenced a habeas corpus proceeding, alleging that he did not suffer from any mental aberrations due to sexual psychopathy and that continuation of his confinement was a violation of his rights.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of two counts of rape and one count of theft. Pursuant to the recommendation of respondent, Department of Health and Social Services, that the prisoner was in need of specialized treatment as a sex deviate, the trial court ordered him committed to the department under Wis. Stat. § 975.06. Pursuant to § 975.11, a person committed was to be discharged when the department opined that there was reasonable probability that he could be given full liberty without danger to the public. The court held that it was not necessary that a formal adversary hearing took place in order to determine whether the commitment should be continued. The court set forth the minimum due process requirements for a reexamination of sex crimes commitment and further held that the decision of the department based upon such examination was reviewable by the committing court upon writ of certiorari.


OUTCOME: The court modified its decision and reinstated it as modified.

State ex rel. First Nat'l Bank v. M & I Peoples Bank


No. 77-515


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


95 Wis. 2d 303; 290 N.W.2d 321; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2517


January 8, 1980, Argued  
April 1, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, with Costs, on May 13, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Wood County: James H. Levi, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff banks sought review of a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Wood County (Wisconsin). The trial court denied plaintiffs' request for injunctive relief and dismissed their complaint in quo warranto and, additionally, for a declaratory judgment on its merits in connection with defendant bank's desire to establish a new branch.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed an application with the Commissioner of Banking, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 221.04(1)(j)1, for permission to establish a new branch bank facility. A report recommended that the application for the branch be granted. The Commissioner and the Banking Review Board (Board) approved defendant's application. Plaintiffs were not notified of the application, the investigation, or the application's approval. Plaintiffs commenced an action in quo warranto pursuant to § 294.04, seeking a determination that defendant's franchise was null and void. As a second cause of action, plaintiffs requested a declaratory judgment pursuant to § 269.56, adjudicating the rights of the parties and interpreting the statute under which defendant's application for a branch bank was granted. The court ruled that an injury had been shown, but found that plaintiffs lacked standing. The court concluded plaintiffs possessed no property right to engage in the banking business free of competitors. Therefore, plaintiffs did not have standing to assert the alleged constitutional infirmity of § 221.04(1)(j)1.


OUTCOME: The judgment and the order were affirmed.

Jessen v. State


No. 78-054-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


95 Wis. 2d 207; 290 N.W.2d 685; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2518


March 5, 1980, Argued  
April 1, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Originally reported in 87 Wis.2d 916, 274 N.W.2d 906.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which summarily affirmed an order of the circuit court which denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.06.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was a former chief deputy sheriff, was charged with 26 six counts of misconduct in public office (falsification of uniform traffic citations), in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.12(4). Defendant's sentence was stayed, and he was placed on probation. After defendant was discharged from probation, he filed a motion for postconviction relief under Wis. Stat. § 974.06, contending that he had been denied due process of law as a result of the unconstitutional suppression of evidence by the State. Certain evidence that inculpated the then sheriff was never made available to defendant prior to trial. The trial court denied defendant's motion. The court of appeals summarily affirmed the denial of the motion. The court affirmed, holding that being in custody was a jurisdictional requirement for a court to entertain a Wis. Stat. § 974.06 motion. Defendant had an available remedy in the form of a writ of coram nobis, which was not abolished by the repeal of a statutory enactment of the common law writ.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion for postconviction relief.

 

321 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Mulder v. Acme-Cleveland Corp.


No. 77-432


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


95 Wis. 2d 173; 290 N.W.2d 276; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2526


January 8, 1980, Argued  
April 1, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County: Allan J. Deehr, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant and third party plaintiff manufacturer sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County, Wisconsin, which dismissed the manufacturer's action against third party defendant employer based upon statutory immunity pursuant to Wisc. Stat. § 102.03(2).


OVERVIEW: After the employee was injured on the job, he obtained an award of compensation under the Wisconsin worker's compensation law. The employee then filed a negligence action against the manufacturers of the equipment which caused his injuries. The manufacturers sought to join the employer as a defendant and potentially-negligent party to the action. The circuit court granted the employer's motion to dismiss. On review, the court affirmed. The court noted that although Wisc. Stat. § 102.03(2) made it clear that an injured employee could only recover worker's compensation payments against his employer, the employee was also permitted to maintain a tort action against any third party whose negligence caused or contributed to the injury pursuant to Wisc. Stat. § 102.29(1). However, Wisc. Stat. § 102.03(2) denied any remedy to that third party tortfeasor against the employer, because the worker's compensation statute made the payment of worker's compensation the employer's exclusive liability for work-related injuries. The court found that this provision was not unconstitutional or unduly harsh, but performed a valid societal purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court dismissing the action against the employer.

Fine v. Elections Board of Wisconsin


No. 79-074


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


95 Wis. 2d 162; 289 N.W.2d 823; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2529


March 3, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
April 1, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Originally reported in 91 Wis.2d 849, 284 N.W.2d 121.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, State Elections Board, sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a trial court decision which granted respondent, election candidate, request to have his full name printed on an election ballot.


OVERVIEW: The candidate was an attorney who ran for a circuit court judgeship position. The candidate sought to have his entire name appear on the ballot because he always used his entire name in his other endeavors, such as his law practice, books and articles, along with a television show. The Elections Board denied the candidate's request based on its policy of not allowing a candidate to display his or her entire name. The candidate sought judicial review. The trial court ordered that the candidate should be able to have his entire name displayed, ruling that there was no legitimate state purpose that would be furthered by such a policy. The Elections Board sought review. The court of appeals affirmed the trial court's order on other grounds. The court affirmed holding that under Wis. Stat. § 7.08(2)(a), the use of initials in place of a candidate's full first and middle names was optional, not mandatory. The Election Board's rationale of preserving space on its election ballots was not a justified state interest. The court had appellate jurisdiction because the matter involved questions of public interest even though it had become moot as to the particular parties involved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the candidate's request to have his full name printed on an election ballot.

 

323 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Crowley v. Knapp


No. 76-398


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


94 Wis. 2d 421; 288 N.W.2d 815; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2492


September 10, 1979, Argued  
March 4, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Crawford County: Richard W. Orton, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed, and cause remanded with directions to dissolve the injunction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant group home owners sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Crawford County (Wisconsin), which enjoined appellants from using their property as a group home on the grounds that it violated restrictive covenants in their deed. The trial court held that respondent neighboring property owners had the right to enforce the covenants, which were contained in a deed from a common grantor.


OVERVIEW: Appellant group home owners turned property they had purchased into a home for retarded adults. Respondent neighboring property owners brought an action to enjoin that use of the property, contending that it violated the restrictive covenants in appellants' deed. The trial court found for respondents and appellants sought review. The court reversed. The court found, first, that respondents could have enforced the covenants because there was evidence that showed that the original grantor inserted the covenants in the deed in order to carry out a general plan or scheme of development. However, the court held that the trial court erred when it concluded that appellants had violated two particular covenants. First, the court held that appellants did not violate the covenant that prohibited the use of garages or outbuildings as residential units because appellants had not, as a matter of fact, engaged in such a use. Second, the court found that the trial court erroneously narrowed the covenant restricting the use to a "single family dwelling" to have meant use by blood relatives because there was no indication in the deed that the grantor intended to impose such a limitation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order that enjoined appellant group home owners from using their property as a group home. The court held that while respondent neighboring property holders had the right to enforce covenants contained in a deed from a common grantor, the restrictive covenants contained in appellants' deed had not been violated.

 

324 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ehlenfeldt


No. 77-306-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


94 Wis. 2d 347; 288 N.W.2d 786; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2493


January 9, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
March 4, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County: Jerold F. Murphy, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin) convicting him of two counts of aiding and abetting the violation of Wis. Stat. § 95.28(1), which prohibited the dismemberment or storage of meat from a diseased animal at premises where other food was sold or prepared for sale. The issues were whether Wis. Stat. § 95.28(1) was unconstitutionally vague and whether the evidence supported the verdicts.


OVERVIEW: Defendant instructed one of his employees to deliver two cows he had purchased at an auction to a meat market and slaughter plant. Despite that fact that the cows could not get up, defendant's employee delivered the two cows to the market. The market employee testified that the meat was subsequently sold over the counter at the market. Defendant subsequently bought a black steer at an auction. Defendant's employee testified that the steer was also sick. Defendant slit the steer's throat on his farm and the animal was taken to the market. The court held that the word "diseased" in § 95.28(1) was not so difficult that person of ordinary intelligence would have been unaware of its meaning. The evidence supported the conviction under count two involving the delivery of the black steer to the market. That the animal was diseased was apparent from the testimony of defendant's employee and a veterinarian who examined the steer. As to the delivery of the two cows, the State was required to prove that the disease from which they were suffering was one that would have ordinarily rendered their meat unfit. There was no evidence that defendant knew that the meat would have been unwholesome.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the judgment of conviction as to count one and as to that count dismissed the information. The court affirmed the judgment as to count two convicting defendant of aiding and abetting the violation of a statute that prohibited the dismemberment or storage of meat from a diseased animal at premises where other food was sold or prepared for sale.

 

325 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Meier v. Purdun


No. 77-195


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


94 Wis. 2d 558; 288 N.W.2d 839; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2504


October 10, 1979, Submitted on Briefs  
March 4, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County: Thomas H. Barland, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, cognovit promissory note makers, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County (Wisconsin) granted to plaintiff note holder based on a judgment of confession under Wis. Stat. § 270.69 (1961) and the order denying their motion to vacate the cognovit judgment under Wis. Stat. § 296.46 (1961) on the ground that Wis. Stat. § 270.69 (1961) unconstitutionally deprived them of notice and an opportunity to be heard.


OVERVIEW: The holder took a judgment by confession on the cognovit promissory note. Over 10 years later, his motion for leave to sue on the judgment was granted under Wis. Stat. § 270.95 (1971) without prior notice to the makers. On appeal from that judgment, the court held that the holder's showing of non-payment and the expiration of the creditor's 10-year lien right under Wis. Stat. § 270.79 (1971) constituted good cause for the trial court to allow an action on the unsatisfied judgment. The court noted that the makers had testified that they knew of the judgment and had attempted to settle the matter, but that no payments had been made. The holder then filed the present action seeking a new judgment based on the cognovit judgment. The makers filed an answer, but their defense were stricken. The court held that a cognovit note did not per se violate the Fourteenth Amendment. Though Wis. Stat. § 269.46 (1961) was liberally construed so as to allow the setting aside of cognovit judgments, the makers failed to bring an action to set aside within one year as required by § 269.46. The time lapse between their knowledge of the judgment and their attempted assertion of defenses was too great.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

326 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Castelaz v. Milwaukee


No. 77-346


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


94 Wis. 2d 513; 289 N.W.2d 259; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2507


December 3, 1979, Argued  
March 4, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Ralph J. Podell, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee brought an action for reinstatement, back pay, and restoration against defendants, a city, its Board of City Service Commissioners, and 10 officials, alleging violations of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, civil rights laws, and the Fair Employment Act. He sought damages from the 10 officials for civil conspiracy. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) granted defendants' motion for summary judgment. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee alleged that he was laid off or transferred without a hearing due to his frequent and public criticism of a model city program and that defendants failed to comply with the required procedures of Milwaukee, Wis., City Service Rule X (Rule X). Defendants argued that Milwaukee, Wis., City Service Rule XII (Rule XII) was controlling. The court held that the employee failed to exhaust administrative remedies. A Rule X hearing was preliminary to a Rule XII hearing, and the inquiry was more limited, being restricted to questions of necessity of the layoff and whether it was good for the civil service. The employee's appeal was an inquiry as to why others were not laid off instead of him. Because no formal written demand for relief was filed under Rule XII, defendant Board was not required to conduct a investigation and hearing as to the reason for the employee's layoff or into the claimed violation of his reinstatement rights. Because no Rule XII demand was filed, the employee was not entitled to a hearing or to a writ of mandamus to compel compliance with Rule XII. The employee was required to exhaust his Rule XII remedies prior to filing his 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to defendants in the employee's action against them alleging civil conspiracy and constitutional, state statutory, and city civil service rule violations.

 

327 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


County of Columbia v. Bylewski


No. 77-125


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


94 Wis. 2d 153; 288 N.W.2d 129; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2463


January 7, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
February 7, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Columbia County: Howard Latton, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed in part; affirmed in part and cause remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. No appeal costs to be taxed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion for reversal of a county court's decision in favor of respondent county's small claims actions alleging that he violated Columbia County, Wisconsin, Code §§ 11.07, 11.13-3(a), by replacing a mobile home and building a garage without a permit. The owner claimed that the home replaced an unusable structure.


OVERVIEW: The landowner purchased the land with an old mobile home on it; that home was a nonconforming use under the Columbia County, Wisconsin, Code. After the landowner replaced it and built the garage, valued at over $ 250, the county court found him guilty of violating Columbia County, Wisconsin, Code §§ 11.07, 11.13-3(a), but declined to impose a forfeiture, instead ordering him to remove both structures. On review, the circuit court affirmed and denied the landowner's request for reversal or a new trial. On further review, the court found that zoning could be enforced by such a civil action, that the county court did not have the authority to issue injunctions in small claims matters pursuant to Wis. Stat. ch. 299, and that it was error to order the owner to remove the structures. The court found that the mobile home was not a "building" as defined in the Columbia County, Wisconsin, Code but was a "trailer," that there was no error in finding that the new home was not an extension of the prior nonconforming use, and there was no error in finding that the owner violated the code by building the garage. The court reversed in part, affirmed in part, and remanded the action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's affirmance of the injunction ordering the owner to remove the mobile home and the garage. The court affirmed the decision that the owner violated the zoning code by replacing the mobile home and building the garage without a permit. The court remanded the action for further proceedings.

 

328 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Sears v. State


No. 77-308-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


94 Wis. 2d 128; 287 N.W.2d 785; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2465


December 4, 1979, Argued  
February 7, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Error to review a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Victor Manian, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant obtained a writ of error to review a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of solicitation to commit an act of sexual perversion, Wis. Stat. §§ 939.30 and 944.17(1), and which sentenced him to an indeterminate term not to exceed two years. Defendant, while dressed in women's clothing, approached a male undercover police officer and offered to perform a sex act in exchange for $ 20.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed his prosecution for solicitation of sexual perversion rather than disorderly conduct denied him equal protection. The court affirmed his conviction. The conscious exercise of some selectivity in enforcement was not in itself a federal constitutional violation so long as the selection was not deliberately based upon an unjustifiable standard such as race, religion, or other arbitrary classification. Here, there was no evidence that defendant's prosecution was based on personal vindictiveness or a desire to prevent the exercise of constitutional rights. At the trial court's evidentiary hearing on defendant's claim, the deputy district attorney and the assistant district attorney testified concerning the factors that led them to charge defendant as they did. They testified that his recidivism required a more substantial charge and that they desired to maintain consistency between the charges brought against patrons arrested by undercover policewomen and the charges brought against prostitutes arrested by undercover policemen. There was also no evidence to support defendant's assertion that females had not been charged with solicitation to commit sexual perversion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

329 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. La Follette v. Democratic Party of United States


No. 79-1328-OA


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


93 Wis. 2d 473; 287 N.W.2d 519; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2412


November 19, 1979, Argued  
January 19, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Action for declaratory judgment and injunction commenced in this Court pursuant to leave granted.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- It is adjudged and declared that the Wisconsin electoral statutes involved in this controversy are constitutional, in full force and effect and binding on the petitioner and respondents; that the presidential preference primary shall be conducted in accordance with the Wisconsin statutes; and that Wisconsin delegates to the Democratic Party national convention shall be apportioned as required by statute in accordance with the results of the presidential preference vote and are not disqualified as delegates solely by reason of the apportionment being determined as required by the Wisconsin statutes.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Attorney General of Wisconsin filed an original action for declaratory and injunctive relief on behalf of the State of Wisconsin. Respondents, the Democratic Party of the United States, the Democratic National Committee, and Democratic Party of Wisconsin, joined the Attorney General in asking the court to determine the parties' rights with regard to Wisconsin's open presidential preference primary law.


OVERVIEW: Wisconsin's presidential preference primary was an open primary in which voters did not have to publicly state a preference for a particular party to vote in that party's primary. The Democratic Party objected to the procedure and stated that it would refuse to recognize Wisconsin delegates to the national convention because they were chosen in violation of Rule 2 of Delegation Selection Rules for the 1980 Convention. The sole function of the Wisconsin presidential preference primary was to apportion the number of delegates among the presidential candidates on the ballot for a specific party. The court determined that the Wisconsin law was constitutional and in full force and effect and that it was binding on the parties. The presidential preference primary was conducted in accordance with Wisconsin law. Wisconsin delegates to the Democratic Party national convention were apportioned as required by statute and the results of the preference vote and were not disqualified by reason of the apportionment having been determined by Wisconsin law.


OUTCOME: The court declared that Wisconsin's open primary law for presidential preference primaries was constitutional and was binding on the parties.

 

330 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Sigma Tau Gamma Fraternity House Corp. v. Menomonie


No. 79-440


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


93 Wis. 2d 392; 288 N.W.2d 85; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2408


December 3, 1979, Argued  
January 15, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dunn County: John G. Bartholomew, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion. No appeal costs to be taxed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to challenge defendant city's condemnation of a fraternity house under the tax increment law, Wis. Stat. § 66.46, plaintiff fraternity sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Dunn County (Wisconsin), which rendered judgment in favor of the city.


OVERVIEW: The fraternity's house, which was maintained, was located in a blighted area. The city sought to condemn the house under the Tax Increment Law, Wis. Stat. § 66.46(3), so that it could create a tax increment financing district to fiance the redevelopment of the area. As part of the redevelopment, the fraternity property would be conveyed to a private developer. The fraternity filed action and contended that the condemnation was improper, that the Tax Increment Law did not authorize condemnation, and that the law was unconstitutional. The trial court rendered judgment in favor of the city, and the fraternity sought review. The court reversed in part. It found that while it was constitutional for the city to condemn property and reconvey the property to a private developer for the public purpose of redevelopment, the city was not authorized to initiate condemnation through the Tax Increment Law. The law provided for the establishment of tax increment financing districts for public improvements but not condemnation. Condemnation proceedings were available under the condemnation statutes. The court also affirmed the constitutionality of the Tax Increment Law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial decision rendered in favor of the city and found that the city erred when it sought condemnation under the tax increment law because the statute did not provide for condemnation.

Fiala v. Voight


No. 77-266


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


93 Wis. 2d 337; 286 N.W.2d 824; 1980 Wisc. LEXIS 2398


December 3, 1979, Argued  
January 8, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Kewaunee County: Donald W. Gleason, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State and game wardens, appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Kewaunee County (Wisconsin), which overruled their demurrer to a complaint filed by plaintiff fish market that alleged the wardens unlawfully seized several boxes of trout and whitefish from its truck.


OVERVIEW: A shipment of fish was being transported from a fishery to the fish market for sale. Wardens stopped the truck and inspected the shipment, then seized it based on the facts that there was no identification as to the type of fish, the number of pounds of fish, or the consignor and destination, and that the invoice for the fish did not conform to the quantity and type of fish contained in the truck. The market filed an action against defendants for wrongful conversion, alleging, inter alia, that the State was negligent in its supervision of the wardens. Defendants demurred, alleging that the trial court lacked jurisdiction based on the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The trial court overruled the demurrer and held that the State could be sued as indemnitor of its employees under Wis. Stat. § 270.58, and defendants appealed. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the trial court erred in denying the State's demurrer because it lacked personal jurisdiction over the State. The State was entitled to the protection of the sovereign immunity doctrine and could not be joined as a party in the absence of its consent to be sued, and it did not consent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded a decision denying the State's demurrer to a complaint against it.

State v. Karpinski


No. 76-586-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


92 Wis. 2d 599; 285 N.W.2d 729; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 2203


October 9, 1979, Argued  
December 4, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County: Clair Voss, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant who had been charged with the criminal offense of possession of a controlled substance appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which reversed the decision of a lower court dismissing the complaint against him, citing the fact that defendant's conduct could have been prosecuted by a city as a civil ordinance violation.


OVERVIEW: The district attorney charged defendant with the misdemeanor criminal offense of possession of controlled substances. In the city in which the offense had been committed, the offense was also a civil violation, and the city ordinance referred to the language of the state criminal statute. The county court dismissed the charge against defendant, holding that the city ordinance was invalid and unconstitutional and that by authorizing the municipality to prohibit conduct already prohibited by the State criminal statutes, the State was involved in the practice of denying constitutional guarantees. The State appealed, and the intermediate court reversed, reinstating the complaint. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed the intermediate court's decision. The court held that the existence of the two statutes penalizing identical conduct did not give the district attorney unbridled discretion in charging criminal offenses. The court further held that the district attorney's discretion to file charges, not file charges, or refer the case to the city attorney completely fell within the proper bounds of prosecutorial discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order reinstating the complaint against defendant.

Nufer v. Village Board of Palmyra


No. 77-064


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


92 Wis. 2d 289; 284 N.W.2d 649; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 2174


October 10, 1979, Submitted on Briefs  
November 6, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County: Henry G. Gergen, Jr., Circuit Judge of the Thirteenth Circuit, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of respondent village board removing the employee from his position as village police chief.


OVERVIEW: The employee had been the village police chief for over 10 years when charges against him were referred to the village board. The charges concerned the employee's improper job performance. After conducting a hearing, the village board removed the employee from his position, and the employee appealed the decision to the circuit court, which affirmed the village board's decision. On appeal, the employee argued that the proceedings against him implicated a liberty interest that entitled him to due process. The court affirmed, however, because none of the charges against the employee allege him to be immoral or dishonest in the manner he operated his office, nor did they accuse him of conduct comparable to charges of disloyalty, communism, subversive activities, or alcoholism. Accordingly, the village board's action did not damage the employee's standing and associations in the community to the degree necessary to implicate a liberty interest in his reputation. The charges neither effectively foreclosed future employment nor stigmatized or injured the employee's reputation. Because no liberty interest was involved, the procedural guarantees of the Due Process Clause did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that affirmed the village board's removal of the employee from his position as village police chief.

Howell Plaza, Inc. v. State Highway Com.


No. 76-545


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


92 Wis. 2d 74; 284 N.W.2d 887; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 2179


October 10, 1979, Submitted on Briefs

DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owner appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted judgment in favor of respondent State Highway Commission in the owner's inverse condemnation action under Wis. Stat. § 32.10 and Wis. Const. art. I, § 13.


OVERVIEW: After learning that the path of a freeway was to pass through the undeveloped portion of the owner's property, taking about 16 acres therefrom, he requested that the Commission purchase the 16-acre tract under its early acquisition procedures. Several letters from the Commission advised the owner that engineering had progressed to the point where acquisition would have been possible. A few years later, the owner was informed that all efforts to purchase the property had been terminated as a result of government investigation into the legality of the Commission's early acquisition procedures. The owner contended that the Commission had so acted as to deprive it of substantially all of the beneficial use of its property, and that as a result of the activities of the Commission, he was unable to develop the land. The court held that the owner's land was not taken or occupied within the meaning of Wis. Const. art. I, § 13 or Wis. Stat. § 32.10. The court found that the owner could have developed the property if he had desired to do so but voluntarily chose not to. The court found that the owner made no attempt to develop the land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the Commission in the owner's inverse condemnation action.

Madison General Hospital Asso. v. Madison


No. 77-152


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


92 Wis. 2d 125; 284 N.W.2d 603; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 2182


October 10, 1979, Submitted on Briefs  
November 6, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: William C. Sachtjen, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County, which held that equipment leased by appellee non-profit hospital was also exempt from the state property tax pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 70.11(4m). The city argued that the particular lease agreement was not entitled to the exemption and that the exemption was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In a prior appeal the non-profit hospital established that the tax-exemption provided under Wis. Stat. § 70.11(4m) applied to all personal property that was used exclusively by the hospital, including leased equipment even if the lessor earned a profit. The city then argued that property provided by one particular lessor was not entitled to the exemption because its pricing schedule was the same nationwide regardless of any local tax exemptions and that, thus, it was the lessor and not the hospital that enjoyed the exemption's benefit. This, the city argued, was unconstitutional. The court held that the legislature's intent was to give non-profit public hospitals a competitive edge with profit hospitals. This was a legitimate public purpose. Thus, the exemption was "reasonable" under Wis. Const. art VIII, § 1. By holding that leased hospital property, whether for profit or not, was not taxable, the cost of the tax was not passed on to the public. In the instant case, that the benefit could be less immediate or direct or could be more immediately beneficial to the lessor, was not enough to overcome beyond a reasonable doubt the legal presumption of the statute's constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court upholding the constitutionality of the personal property tax exemption for the non-profit hospital despite the unusual short-term benefit to the particular lessor of hospital equipment was affirmed by the court.

Bonneville Estate v. Wisconsin Dep't of Revenue


No. 77-003


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


91 Wis. 2d 726; 284 N.W.2d 52; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 2155


September 12, 1979, Submitted on Briefs  
October 9, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County: Gordon Myse, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant estate sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of the Tax Appeals Commission that held that Wis. Stat. § 71.09(7)(b), governing the homestead exemption, was constitutional. The estate asserted that the statute violated equal protection guarantees.


OVERVIEW: Section 71.09(7)(b) required that a claim for a homestead tax credit must claim be filed during the lifetime of the claimant and that death extinguishes the right to file for homestead credit. The estate's attempt to claim a homestead credit after the death of the decedent was denied by the state. The circuit court affirmed the decision that the statute was constitutional. The court rejected the estate's claim that the statutory provision limiting homestead credit to a claimant who files before her death constituted an unreasonable and arbitrary classification which violated the constitutional guarantee of equal protection. The court explained that the purpose of the statute was not to reimburse a member of the claimant's household or the claimant's estate for the expenses incurred in the prior year, but was clearly intended to grant relief to a claimant. The court concluded that the classification, limiting the exemption to a claimant who lived beyond the tax year during which the expenses qualifying for homestead credit were incurred, was rational and was convenient for purposes of administration of the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that upheld the constitutionality of the statute.

Lepley v. State


No. 77-091-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


90 Wis. 2d 369; 280 N.W.2d 124; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 2088


May 2, 1979, Argued  
June 29, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Error to review an order of the Circuit Court for Ashland County: Lewis J. Charles, Reserve Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Ashland County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to withdraw his guilty plea for first-degree murder and for a new trial. Defendant contended that the trial court's inquiry was insufficient to determine his competency.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to first-degree murder when he was 16-years-old, and he was sentenced to life in prison. Subsequently, defendant filed a motion for postconviction relief claiming that the trial court had failed to conduct an appropriate inquiry to determine whether he was competent. Defendant's motion to withdraw the guilty and for a new trial was denied. The court affirmed. Specifically, the court held that the trial court conducted a sufficient inquiry to determine the defendant's competency once the issue was brought to its attention. The trial court made specific inquiries of defendant to determine the extent of his education and general comprehension, it questioned defendant regarding his education, it considered psychometric examinations and psychiatric evaluations, and it asked defendant whether he agreed with the district attorney's version of the crime. Defendant's responses to the trial court's questioning were lucid and gave no hint of any gross mental deficiency. As such, the trial court properly denied the motion for postconviction relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

Supreme Court of Wisconsin


91 Wis. 2d 103; 280 N.W.2d 757; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 2125; 37 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1134; 20 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P30,115

The Act's constitutionality was not properly before the court.

State ex rel. Wisconsin Health Facilities Authority v. Lindner


No. 77-895-OA


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


91 Wis. 2d 145; 280 N.W.2d 773; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 2129


January 9, 1979, Argued  
June 29, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Action for declaratory judgment.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Chapter 231, Laws of 1973, is valid and constitutional; and respondent is ordered to honor the voucher of the Authority.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Wisconsin Health Facilities Authority, in this original action, sought a declaration that the Authority's operation was constitutional. Respondent Secretary of the Wisconsin Department of Administration had declined to approve a voucher appropriated by the Wisconsin Legislature to fund the functional establishment of the Authority because he concluded Wis. Stat. § 231 (1974) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The principal issue sought to be resolved was whether or not the act creating the Authority violated the Establishment Clause of U.S. Const. amend. I or its state constitutional counter-part, Wis. Const. art. I, § 18. The Authority was created pursuant to 1973 Wis. Laws 304 (the Act) and codified at Wis. Stat. § 231 (1974). The court noted that the Secretary conceded that the Act carried a "wholesome secular purpose" to improve health care delivery by lowering health care costs. The court evaluated the constitutionality of the Act as it applied to what the parties agreed to be the Wisconsin hospital with the greatest religious manifestations. The court concluded that because the hospital was not a pervasively religious institution and because the Act insured against benefiting any significant religious activities within the hospital, the Act did not have the primary effect of advancing religion. The court concluded the Act did not violate the Establishment Clause. The court concluded that under the primary-effect test the aid did not advance religion, instead it flowed to the predominantly secular aspects of health care and was not violative of Wis. Stat. art. I, § 18.


OUTCOME: The court held that the Act creating the Authority was valid and constitutional. The court ordered the Secretary to honor the voucher of the Authority.

 

340 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Elm Park Iowa, Inc. v. Denniston


No. 78-085


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


91 Wis. 2d 227; 280 N.W.2d 262; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 2130



June 29, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Leander J. Foley, Jr., Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: Jurisdiction transferred to the court of appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant moved the court to retain jurisdiction over its appeal of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which was filed on July 28, 1978, four days before the effective date of those portions of Wis. Stat. ch. 752 relating to the jurisdiction of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals and which was subject to transfer to that court in the court's discretion under 1977 Wis. Laws ch. 187, § 131.


OVERVIEW: 1977 Wis. Laws ch. 187, § 131 provided that appeals pending in the court in which the respondent's brief had not been filed as of April 1, 1978, could be transferred to the court of appeals even if it did not have jurisdiction at the time the appeal was taken. However, appellant argued that until August 1, 1978, it had a vested statutory right of appeal to the court, that transferring the appeal to another forum would have violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and that the transfer law was an unconstitutional attempt to delegate legislative power to the court. The court held that: (1) no litigant had a vested right in a particular remedy, so he could have none in rules of procedure that related to the remedy; (2) the statute provided a procedural means for equalizing work load between the newly created court of appeals and the court and did not create a new appeal right; and (3) in making the new appellate structure retroactively applicable to a limited class of cases, the legislature had violated no vested rights and had not violated the separation of powers doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellant's motion to retain jurisdiction and transferred the matter to the court of appeals.

Both parties appealed the trial court's judgment and order. The court affirmed the order, but modified the damage award. The court reasoned that since the insurance policy carried limits exceeding the statutory limitations and included language expressly waiving that defense, plaintiff was entitled to recover for all damages covered by the policy, up to the policy limits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, but modified the award of damages; since the government defendant's insurance policy carried limits exceeding the statutory limitations and included language expressly waiving that defense, plaintiff was entitled to recover for all damages covered by the policy, up to its policy limits.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner department of revenue appealed and respondent corporation cross-appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which in reviewing a decision of the tax appeals commission, set aside some of the commission's findings and conclusions of law. Finally, the court remanded the question of whether the department properly weighted the apportionment formula of § 71.07(2), to the commission for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the trial court's judgment that held that the subsidiary was a unitary business. The court reversed that part of the judgment that rejected the department's interpretation of the statutory situs income exclusion. The court remanded to the commission the question of whether the department properly weighted the cost of manufacturing the cost of manufacturing when applying the statutory apportionment formula.

Holland v. State


No. 77-485-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


91 Wis. 2d 134; 280 N.W.2d 288; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 2128


May 2, 1979, Argued  
June 29, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on August 27, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed and the order vacated; the judgment and order of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which ruled that the trial court committed prejudicial error by improperly instructing the jury that unanimity was required before it could find defendant guilty during a trial in which he was convicted of second-degree murder and party to a crime in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 940.02, 939.05. The State asserted that the court of appeals erred in vacating defendant's conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice entered an apartment shared by two women, where they sexually assaulted both women by force. One woman was severely injured during the incident and died in the hospital a week later from those injuries. Defendant was convicted of second-degree murder, party to a crime, and asserted, on appeal, that the trial court erred in its jury instructions. The court of appeals reversed the conviction, finding that the trial court committed prejudicial error in failing to instruct the jury that before it could find defendant guilty of the crime charged, it had to agree unanimously on which category of the party to a crime statute was violated. The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals and affirmed the trial court's conviction, holding that unanimity was only required with respect to the ultimate issue of guilt or innocence of the crime charged. The court concluded that it was not necessary that the jury agreed on a theory of defendant's participation, so long as they agreed that defendant was in participation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals and affirmed defendant's conviction for second-degree murder, party to a crime.

 

344 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Cresci v. State


No. 76-639-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


89 Wis. 2d 495; 278 N.W.2d 850; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 2039


January 31, 1979, Submitted on Briefs  
May 30, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Error to review an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: John L. Coffey, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a writ of error to review an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to amend the sentence imposed against him following his conviction for robbery.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was out on parole, he was convicted of robbery. The trial court sentenced defendant to an indeterminate term of not more than 10 years, consecutive to the sentences he had been serving when he violated his parole. The following day, the trial court modified the sentence by ordering it to run concurrent. Defendant's parole, however, was not revoked until nearly two months later. Defendant then filed a motion to amend his sentence by reducing the term imposed. Without giving notice to defendant, the trial court held a hearing on the motion and denied it. The court reversed the trial court's order. Because defendant had not been returned to the state prison prior to his sentencing, he was not during that time serving a sentence under the provisions of Wis. Stat. § 973.15(1)(1973). Thus, the trial court was without authority to impose a consecutive sentence. Although the trial court, sua sponte, reduced defendant's sentence, its reason for doing so was not to correct an otherwise illegal sentence. Thus, the trial court's intention was at issue. The trial court's failure to give defendant notice of the hearing was error, and such error was not harmless.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which denied defendant's motion to amend the sentence imposed against him. The case was remanded to the trial court for an evidentiary hearing on the trial court's intention at the time of sentencing.

 

345 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Wisconsin Dep't of Revenue v. Moebius Printing Co.


Nos. 76-766, 76-767


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


89 Wis. 2d 610; 279 N.W.2d 213; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 2068


March 28, 1979, Argued  
May 30, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Case No. 76-766. Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Michael B. Torphy, Jr., Circuit Judge.

Case No. 76-767. Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Michael B. Torphy, Jr., Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Case No. 76-766. Judgment affirmed. Case No. 76-767. Judgment modified and, as modified, affirmed; cause remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Wisconsin Department of Revenue sought review of judgments of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) that reversed that part of a decision and order of the Wisconsin Tax Appeals Commission that upheld the Department's sales tax assessment against respondent taxpayer, and that affirmed that part of the decision and order that held that a sales tax assessment against the taxpayer was barred by a prior field audit by the Department.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a printing and lithographing firm, sold printing materials to its customers in Wisconsin, but accepted certificates of sales tax exemption from customers who stated that the printed materials purchased would be distributed outside of Wisconsin. A tax representative of the Department examined the books and records of the taxpayer for a certain month and found the taxpayer in compliance. The tax representative later issued a letter to the taxpayer that stated the favorable findings. However, a subsequent audit revealed discrepancies. The Department assessed sales taxes against the taxpayer for a period that predated the original audit and letter. The tax appeals commission held that the assessment for the month of the first audit was barred, but upheld the remainder of the assessment. The circuit court reversed the commission and held that the Department could not assess the sales tax. The court found that the exemption from taxation was intended under the use tax and not under the sales tax. However, the court held that the Department was estopped from collecting the sales tax after it issued the letter of compliance to the taxpayer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of a judgment that affirmed that part of the decision and order that held that a sales tax assessment against the taxpayer was barred by a prior field audit by the Department. The court modified that part of the judgment that reversed that part of a decision and order that upheld the Department's sales tax assessment against the taxpayer, and as modified, affirmed and remanded the cause for further proceedings.
