Mast v. Olsen


No. 76-275


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


89 Wis. 2d 12; 278 N.W.2d 205; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 1983


January 9, 1979, Submitted on Briefs  
May 1, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the County Court of Milwaukee County: Terence T. Evans, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order modified and, as modified, affirmed; the cause is remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff creditor brought an action against defendant surety to recover a judgment obtained against the debtor. The County Court of Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) denied the surety's motion to dismiss the complaint and the surety appealed.


OVERVIEW: The surety executed a bond for release of the debtor's property, which had been attached. Under the release bond, the surety agreed to pay the creditor the amount of a judgment not exceeding $ 14,586 which the creditor might recover against the debtor. The creditor obtained an $ 8,473 judgment against the debtor, but the surety refused to pay. The surety sought to dismiss the creditor's complaint on the grounds that Wis. Stat. § 266 (1973), pursuant to which the debtor's property was attached, was unconstitutional. The court held that the trial court correctly denied the motion to dismiss but incorrectly determined that the surety did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of § 266 or was estopped from doing so. The surety had a sufficient economic stake in the outcome to raise such a challenge and the record was insufficient to determine whether the surety was estopped from challenging the attachment procedure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying the surety's motion to dismiss the complaint but modified the trial court's order to allow the surety to raise the issues of the constitutionality of the attachment statute and estoppel in later proceedings.

 

347 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Hilber v. State


Nos. 76-624-CR, 77-391-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


89 Wis. 2d 49; 277 N.W.2d 839; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 1986


January 9, 1979, Submitted on Briefs  
May 1, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 76-624-CR. Error to review a judgment and an order of the County Court of Rock County: Edwin C. Dahlberg, Judge.

No. 77-391-CR. Error to review a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Victor Manian, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgments and orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two juvenile defendants, each of whom were convicted first-degree murder, sought review of judgments and orders of a Circuit Court and a County Court (Wisconsin), which denied their motions to vacate their life sentences, on the ground that the Youthful Offenders Act by its express terms did not apply to persons found guilty of crimes for which the maximum penalty is life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendants contended that Wis. Stat. § 54.03(1) was unconstitutional. The statute provided that youthful offender status could not be granted to a person found guilty of a violation of law for which the maximum penalty provided was life imprisonment. The lower courts sustained the validity of the statute. The court affirmed the judgments. Specifically, the court found that the disparate treatment of juveniles found guilty of crimes carrying a penalty of life imprisonment and juveniles found guilty of other crimes was not unconstitutional because defendants' statutory right to youthful offender treatment was no fundamental. Furthermore, there was a rational basis for enacting the law where the paramount purpose of the statute was to protect members of society. Defendants failed to carry their burden of proving that it was arbitrary or invidious for the legislature to act on the predicate that the public safety and welfare require a person convicted a crime punishable by life imprisonment to be excluded from the Youthful Offenders Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments and orders.

 

348 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hart


No. 76-644-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


89 Wis. 2d 58; 277 N.W.2d 843; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 1987


November 29, 1978, Argued  
May 1, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the County Court of Milwaukee County: Patrick J. Madden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the County Court of Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which, based on Wis. Stat. § 48.17 (1975) (later amended and renumbered), granted a motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction filed by defendant, who was 17 at the time he violated Wis. Stat. §§ 346.67, 343.05, which were crimes as defined by Wis. Stat. § 939.12, and at the time the criminal action was commenced against him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the distinction made in § 48.17 between children over 16 who violated the Motor Vehicle Code (Code) and those children over 16 who were accused of other crimes denied him the equal protection of the laws by depriving him of the protections of the juvenile justice system. On appeal, the court held that, given the need to promote highway safety and to deter dangerous conduct and given the fact that a substantial number of children over 16 drove and caused a significant number of accidents involving death, personal injury, and property damage, the legislature might reasonably have believed that mandatory criminal court jurisdiction, rather than juvenile court jurisdiction, over Code offenses by 16 and 17-year-olds was more likely to deter such children from Code violations. The court held that § 48.17 did not offend the equal protection guarantees of either U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Wis. Const. art. I, § 1. Defendant had not carried his burden of proving it arbitrary or invidious for the legislature to endeavor to promote highway safety by enforcing the provisions of the Code similarly against all persons over 16 who used the highways.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with the opinion.

 

349 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lee


No. 76-243-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


88 Wis. 2d 239; 276 N.W.2d 268; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 1914


January 31, 1979, Argued  
March 27, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County: William E. Crane, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a county court order denying his motion to withdraw a plea of no contest on the ground of manifest injustice. The issues included whether failure to move for withdrawal of the plea within 120 days of conviction, as prescribed by Wis. Stat. § 971.08(2), deprived the county court of jurisdiction to consider the motion.


OVERVIEW: Although the county court did not inform defendant that it was not bound by a plea bargain, during the hearing on the motion to withdraw the plea, defendant's attorney stated that he advised defendant before the plea bargain that a sentence recommendation would not be binding on the county court. On appeal, the court noted that § 971.08(2) reduced from one year to 120 days the time for withdrawing a guilty plea and a motion to withdraw such a plea was directed to the discretion of the trial court in the interest of justice, which the trial court had the inherent power to hear. Section 971.08(2) did not set a jurisdictional time limit for considering a motion to withdraw a plea, but, beyond the 120-day period, unless exceptional circumstances were shown, it would be an abuse of discretion to consider such a motion. Because the State did not object to the untimeliness of the motion, any error was waived. The court held that the county court's conclusion that defendant was fully aware of the possible consequences of his plea was supported by the record and there was no clear and convincing evidence that a manifest injustice resulted from the denial of the motion to withdraw the plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Wisconsin Bingo Supply & Equipment Co. v. Wisconsin Bingo Control Board


No. 76-428


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


88 Wis. 2d 293; 276 N.W.2d 716; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 1924


February 27, 1979, Argued  
March 27, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Michael B. Torphy, Jr., Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed the denial of respondent, the Wisconsin Bingo Control Board, of the corporation's application for a bingo supplier's license.


OVERVIEW: The corporation filed an application for a bingo supplier's license with the Wisconsin Bingo Control Board. The Board denied the application pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 163.27(2) and Wis. Stat. § 163.27(4) on the ground that the vice-president of the corporation and 50 percent shareholder was a gambling promoter. The lower court affirmed the Board's determination, and an appeal was taken. On appeal, the court held that, despite the fact that the term "gambling promoter" was not expressly defined, the reference to Wis. Stat. § 945 and the declaration of legislative intent and purpose contained in Wis. Stat. ch. 163, provided the Board with guidelines to apply the term gambling promoter with sufficient definiteness to satisfy the constitutional requirements of due process. The court further held that there was substantial evidence in the record from which the Board could have made its finding that the vice-president was a gambling promoter in that he or his corporation sold tip tickets, had been fined for the possession of gambling devices and had sold and leased gambling devices for profit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision, which affirmed the denial by the Wisconsin Bingo Control Board of the corporation's application for a bingo supplier's license.

 

351 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Pollnow v. State Dep't of Natural Resources


No. 76-009


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


88 Wis. 2d 350; 276 N.W.2d 738; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 1929


November 27, 1978, Argued  
March 27, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on May 15, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Oneida County: Ronald D. Keberle, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order reversed and cause remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Oneida County (Wisconsin), which determined that defendant state had a fee simple absolute in a disputed parcel of land and denied the landowners' motion for relief.


OVERVIEW: The landowners bought a parcel of land. A right of way, which ran across the land, was maintained by the railroad. The state bought the right of way by quitclaim deed. The landowners blocked the right of way with a fence. The questions on appeal were: (1) was the railroad granted a right of way across the plaintiffs' land by the Railroad Right Of Way Act of 1875? (2) Did the railroad acquire a fee simple absolute in the property occupied by its right of way by adverse possession or was the interest in the right of way merely an easement? (3) If the railroad acquired only an easement by prescription through adverse possession, could that easement be conveyed to the state? (4) Did the clause in the deed excepting and reserving the railroad right of way also except the land beneath the right of way from the conveyance? The court held that (1) the railroad acquired an easement in the property by adverse possession, and the state did not acquire good title with the quitclaim deeds. And (2) the clause in the deed did not except the land beneath the right of way from the conveyance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the railroad.

Miller v. Wauwatosa


No. 76-410


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


87 Wis. 2d 676; 275 N.W.2d 876; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 1900


January 29, 1979, Argued  
February 27, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from orders of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Robert J. Parins, Circuit Judge of the Fourteenth Circuit, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) in favor of respondent city in the landowner's action challenging the city's relocation of a roadway.


OVERVIEW: The landowner owned property abutting a city street. The city moved the traveled portion of the roadway, and the landowner brought an action claiming that the movement of the roadway constituted a discontinuance. The trial court entered a judgment in favor of the city, and the landowner sought review. The court affirmed, holding that the landowner had certain rights as the owner of property abutting the road. Wis. Stat. § 80.47. Only the landowner's right of access was involved in his challenge to the city's discontinuance, and the landowner still had access to the road after the discontinuance. Also, Wis. Stat. 66.296(2m) did not retroactively deprive the landowner of his reversionary interest in his easement to the road. The landowner was not entitled to an injunction against the city because the landowner was not deprived of a fundamental vested right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the city in the landowner's action challenging the relocation of the roadway.

Kozlowski v. John E. Smith's Sons Co.


No. 76-368


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


87 Wis. 2d 882; 275 N.W.2d 915; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 1909


January 9, 1979, Argued  
February 27, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Louis J. Ceci, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff widow appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted defendant manufacturer's motion for directed verdict and entered a judgment of dismissal, in the widow's products liability action against the manufacturer for the death of her husband that occurred as her husband was in the process of cleaning the manufacturer's product.


OVERVIEW: The widow's husband was killed in an industrial accident at his employer's plant while cleaning a sausage stuffer manufactured by the manufacturer. The husband was using maximum pressure as he cleaned, causing the cylinder and piston to jut beyond the safety line of the machine, fracturing the safety ring, resulting in a piece of the ring fracturing an ammonia pipe. The husband died of ammonia asphyxiation. There was a safety by-pass valve available, of which the employer was unaware. Evidence at trial also revealed that the machine had been in disrepair for one year prior to the accident and that the husband was not following the cleaning procedures set out by the employer. The trial court granted a directed verdict in favor of the manufacturer and dismissed the action. The court held that the directed verdict was improper because there was sufficient evidence to require the matter to go to the jury, including evidence of negligence attributable to the employer, evidence of an unreasonably dangerous defective condition in the design of the product, whether the defect was obvious, and whether the manufacturer gave sufficient warning regarding the use of pressure during cleaning.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the manufacturer and remanded the case for a new trial.

Laufenberg v. Cosmetology Examining Board of Wisconsin Dep't of Regulation & Licensing


Nos. 76-191, 76-192


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


87 Wis. 2d 175; 274 N.W.2d 618; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 1995


October 2, 1979, Argued  
January 30, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on May 1, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: William C. Sachtjen, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a cosmetologist and a barber, challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which upheld the decisions of respondents, the Cosmetology Examining Board of Wisconsin Department of Regulation & Licensing and the Barber's Examining Board of Wisconsin Department of Regulation & Licensing, that they violated Wis. Stat. §§ 159.09 and 159.12.


OVERVIEW: The Cosmetology Examining Board found that the cosmetologist practiced cosmetology and operated a beauty salon on a premise not licensed as a beauty salon in violation of Wis. Stat. § 159.09(1). It also concluded that she practiced cosmetology while not under the supervision and of a licensed manager in violation of Wis. Stat. § 159.12(2). The Barber Examining Board found that the barber' was not licensed as a managing cosmetologist and his shop was not licensed as a beauty salon. The court found that the cosmetologist and barber failed to provide proof that would support a holding that Wis. Stat. §§ 159.09 and 159.12 were arbitrary and unreasonable and therefore unconstitutional. Their two professions were not sufficiently similar so as to make §§ 159.09 and 159.12 unreasonable. There was a rational basis for requiring licensed cosmetology operators to practice only under the supervision and direction of a licensed manager. The requirement was reasonable related to achieving the legislature's goal to insure that cosmetology was practiced only by competent operators.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding the decisions of the Cosmetology Examining Board and Barber's Examining Board that the cosmetologist and barber violated the licensing statutes.

State v. Dix


No. 76-659-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


86 Wis. 2d 474; 273 N.W.2d 250; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 2014


November 28, 1978, Argued  
January 9, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on February 27, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Error to review a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Racine County: Richard G. Harvey, Jr., County Judge of Racine County, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which, following a jury trial, convicted him of two counts of attempted first-degree murder and two counts of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been charged following two violent muggings. Both victims identified defendant and he presented an alibi defense and an insanity defense. The court affirmed his convictions because the evidence was sufficient to sustain them. Defendant argued that the State failed to prove the unequivocal act element because the knife wounds inflicted upon the victim were not of a sufficiently aggravated nature. The court found that defendant misunderstood the nature of the charge. Attempted first-degree murder did not require that injuries of any particular degree of severity result and an unequivocal act had clearly been shown. Additionally, the armed robbery conviction was appropriate because the facts showed evidence of a use of force to overcome the victim's resistance and the intent to steal was reasonably inferred from the fact that he actually did take her purse. The court held that by instructing the jury that a victim's successful evasive action could have been considered an extraneous factor the trial court was correctly informing them of the court's interpretation of law. The court held that it remained constitutional to burden defendant with proving his insanity defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions.

Locklear v. State


No. 76-595-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


86 Wis. 2d 603; 273 N.W.2d 334; 1979 Wisc. LEXIS 2027


November 29, 1978, Submitted on Briefs  
January 9, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Error to review an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County: Clair Voss, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a writ of error to review a judgment and an order from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin). The order affirmed defendant's conviction by the county court of three counts of issuing worthless checks, a violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.24(1) (1975). The order affirmed the sentence that was stayed and defendant's probation.


OVERVIEW: The county court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the State's complaint alleging violations of § 943.24(1). After he pled guilty, defendant filed a notice of appeal and a motion for reversal and to dismiss the complaint on the basis that § 943.24 was unconstitutional. The contested judgment and order were affirmed. The court held that the State did not abuse its discretion and violate defendant's constitutional rights by its policy not to charge a person with issuing a worthless check if that person made payment on the check within five days of the demand. The court found that defendant neither proved any discrimination against poor people nor proved that the district attorney knew of the financial status of the individuals to whom the five-day notices were sent. The court held that the State's charging policy was not discriminatory and was based on justifiable and reasonable considerations. The court found that, although those who timely made restitution avoided prosecution and those who did not make restitution were charged, no proof existed that those who were similarly situated were treated unequally whether they were rich or poor, or new felons or repeat offenders.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and the order challenged by defendant.

Wisconsin's Environmental Decade, Inc. v. Department of Natural Resources


No. 76-086


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


85 Wis. 2d 518; 271 N.W.2d 69; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1265


October 3, 1978, Argued  
October 31, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: George R. Currie, Reserve Circuit Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the city and an environmental group, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed an order of respondent, the Wisconsin Department of Natural Resources (DNR). The DNR's order issued permits for the chemical control of lake weeds. The issues on appeal centered around the division of power between the city and the DNR with respect to the chemical control of lake weeds.


OVERVIEW: The city issued a resolution establishing a city policy of protesting and preventing the use of chemicals by others. The DNR issued permits to certain groups for the chemical treatment of lake weeds, and the city objected. The DNR's permit order was affirmed, and affirmed again on appeal. The court concluded that the evidence supported the DNR's findings that the chemicals permitted to be used were safe and effective as properly applied. Wis. Stat. § 144.025(2)(i) vested express authority in the DNR to supervise chemical treatment of waters, based on the state's "public trust" duties, the language of the statute itself, and the clear legislative purpose to centralize overall water resource management under the DNR pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 144.025(1). The city had the power to prohibit chemical treatment of aquatic nuisances in lake waters under Wis. Stat. § 62.11(5), unless there was express language elsewhere in the statutes restricting or revoking it. Therefore, the city's resolution was invalid because it conflicted with the DNR's statutory authority, which had not been withdrawn.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which had affirmed the DNR's order issuing permits for the chemical control of lake weeds. The court concluded that the DNR had the statutory authority to supervise chemical treatment and issue the permits over the city's objections. The city's conflicting resolution was invalid. The DNR's findings were supported by substantial evidence.

Lhost v. State


No. 76-564-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


85 Wis. 2d 620; 271 N.W.2d 121; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1273


October 4, 1978, Argued  
October 31, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Errors to review a judgment and orders of the County Court of Brown County: John C. Jaekels, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the County Court of Brown County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment of his conviction for the crime of attempted rape, which was defined by Wis. Stat. § 944.01 (1973) and Wis. Stat. § 939.32(2) (1973).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted rape. On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient, and that it was error for the trial court to refuse to admit into evidence the results of a polygraph test which were favorable to defendant because the prosecution refused to stipulate that the results would be admissible. In affirming, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to prove the elements of attempted rape; the facts created a reasonable inference that defendant intended to have sexual intercourse with the victim, and that defendant would use force to accomplish the same. The court then held that the requirement that the prosecution stipulate to the admission of the results of the allegedly exculpatory polygraph evidence did not violate defendant's due process right to compulsory process. The court stated that there was the opportunity for extraneous factors to influence polygraph tests results, which, if admitted, had the potential to confuse the jury and lead the jury into collateral inquiries, and thus the stipulation condition insured that the polygraph examination would be used as an investigative tool, and not as a device to confuse the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Steeno v. State


Nos. 76-388-CR, 76-660-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


85 Wis. 2d 663; 271 N.W.2d 396; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1275; 2 A.L.R.4th 608


October 4, 1978, Submitted on Briefs  
October 31, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 76-388-CR. Appeal from a judgment and on order of the Circuit Court for Brown County: Robert J. Parins, Circuit Judge.

No. 76-660-CR. Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Rock County: Arthur L. Luebke, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed. As to Case No. 76-660-CR, Kenneth W. Stubbendick, Plaintiff in Error, v. State of Wisconsin, Defendant in Error, for all of the above-stated reasons, judgment and order are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Brown County and Rock County (Wisconsin), which imposed a one-year mandatory imprisonment following their third conviction of driving after their license was revoked in violation of Wis. Stat. § 343.44(2) (1975).


OVERVIEW: Both defendants were convicted, for the third time, of driving after their license had been revoked in violation of Wis. Stat. § 343.44(2). Pursuant to § 343.44(2), after a third conviction under that statute a mandatory one-year prison sentence was imposed. Both defendants appealed the mandatory imprisonment and the appellate courts affirmed. Thereafter, the court granted review. Defendants alleged the one-year mandatory imprisonment provision constituted cruel and unusual punishment contrary to the Eighth Amendment and Wis. Const. art. I, § VI. The court affirmed defendants' sentences. It did not find § 343.44(2) constitutionally defective. A mandatory one-year term of imprisonment for those who could not abide by the state's traffic laws and who persisted in driving after having their drivers' licenses revoked did not shock the public conscience so as to constitute cruel and unusual punishment. In light of the potential for great harm caused by such persons public sentiment demanded a strong legislative response to the problem, including the mandatory imprisonment of drivers who had no respect for the motor vehicle laws of the state.


OUTCOME: Defendants' mandatory imprisonment following their third conviction for driving with a revoked license was affirmed.

Cheatham v. State


No. 76-453-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


85 Wis. 2d 112; 270 N.W.2d 194; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1052


September 7, 1978, Argued  
October 3, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Error to review a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Richard W. Bardwell, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) for the infliction of great bodily harm to another human being in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.23.


OVERVIEW: The victim was struck on the head and dragged on a sidewalk by her wrists. Her assailant ran away after several people arrived at the scene. The witnesses and the victim identified defendant as the assailant. On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support a finding that the victim's injury constituted "great bodily harm" as defined by Wis. Stat. § 939.22(14), and that the definition of "great bodily harm" set forth in § 939.22(14) was unconstitutionally vague on its face or as interpreted by the court in a prior case. Rejecting both arguments, the court affirmed the judgment of conviction. The court held that that the issue of the severity of the victim's injury was properly submitted to the jury. Because the evidence showed that defendant's attack left the victim with a fractured skull and a permanent hole in her head, the jury could have found that the victim's injury constituted "great bodily harm." The court further held that the definition of "great bodily harm" set forth in § 939.22(14) was not unconstitutionally vague. The court believed that the jury was capable of deciding whether the victim's injuries were greater than mere bodily harm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Holtz & Krause, Inc. v. Department of Natural Resources


Nos. 77-668, 77-669


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


85 Wis. 2d 198; 270 N.W.2d 409; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1058


September 5, 1978, Argued  
October 3, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motions for Reconsideration Denied, without Costs, on November 28, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals and Cross-appeals from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Marathon County: Ronald D. Keberle, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- That part (paragraph 1) of the judgment, reversing paragraphs 1 through 4 of the DNR order and remanding the case to the DNR for further evidence, is reversed. That part (paragraph 2) of the judgment, affirming the remainder of the order, is affirmed. The cause is remanded to the circuit court with directions to affirm the DNR order and remand to the DNR for a determination of a date for implementation of the department order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Department of Natural Resources (DNR) and public intervenor, and respondents, city and waste landfill corporation, appealed and cross-appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Marathon County (Wisconsin) that affirmed in part and reversed in part a DNR order prescribing a schedule for the abandonment of a solid waste disposal landfill.


OVERVIEW: The DNR issued an order prescribing a schedule for the abandonment of the corporation's solid waste disposal landfill. The circuit court affirmed the order in part and reversed in part, determining that there was substantial evidenced supporting the DNR's findings that the landfill was having a detrimental effect on the ground and surface water. The case was remanded to the DNR for further evidence on the question of a schedule for abandonment. Appeals and cross-appeals were taken by all parties of the circuit court's judgment. The court reversed that part of the judgement that remanded the case to the DNR and affirmed that portion of the judgment that affirmed the DNR's order. The court held that the DNR properly based its order on the 1000-foot rule of Wis. Admin. Code § NR 151.12(4)(a); that the abandonment schedule was supported by substantial evidence; and that the DNR was not required to prepare an environmental impact statement in connection with the abandonment order. The court's holding obviated an inquiry into the application of the rules proscribing landfill sites where the DNR had found that leaching may have had a detrimental effect on ground and surface waters.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the circuit court judgment that remanded the case to the DNR for further evidence, and affirmed that part of the judgment affirming the remainder of the DNR's order.

State ex rel. Deisinger v. Treffert


No. 76-714


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


85 Wis. 2d 257; 270 N.W.2d 402; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1062


September 7, 1978, Argued  
October 3, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County: William E. Crane, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin) releasing defendant. The state contended that defendant should not have been released. Defendant contended that Wis. Stat. § 971.14(5) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was not competent to stand trial on a criminal offense. Apparently, the trial court released defendant after the period of his confinement exceeded the maximum potential for the offense he was charged with. The state contended that defendant should have remained confined for 24 months under WIS. Stat. § 971.14(5). Apparently, defendant contended that § 971.14(5) was unconstitutional because it required defendant to be confined for a period longer than his potential maximum penalty. Defendant also contended that he should have been given credit for time served for the period he was confined . The court affirmed the order releasing defendant. The court held that defendant was entitled to be released on the date his confinement exceeded his potential maximum sentence penalty under the offense charged because the state did not establish that defendant was dangerous as required by Wis. Stat. § 51. The court also stated that defendant's continued confinement could only proceed only after defendant would have been given the due process guarantees accorded civil committees under Wis. Stat. § 51. The court stated that § 971.14(5) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order releasing defendant from confinement.

 

364 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. La Follette v. Torphy


No. 77-860


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


85 Wis. 2d 94; 270 N.W.2d 187; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1051


September 6, 1978, Argued  
October 3, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Action for a declaratory judgment, commenced pursuant to leave granted.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The Improvements Tax Relief provisions of sec. 79.24 and 79.25, Stats., are declared unconstitutional as violative of art. VIII, sec. 1, of the Wisconsin Constitution.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to leave granted, petitioner attorney general brought an original action for a declaratory judgment against respondent Secretary of the Wisconsin Department of Administration to determine whether the Improvements Tax Relief provisions of Wis. Stat. §§ 79.24 and 79.25 violated the uniformity of taxation clause, Wis. Const. art. VIII, § 1, and state and federal equal protection clauses, Wis. Const. art. I, § 1 and the Fourteenth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The attorney general obtained the court's permission to bring the action after the Secretary refused to allot funds to implement the Improvements Tax Relief law, Wis. Stat. §§ 79.24 and 79.25, which provided tax credits to two classes of property owners for improvements that resulted in increased property tax assessments. The state paid the tax credit to the property owner from the general revenue fund. The credit could be applied to any outstanding liability the owner had with the state revenue department. The court concluded that §§ 79.24 and 79.25 did not violate equal protection because the classifications were reasonably related to the legislation's purposes. The court found, however, that §§ 79.24 and 79.25 contravened Wis. Const. art. VIII, § 1, because the classifications effected an unequal burden and the uniformity of taxation clause required that taxation act alike on all persons similarly situated. The court held that the Improvements Tax Relief law was a tax statute subject to the uniformity clause because it had the effect of changing individual tax burdens by granting a partial exemption and was predicated upon property ownership and the assessment of improvements.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the Improvements Tax Relief provisions did not contravene the federal or state equal protection clauses but that they were unconstitutional as violative of the uniformity of taxation clause of the Wisconsin Constitution.

Niagara of Wisconsin Paper Corp. v. Wisconsin Dep't of Natural Resources


Nos. 76-668, 77-326


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


84 Wis. 2d 32; 268 N.W.2d 153; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1071; 11 ERC (BNA) 2024; 8 ELR 20739


May 1, 1978, Argued  
June 30, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 76-668 -- Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: George R. Currie, Reserve Circuit Judge, Presiding.

No. 77-326 -- Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Richard W. Bardwell, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Wisconsin Department of Natural Resources (DNR) challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), that the DNR was required to modify Wisconsin Pollution Discharge Elimination System (WPDES) permits to appellee paper companies under Wis. Stat. § 147, which was based on the Federal Water Pollution Control Act Amendments of 1972 (FWPCAA), 33 U.S.C.S. § 1251 et seq.


OVERVIEW: In issue was whether WPDES permits issued under interim rules based on Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) guidelines were required to be revised to reflect the final EPA regulations which the DNR had adopted. DNR asserted that if its permits were not vested with some finality, if every change in a rule or regulation would demand a change in the permit, there would result an administrative nightmare of uncertainty, etc. On the other hand, the paper companies contended and the lower courts agreed that Wis. Stat. § 147.021, stood for a policy of uniformity; that while recognizing the need for effluent limitations, the legislature sought to insure that Wisconsin industries would have an equal footing with competitors in other states, and that this policy would be defeated if permits issued under the older, more stringent rules were not modified. The court found that the DNR incorrectly accepted EPA guidelines as best practicable control technology currently available (BPT) standards. The legislature intended that industrial polluters be bound only to a final determination of BPT. Thus permittees were entitled to an actual determination of BPT in accordance with due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that the DNR was required to modify the WPDES permits to the paper companies.

State v. Tronca

Bence v. Milwaukee


No. 76-027


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


84 Wis. 2d 224; 267 N.W.2d 25; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1081


May 3, 1978, Submitted on Briefs  
June 30, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Leander J. Foley, Jr., Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, City and Annuity and Benefit Fund, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which overruled their demurrer to the complaint of respondents, retired police officers and employees, for declaratory judgment under Wis. Stat. 269.56, now re-numbered as Wis. Stat. § 806.04(2).


OVERVIEW: Respondents alleged that a charter ordinance adopted by the Council was unconstitutional because it deprived them of their constitutional rights of equal protection and due process in respect to their pensions. When respondents were unable to gain redress from the Council, they filed an action for declaratory judgment. Appellants filed a demurrer to the complaint, which the trial court overruled. On appeal, the judgment was affirmed. The court held that portions of the complaint referred to sufficiently asserted a justiciable controversy and sufficiently stated a caused of action for declaratory judgment. The court also ruled that the trial court properly overruled the demurrer on the grounds that the ordinance was severable. Therefore, it was unnecessary to join the other officers in the suit. It was the duty of the city attorney to appear on behalf of respondents. Thus, the interests of other police officers in the Fund were sufficiently represented, even though they were not joined.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment overruling appellants' demurrer to the complaint.

Midwestern Gas Transmission Co. v. Wisconsin Dep't of Revenue

Supreme Court of Wisconsin

June 6, 1978, Argued  
June 30, 1978, Decided

DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Revenue (Wisconsin) sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which reversed an administrative order affirming the Department's assessment of a use tax on natural gas consumed by respondent taxpayer at its Wisconsin compressor stations.


OVERVIEW: The Department assessed a use tax on natural gas consumed at the taxpayer's compressor stations. The gas was used to propel the bulk of the taxpayer's natural gas though its Wisconsin pipelines. An administrative decision upholding the assessment was overturned by the circuit court, which determined that the tax violated the Commerce Clause of the U.S. Constitution, U.S. Const. art. The court found that the tax was an improper burden on an activity that was an integral and inseparable part of the interstate flow of the taxpayer's natural gas. Moreover, the court found that the taxpayer's activity did not have a substantial nexus with the state, which, the court noted, was the key issue in determining whether a use tax was valid under § 8(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court judgment.

Will v. State


No. 76-366-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


84 Wis. 2d 397; 267 N.W.2d 357; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1092


June 7, 1978, Argued  
June 30, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Error to review an order of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County: William E. Crane, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order modified and, as modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a trial court's decision to sentence defendant to 25 days in jail if he was unable to pay a fine in a criminal case after 90 days.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant. He was sentenced to five days in jail and ordered to pay a fine of $ 250. Defendant contended that he was unable to pay the fine because he was indigent. The trial court gave defendant an additional 90 days to pay the fine, but ordered a 25 day jail sentence if defendant was unable to pay. The trial court's decision was affirmed on appeal. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 973.05 did not violate defendant's rights under the Equal Protection Clause because the trial court had the discretion to allow defendant to make installment payments on the fine. This procedures gave the trial court sufficient flexibility to avoid unconstitutionally imprisoning an offender who was unable to pay a fine. The trial court erred because it did not consider modifying the sentence to take into consideration defendant's financial state. The trial court chose the 90 day period arbitrarily, without giving reasons why the period itself was reasonable. Finally, the court held that there was no constitutional bar to the State's attempts to collect the fine for an indeterminate period of time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order giving defendant 90 days to pay his fine. The court modified the order to permit defendant to apply for a modification of the sentence if he was still unable to pay the fine after 90 days.

In re Estate of Blumreich


Nos. 75-728, 76-068


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


84 Wis. 2d 545; 267 N.W.2d 870; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1101


March 7, 1978, Submitted  
June 30, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from two orders of the County Court of Shawano-Menominee County: Edward P. Herald, County Judge of Oconto County, Presiding; and Ralph J. Strandberg, County Judge of Langlade County, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner minor filed an action in the Shawano-Menominee County Court (Wisconsin), Probate Branch, for a support allowance from decedent's estate and for a determination that minor was decedent's sole surviving heir. The petition was denied. Thereafter, minor commenced a similar action for declaratory relief in the Shawano-Menominee County Court (Wisconsin). Again, minor was unsuccessful. The appeal of both cases followed.


OVERVIEW: Minor was conceived by two unmarried individuals. While decedent told acquaintances that he was the father of the unborn child, he made no written acknowledgement of paternity, no admission of paternity in open court, and there was no adjudication of paternity. Decedent died approximately two and one-half months before minor's birth. In affirming the lower courts' denials of minor's requests for relief, the court held that, because minor was unable to satisfy the statutory requirements for establishing paternity as required by Wis. Stat. Ann. § 852.05(1), he was not able to establish paternity by way of a declaratory judgment action or an action in probate court following decedent's death. The court held that minor was not entitled to support allowance from decedent's estate. Lastly, the court rejected minor's argument that the statute denied equal protection and due process of law to an illegitimate child born after the death of his putative father. The court explained that the statute's exclusion of other forms of posthumous proof of paternity represented a reasonable effort to eliminate imprecise and unduly burdensome methods of establishing paternity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders.

 

371 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. Kolstad


No. 77-351


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


84 Wis. 2d 579; 267 N.W.2d 886; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1102


May 1, 1978, Argued  
June 30, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the County Court of Barron County: Fred Van Sickle, County Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed, with directions to dismiss the complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the driver in an accident that caused the death of plaintiff child's putative father, appealed an order of the County Court of Barron County (Wisconsin), which denied the driver's motion to dismiss the child's wrongful death action. The attorney general filed a brief amicus curiae urging that Wis. Stat. § 852.05(1) and Wis. Stat. ch. 52 be construed to permit commencement of a paternity proceeding after the death of a putative father.


OVERVIEW: The appeal concerned the narrow question of whether the decedent's posthumous illegitimate child could maintain an action for the death of his putative father under the wrongful death statutes, Wis. Stat. §§ 895.01, 895.03, 895.04. The court held that he could not. Prior caselaw rejected the argument that Wis. Stat. ch. 52 should be construed to permit a posthumous paternity proceeding as well as the argument that the requirements of the Wrongful Death Act and Wis. Stat. § 852.05(1) denied after-born illegitimate children equal protection or due process of law. The child acknowledged that he could not meet the burden of proof required by § 852.05(1), which prescribed means of proof of paternity for illegitimate children by subsequent marriage, adoption, adjudication, oral or written admissions in open court, or acknowledgment in writing signed by the putative father without a witness. The only types of proof excluded by the statutes were oral admissions outside of court or unsigned written acknowledgments, and the court held that sound policy reasons for these legislative exclusions were readily apparent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the county court, with directions to dismiss the complaint.

State ex rel. Huser v. Rasmussen


No. 76-759


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


84 Wis. 2d 600; 267 N.W.2d 285; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1104


May 3, 1978, Submitted on Briefs  
June 30, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Denied, without Costs, on September 21, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Green Lake County: Jerold E. Murphy, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Green Lake County (Wisconsin), which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus after he was bound over for trial on four counts of delivering a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: A criminal complaint charged defendant with five counts of delivering a controlled substance in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 161.41(b), -.16(4). The complaint was later reduced to four counts. A preliminary examination was held, and defendant was bound over for trial. Defendant filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The trial court dismissed the petition. Defendant argued that the testimony of the State's chemists was insufficient to establish probable cause to believe that he had committed a felony and that the hearing court improperly limited his right of cross-examination. The court found that the evidence produced at the preliminary examination supported the determination that there was probable cause to believe that defendant had committed a felony. It was unnecessary for the State to identify the particular substance delivered as d-cocaine or l-cocaine because Wis. Stat. § 161.16(4) controlled the delivery of the isomer of cocaine known as d-cocaine. The trial court did not err in restricting cross-examination of an undercover agent because the questions defendant sought to ask went beyond the plausibility of his story and were directed toward his general credibility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which denied defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

Department of Health & Social Services v. State Personnel Board


No. 76-116


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


84 Wis. 2d 675; 267 N.W.2d 644; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1110


June 6, 1978, Argued  
June 30, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: William C. Sachtjen, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Wisconsin State Personnel Board and a former state employee, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which reversed the Board's order that required respondent employer to immediately reinstate the employee. The circuit court reversed, finding that the Board lacked jurisdiction to hear the employee's case.


OVERVIEW: After acquiring permanent status, the employee was promoted to a position within another agency. Prior to the end of his probationary period for his new position, he was discharged. The Board found that the employee was improperly terminated and ordered reinstatement. The court found that the circuit court properly determined that the Board lacked jurisdiction because the employee did not have permanent status in class after the promotion, as required under Wis. Stat. § 16.05(1)(e) (1975). The provision required that status in class related to a class in which the employee was then serving and not a past position. Further, Wis. Admin. Code § Pers. 14.03 and Wis. Stat. § 16.22(1) provided that, for promotion between agencies, an employee was required to serve a probationary period. The court found that the provisions did not violate equal protection where there was a reasonable distinction between inter-departmental and intra-departmental promotions because of a bureaucratic practice of "up and out." Further, because the employee had no permanent status in class, the employee was not deprived of a due process property or liberty interest in continued public employment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order reversing the Board's decision.

Grand Lodge-Free & Accepted Masons v. Conta

Supreme Court of Wisconsin


84 Wis. 2d 701; 267 N.W.2d 375; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1112

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lodges appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied their motion for a temporary injunction to prevent defendant tax officials from continuing investigations of the lodges' membership requirements pending the circuit court's determination of the lodges' petition for declaratory relief. The lodges sought a declaration that the officials had no authority to proceed with the investigations.


OVERVIEW: Wis. Stat. § 70.11(4) granted property tax exemptions to lodges, and Wis. Stat. § 71.01(3)(a) granted income tax exemptions to benevolent associations. An unrelated federal court decision held that the statutes were unconstitutional insofar as they afforded benefits to organizations that discriminated in their membership on the basis of race. The tax officials investigated the lodges and found that each lodge discriminated on the basis of race. Administrative procedures were substantially complete in respect to four of the lodges. However, the court modified the order and enjoined administrative proceedings involving all the lodges, except the four, pending completion of administrative hearings and final court review as to the four.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the orders and affirmed the denial of the lodges' petition to enjoin administrative procedures as to the four lodges. The court modified the denial of the petition to enjoin administrative action in respect to all lodges and enjoined such action as to the remaining lodges pending final court review of the four. The court enjoined the officials from summarily revoking the lodges' tax exempt status during the injunction.

Browne v. Milwaukee Bd. of Sch. Dirs.


No. 77-318


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


83 Wis. 2d 316; 265 N.W.2d 559; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 991


February 6, 1978, Argued  
May 2, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Denied, without Costs, on June 30, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Michael J. Barron, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed and cause remanded to the Milwaukee Circuit Court to transfer the cause to W.E.R.C. for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff non-union municipal workers challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which referred the case to the Wisconsin Employment Relations Commission and denied the workers' motion to escrow deductions in an action against defendant school board, unions, and others. The dispute involved whether fair-share deductions pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 111.70(1)(h) (1975) were spent for impermissible purposes.


OVERVIEW: The workers challenged the transfer to the Wisconsin Employment Relations Commission (W.E.R.C.) and also the denial of their motion to escrow all fair-share deductions. The court affirmed. The workers petitioned the court for a writ of mandamus requiring the trial court to vacate its order of referral to W.E.R.C. and exercise jurisdiction in the case. The court entered an order holding the mandamus petition in abeyance, pending the disposition of the appeal. The court denied the unions' motion to dismiss the appeal for want of jurisdiction. In applying the doctrine of primary jurisdiction to the unresolved facts and issues of the case the trial court did not abuse its discretion in transferring the case to W.E.R.C. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 111.70(1)(h) (1975) was constitutional on its face and by its terms could not require the workers to contribute to political purposes in violation of their First Amendment rights. The trial court indicated that it was pure speculation to determine without any factual basis what percentage of funds were in fact impermissibly spent by unions. That statement at least demonstrated an exercise of discretion by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying the workers' motion to escrow funds deducted by the unions. The court remanded the case to the trial court for transfer to W.E.R.C. for further proceedings.

State ex rel. Kleczka v. Conta


No. 77-463-OA


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


82 Wis. 2d 679; 264 N.W.2d 539; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1174


January 23, 1978, Argued  
April 5, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Action for declaratory judgment.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Rights declared validating the partial vetoes exercised by the Governor pursuant to art. V, sec. 10, Wisconsin Constitution, upon enrolled Assembly Bill 664, published as ch. 107, Laws of 1977. Relief requested by petitioners denied. No questions concerning the validity of ch. 107, Laws of 1977, other than those relating to the approval, enactment, and publication thereof, are now determined.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, state senator and representative, sought a declaratory judgment that a partial veto of an enrolled election campaign finance bill by respondent Governor of the State of Wisconsin was legally deficient, and that the entire enrolled bill had the force of law. The senator and the representative contended that the bill did not fall under the partial veto provisions of Wis. Const. art. V, § 10, because it was not an appropriation bill.


OVERVIEW: The enrolled bill to create Wis. Stat. § 71.095 concerned election campaign finance through a legislatively created campaign fund. The Governor vetoed a part of the bill that required taxpayers to add a sum to their taxes if they desired to contribute to the campaign fund. The Governor changed the part by requiring taxpayers to indicate the sum to be "checked off" for the fund, a change that would have increased the fund. The court declared the partial vetoes valid. The enrolled bill was an appropriation bill because when it authorized public money being expended when it went to the Governor, it authorized the expenditure of public money. The Governor properly returned the objected-to part of the bill to the legislature within the six days called for by Wisconsin Constitution because for partial vetoes, the entire bill did not need to be returned. Petitioners admitted that for the preceding 15 years, the legislature had acquiesced to the Governor so returning objected-to portions of bills. The portions of the bill that the Governor struck were severable because the partial veto did not affect the appropriation.


OUTCOME: In the case filed by the senator and the representative, the court declared that the Governor's partial vetoes were valid. The court declined to hold that the entire enrolled bill had the force of law.

 

378 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


O'Connell v. Board of Educ.


No. 77-295


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


82 Wis. 2d 728; 264 N.W.2d 561; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1175


March 7, 1978, Argued  
April 5, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Pending. This Motion was not Decided at the Time the Volume Went to Press. Its Disposition will be Reported in a Later Volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County: Jerold E. Murphy, Circuit Judge of the Eighteenth Circuit, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment vacated with directions to dismiss the complaint of the plaintiffs without prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which was rendered in favor of respondents, a school district, a village board of education, and others, in the parents' declaratory judgment suit asking the court to compel the school district to transport their children to a private school outside of the district's boundaries.


OVERVIEW: The parents had children who attended a private school and brought suit asking the court to compel the school district to transport their children to the school, which was located outside the boundaries of the school district. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the school district and the parents appealed on equal protection grounds. The court noted that there was a threshold question in the appeal which had not been briefed by the parties regarding whether the trial court had jurisdiction to determine the constitutional issues raised by the parents. The court held that because the parties were seeking declaratory relief, the requirement of Wis. Stat. § 269.56(11) (1973) of service on the Wisconsin Attorney General was applicable to the case. The court therefore held that the trial court was without jurisdiction to try the case in the absence of service upon the Attorney General. The court remanded the case to the trial court with directions to set aside the judgment and dismiss the parents' complaint for the reason that the Attorney General was not served with a copy of the proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court with directions to dismiss the complaint of the parents without prejudice.

State ex rel. Bell v. County Court for Columbia County


No. 77-379


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


82 Wis. 2d 401; 263 N.W.2d 162; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1153


February 7, 1978, Argued  
March 7, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Columbia County: Howard Latton, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed and cause remanded for trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin), which required defendants to stand trial after the court concluded that there was a reasonable probability that defendants had committed a violation of Wis. Stat. § 161.41(1)(b) and that the information charging defendants with the crime was sufficient.


OVERVIEW: After defendants were charged with manufacturing methamphetamine, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 161.41(1)(b), they were ordered to stand trial after a preliminary hearing. Defendants appealed and argued that the information failed to charge them with a violation of § 161.41(1)(b) because no methamphetamine was found at the scene and some methamphetamine was required to exist before a charge of manufacture could be brought in light of the fact that there was no immediate precursor for methamphetamine. The court disagreed and held that the statutory language did not require the existence of the controlled substance created through defendants' activities to constitute a violation of the prohibition of controlled substance manufacture. The court further held that § 161.41(1)(b) was not unconstitutionally vague. Defendants also contended that there was insufficient evidence at the preliminary hearing to establish probable cause. The court affirmed the trial court's order. The court found that there was sufficient competent evidence to permit the magistrate to conclude that, within the realm of reasonable probability, defendants had committed a violation of § 161.41(1)(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order and remanded the cause for trial.

State ex rel. First Nat'l Bank v. M & I Peoples Bank


No. 75-730


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


82 Wis. 2d 529; 263 N.W.2d 196; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1161


January 5, 1978, Submitted on Briefs  
March 7, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Wood County: James H. Levi, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant national bank challenged a determination of the Circuit Court for Wood County (Wisconsin), which dismissed the national bank's suit for a determination that it could raise by a complaint in quo warranto, issues that could have been resolved in an action for review under the Administrative Procedure Act, Wis. Stat. ch. 227. The national bank sought a determination that respondent branch bank's franchise was null and void.


OVERVIEW: The branch bank applied to respondent Commissioner of Banking, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 221.04(1)(j) for permission to establish a branch bank facility. The national bank filed a formal protest and the Commissioner and respondent Banking Review Board approved the application. The Board refused the national bank's motion for rehearing. The national bank filed a petition in a lower court seeking to set aside the order under Wis. Stat. § ch. 227, but the petition was dismissed for failure to file within 30-days. The present action was filed after a lower court dismissed the national bank's complaint for a declaratory judgment to set aside the Commissioner's order. The court affirmed. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 221.04(1)(j) provided that an application for a branch bank by a state chartered bank must be approved by both the Commissioner and the Board and Wis. Stat. § 220.035(3) provided that any final order or determination of the banking review board was subject to review in the manner provided in Wis. Stat. ch. 227. The court found that these sections created an exclusive statutory remedy of appeal under ch. 227 and the national bank was not entitled to quo warranto review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court dismissing the national bank's suit for a determination that it could raise by a complaint in quo warranto against the branch bank, the Commissioner, and the Board.

State ex rel. Ft. Howard Paper Co. v. State Lake Dist. Board of Review


No. 77-042


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


82 Wis. 2d 491; 263 N.W.2d 178; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1159


January 5, 1978, Argued  
March 7, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Brown County: Robert J. Parins, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Reversed and remanded with instructions to return the case to the Lake District Board of Review for purposes of setting aside the assessment and entering another assessment not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner manufacturer appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which dismissed a writ of certiorari and affirmed the decision of the State of Wisconsin Lake District Board of Review. The Board reduced the assessment for the manufacturer's improvements, but the manufacturer claimed that the Board failed to properly consider deductions for excess operating costs and certain market adjustments.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer's buildings comprised a paper mill. It challenged its 1975 assessment, which was 57 percent greater than the preceding year's assessment. The manufacturer claimed the Board's valuation was erroneous because the Board failed to consider excess operating costs caused by the inefficient layout of the buildings and production process. The circuit court affirmed the Board's decision. On appeal, the court found that despite the Board's misgivings about the concept of excess operating costs, such costs were deducted. However, the Board erred when it deleted the undisputed market adjustments from its final appraisal. The circuit court's uniformity analysis was incorrect, but the valuation of the manufacturer's property under Wis. Stat. § 70.955(7)(b) (1975) was constitutional. The manufacturer failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the statute caused a non-uniform valuation of its property in 1975, or that its improvements were unconstitutionally overvalued as compared to other Lake District manufacturers. The legislature did not deny the manufacturer equal protection of the law by providing a unique and specialized means of valuing manufacturing property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with instructions to return the case to the Lake District Board of Review for purposes of setting aside the assessment and entering another assessment. The court remanded for the Board to correct its assessment to include the market adjustments of the five buildings in question.

Holy Trinity Community School, Inc. v. Kahl


No. 75-731


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


82 Wis. 2d 139; 262 N.W.2d 210; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1134


October 5, 1977, Argued  
February 7, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Richard W. Bardwell, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded, with directions to enter judgment ordering the Superintendent of Public Instruction to designate an attendance area co-extensive with the school district.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant private school sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) that entered a judgment affirming the order of respondent Superintendent of Public Instruction. The superintendent had dismissed the school's petition for a district-wide attendance area after finding that the school was Catholic, despite contentions to the contrary, and its attendance area would have overlapped with other Catholic schools.


OVERVIEW: At the hearing, the school introduced evidence that it was a nondenominational school as proven by its articles of incorporation. However, after making a detailed inquiry into the school's operation, the superintendent concluded that the school was Catholic. The school contended that the question of religious affiliation was not justiciable in a court of the civil government. The court ruled that the superintendent's inquiry constituted an excessive entanglement of church and state. The court held that the entanglement doctrine under the First Amendment prohibited excessive intermixture of government and religion in the shape of intensive governmental control and surveillance. The court reasoned that the superintendent's detailed inquiry into the school's practices was repugnant to the Constitution. The court further reasoned that such could have been avoided by accepting the school for what it purported to be according to its articles of incorporation. The court held that a detailed inquiry was only permitted where fraud was alleged and proven. The court concluded that because there were no allegation of fraud in this case, the inquiry constituted an excessive entanglement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment entered in favor of the superintendent and remanded with instructions.

Layton School of Art & Design v. Wisconsin Employment Relations Com.

Supreme Court of Wisconsin

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner president appealed an order of the Circuit Court, Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which affirmed respondent employment relations commission's findings, conclusion, and order which found that the president committed perjury.


OVERVIEW: The president was the director of an institution of higher learning, and he terminated the employment of several teachers. The commission found that the president committed various unfair labor practices and that he committed the crime of perjury. The trial court affirmed the findings of the commission relating to the president's commission of perjury, and the president appealed. The court affirmed the order, ruling that an administrative body which did not adjudicate in the sense that a criminal court did could nevertheless exercise a function very much akin to making an official adjudication of criminal culpability.


OUTCOME: The order finding that the president committed perjury was affirmed.

 

384 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Strykowski v. Wilkie


No. 76-596-OA


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


81 Wis. 2d 491; 261 N.W.2d 434; 1978 Wisc. LEXIS 1218


September 1, 1977, Argued  
January 3, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Action commenced pursuant to leave granted.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Rights declared and cause remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, three medical malpractice claimants, sought a declaration that Wis. Stat. § 655 was unconstitutional and sought review of respondent Administrative Director of Courts (administrator), who convened six-member panels pursuant to § 655 to hear the three malpractice claims at issue. The statute established that all malpractice claims must first be reviewed by a patients' compensation panel, convened by the administrator.


OVERVIEW: The claimants argued that Wis. Stat. § 655 was unconstitutional as a violation of equal protection and due process, an unlawful delegation of judicial authority, and a violation of the right to a jury trial. The claimants objected to the convening of six-member patients' compensation panels to hear their cases. The court agreed that § 655 did not authorize the convening of a six-member panel and noted that, between the time the claimants petitioned the court and the court's decision, the legislature had amended the language of Wis. Stat. § 655.03(1)(b) and § 655.03(2)(a)(3) to remove ambiguity regarding its intention to require five-member panels for cases like the claimants'. The court rejected the claimants' constitutional challenges. The court held that § 655 had a rational basis to improve malpractice claim procedure and maintain the quality of health care. The court noted that it was not violative of due process to require parties to seek administrative resolution of claims before gaining access to the courts. The court also found that the admission into evidence of a panel's findings of fact was not error, as long as proper jury instructions were given.


OUTCOME: The court held that it was error for the administrator to convene six-member panels to hear the claimants' malpractice suits. The court concluded that the law only authorized the appointment of five- and three-member panels. The court held that the statute establishing review by patients' compensation panels was constitutional and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

Reidinger v. Optometry Examining Board

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff optometrist sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which quashed a writ of certiorari and affirmed the license revocation order issued by defendant Optometry Examining Board.


OVERVIEW: The optometrist was convicted on felony charges of federal income tax evasion, 26 U.S.C.S. § 7201. The Board consequently held a hearing pursuant to § 449.09 (1975), and issued an order revoking the optometrist's professional license pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 449.07(1)(d) on the basis that he had been convicted of a felony. The optometrist applied by writ of certiorari to the trial court for review of the Board's decision, and the trial court quashed the writ. In reversing the Board's order, the court did not reach the optometrist's constitutional claim. The court remanded the case to the Board for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision that had upheld the Board's decision to revoke the optometrist's license, and remanded the case to the Board for further proceedings.

Armes v. Kenosha County


No. 75-765


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


81 Wis. 2d 309; 260 N.W.2d 515; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1164


November 1, 1977, Argued  
December 13, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Denied, without Costs, on February 7, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from orders of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County: Harold M. Bode, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Orders reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee challenged an order of the Circuit Court for County (Wisconsin), which sustained a demurrer to the employee's complaint against respondent county on the ground that the amended complaint was not commenced within the period provided in Wis. Stat. § 59.76.


OVERVIEW: The employee was discharged from his position as a county park employee, and he was unsuccessful in his attempts to regain his employment. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 59.76, the employee filed a notice of claim against the county for wrongful discharge. The claim was disallowed by the county board. The employee appealed and claimed he was not notified of the disallowance. The trial court sustained a demurrer to the complaint on the ground that the amended complaint did not state a cause of action because the action was not commenced within the statutory period. The employee appealed and the issue presented was whether under Wis. Stat. § 59.76, the employee could commence an action against the county more than six months after the actual disallowance of the claim by the county board but within six months after the adjournment of the next annual session of the county board after the claim was filed. The court reversed and held that whether the board disallowed the claim or failed to act upon the claim, the employee was permitted under § 59.76(2) to commence his action within six months from the adjournment of the next annual session of the board after the claim was filed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that sustained the county's demurrer.
