First Nat'l Leasing Corp. v. Madison


No. 75-753


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


81 Wis. 2d 205; 260 N.W.2d 251; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1155


November 2, 1977, Argued  
December 13, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Richard W. Bardwell, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff leasing company brought an action against defendant municipality to recover property taxes it paid on equipment it leased to a hospital. The Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) entered a judgment for the leasing company and held that the equipment was exempt from property tax under Wis. Stat. § 70.11(4m). The municipality appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company leased the equipment to a non-profit hospital located within the municipality. The equipment was used exclusively by the hospital. The company, which was engaged in business for profit, depreciated the equipment for income tax purposes, and used the property as collateral for a loan. The municipality argued that the company's ownership of the equipment, and its use of the equipment for tax and financing purposes, excluded the property from the property tax exemption under Wis. Stat. § 70.11(4m), which was granted for property used exclusively by a non-profit hospital. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that requirement in § 70.11(4m) that the equipment be used exclusively by the hospital was satisfied when the property was in possession of the hospital, and was operated only by authorized hospital personnel in connection with the regular activities of a hospital. Accordingly, the equipment was exempt from taxation under § 70.11(4m). The court further held that § 70.11(4m) was a reasonable legislative classification and was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

Unified School Dist. v. Wisconsin Employment Relations Com.


No. 75-559


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


81 Wis. 2d 89; 259 N.W.2d 724; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1146; 97 L.R.R.M. 2489


November 2, 1977, Argued  
November 30, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: William C. Sachtjen, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner school district appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed the order of respondent, Wisconsin Employment Relations Commission, which found that the school district's refusal to bargain with a union constituted an unfair labor practice in violation of the Municipal Employment Relations Act, Wis. Stat. § 111.70 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The Commission ordered the school district to resume operation of the food service program, reinstate its former employees, make them whole for any losses, post a notice of compliance, and on request bargain with the union regarding both the decision to subcontract and its effect. The court held that the school district decision to subcontract its food service program was a mandatory subject of collective bargaining under Wis. Stat. § 111.70(1)(d). According to the court, the primary impact of the decision was on the conditions of employment, the decision was essentially concerned with wages and benefits, and that aspect dominated any element of policy formulation. The court also found that the MERA did not violate the "one man, one vote" principle of the Fourteenth Amendment. According to the court, every time governmental units contracted with a private party, the private party had a disproportionate interest in and influence upon the governmental decision, but this influence did not constitute a denial of equal protection. Furthermore, the court duty to bargain collectively did not require the school district to reach any agreement with the union.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.

Chicago & North Western Transp. Co. v. Pedersen


No. 75-702


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


80 Wis. 2d 566; 259 N.W.2d 316; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1215; 59 Oil & Gas Rep. 570

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surface property owners sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Bayfield County (Wisconsin), which rendered a declaratory judgment holding that Wis. Stat. § 700.30 (1973) was unconstitutional and enjoining all county registers from enforcing the act.


OVERVIEW: Respondent railroad companies claimed acres of severed mineral rights within the state and commenced a declaratory judgment action to have Wis. Stat. § 700.30 declared unconstitutional and to have its enforcement enjoined. The trial court agreed and issued a judgment holding the statute was unconstitutional because its provisions providing that mineral rights would revert to the surface owners where the rights were not registered and taxes were not paid on them was essentially taking one private owner's property for the private use of another. The surface owners, on appeal, asserted that the trial court erred in finding the statute unconstitutional and enjoining its enforcement.. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the registration fees were a tax and the enforcement provision of Wis. Stat. § 700.30 allowed for the deprivation of property without due process. The court concluded that because the enforcement provision was not severable from the statute as a whole, the entire statute failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the declaratory judgment of the trial court holding that the enforcement provision of the applicable statute was unconstitutional as violating procedural and substantive due process and enjoining its enforcement.

Abramowski v. Wm. Kilps Sons Realty, Inc.


No. 75-418


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


80 Wis. 2d 468; 259 N.W.2d 306; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1209


September 2, 1977, Argued  
November 1, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Pending. This Motion was not Decided at the Time the Volume Went to Press. Its Disposition will be Reported in a later Volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County: Howard J. Du Rocher, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order sustaining the demurrer to the complaint and dismissing the complaint is reversed and the cause remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff purchaser sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which granted a demurrer filed by defendant builder in the purchaser's action alleging that as a result of the builder's negligence, the basement walls and foundation cracked and caved in and damaged other parts of the house.


OVERVIEW: The builder contracted with the contractor and the purchaser's late husband to design and build a single family residence. The house was completed and the purchaser bought the house. The purchaser alleged that the builder negligently constructed the dwelling in that no drainage tiles were placed along the north walls, no stone was laid over the tile system around the home, and the home was constructed over an unsuitable and inadequate soil base. The purchaser further alleged that as a result of the builder's negligence, the basement walls and foundation cracked and caved in and damaged other parts of the house. The trial court sustained the demurrer filed by the builder and the court reversed. The court held that the purchaser could not base the claim on the contract because the purchaser was not a party to the contract and a contract could not be enforced by a person not a party to it. Further, the action for negligent construction was not barred by the statute of limitations because the statute did not begin to run until the purchaser suffered the injury.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order sustaining the demurrer to the complaint and dismissing the complaint.

 

391 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Sieloff v. Golz


Nos. 75-478, 75-512, 76-321


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


80 Wis. 2d 225; 258 N.W.2d 700; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1189


September 6, 1977, Submitted on Briefs; September 2, 1977, Argued  
October 18, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 75-478: Appeal from order of County Court of Columbia County: Lewis W. Charles, Judge.

No. 75-512: Error to review an order of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County: Peter G. Pappas, Circuit Judge.

No. 76-321: Appeal from an order of the County Court of Lincoln County: Donald E. Schnabel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- No. 75-478, order affirmed; No. 75-512, order reversed; No. 76-321, order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the County Court of Columbia County (Wisconsin), which quashed his writ of habeas corpus pursuant to the Uniform Criminal Extradition Act, Wis. Stat. § 976.03. The State appealed an order of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which granted a second defendant's writ of habeas. A third defendant appealed an order of the County Court of Lincoln County (Wisconsin), which denied his writ of habeas.


OVERVIEW: Defendants in three matters were subjected to extradition proceedings. Each sought habeas relief and challenged the Governor's extradition warrant. The first and third petitions were quashed. The second was granted based on the demanding state's failure to show probable cause in its affidavit. On appeal, the court affirmed the lower court's judgments in the first and the third case and reversed as to the second case, concluding that the constitutional and statutory mandates for extradition were met in all three matters. As to the first matter, the demanding state's failure to submit a warrant with its affidavit had no effect on the validity of the Governor's extradition warrant. That was so because the demanding state sufficiently showed probable cause with its affidavit. As to the second case, the demanding state's affidavit, which was in the form of a complaint, circumstantially established probable cause and satisfied the minimum requirements for complaints. In the third case, it was unnecessary to accompany a grand jury indictment with an affidavit proving probable cause. Rather, imposing such a requirement would undermine the secrecy of grand jury proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, which quashed the first defendant's habeas petition. The court reversed the lower court's judgment, which granted a second defendant's writ of habeas. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, which denied a third defendant's habeas petition.

State v. Mendoza


No. 75-806-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


80 Wis. 2d 122; 258 N.W.2d 260; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1184


June 2, 1977, Argued  
October 4, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment and orders of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Hugh R. O'Connell, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and orders reversed and cause remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) convicted defendant of two counts of first degree murder under Wis. Stat. § 940.01, for the admitted killing of two off-duty police officers. Defendant appealed the conviction, two consecutive sentences of life imprisonment, and the orders denying post-conviction motions for relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted to killing two off-duty police officers, but maintained that he had done so in self-defense. On its own motion, the trial court transferred the trial venue, over the objection of defendant and his counsel. On appeal, the court held that: (1) Wis. Const. art. I, § 7, guaranteed defendant the right to be tried in the county in which the crime was committed; (2) the only authorized change of venue under Wisconsin law was at defendant's request, under Wis. Stat. § 971.22; (3) the trial court had no authority to order a change of venue sua sponte, and the subsequent proceedings were void; (4) the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury on the theory of imperfect self-defense, embodied as the lesser-included offense of manslaughter in Wis. Stat. § 940.05, but did not err in refusing to instruct the jury on complete self-defense or heat of passion; and (5) the trial court did not err in refusing to permit defendant's experts to testify regarding the polygraph results or restricting defendant's expert testimony regarding the victims' intoxication.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction and remanded for a new trial.

Ryan v. State


No. 75-868-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


79 Wis. 2d 83; 255 N.W.2d 910; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1479


June 2, 1977, Argued  
July 1, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Errors to review an order and judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Jerold E. Murphy, Circuit Judge of the Eighteenth Circuit, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city alderman sought review of his conviction for misconduct in public office in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.12(5) entered by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin). Defendant argued that § 946.12(5) was unconstitutionally vague and unconstitutional as applied to the facts. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred by admitting his testimony from the John Doe proceeding as evidence.


OVERVIEW: After a restaurant obtained a liquor license, the restaurant owner sent defendant two gift certificates worth $ 300. When the owner later obtained a dog-grooming license, defendant was again sent two gift certificates worth $ 300. The offer and acceptance of the gift certificates came after defendant had voted. The businesses were located in defendant's political district or ward and defendant used the gift certificates. Subsequent to a John Doe proceeding, defendant was charged with violating § 946.12(5). The court held that: (1) § 946.12(5) was constitutionally specific and not vague on its face because it gave reasonable notice of the prohibited conduct; (2) any officeholder who accepted anything of value subjected himself to the possibility of prosecution; (3) defendant's use of the gift certificates violated the public trust; and (4) defendant's due process rights in the John Doe proceeding were satisfied by the presence of counsel and his right to claim the privilege against self-incrimination so defendant's testimony from that proceeding was admissible in his criminal trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

394 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Althouse v. Madison


No. 76-158


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


79 Wis. 2d 97; 255 N.W.2d 449; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1480


May 4, 1977, Submitted on Briefs  
July 1, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Richard W. Bardwell, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded with directions to the circuit court to enter the peremptory writ of mandamus to compel the common council to place the proposed ordinance on the ballot for approval or rejection at the next election as provided by the statutes.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant initiative petitioners sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Dane County (Wisconsin), which declined to grant a writ of mandamus in favor of the initiative petitioners, and refused to compel respondent city counsel to place on the ballot a referendum question.


OVERVIEW: The initiative petitioners successfully campaigned to force a "Fair Rent Ordinance" onto the ballot, in accordance with Wis. Stat. § 9.20(1). The city council refused to place the question on the ballot and claimed that the ordinance was in violation of state statutes and the state constitution. The initiative petitioners requested a writ of mandamus from the trial court. The trial court denied mandamus. The initiative petitioners sought review. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held: (1) it was not the prerogative of the city council to reach a conclusion with the respect to the unconstitutionality or invalidity of the proposed ordinance; (2) it was error for the trial judge to assume the unconstitutionality of the ordinance; (3) the only inquires permissible by either the city council or the trial judge at the mandamus hearing were in respect to whether the ordinance was legislative in nature, whether it proposed new legislation and not the repeal of existing legislation, and whether it was proper in form; and (4) the ordinance was proper, thus, the city council erred in not permitting the ordinance to go to referendum.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, granted a writ of mandamus in favor of the initiative petitioners, and ordered that the proposed ordinance be placed on the ballot as a referendum question.

 

395 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Hopper v. Madison


No. 75-143


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


79 Wis. 2d 120; 256 N.W.2d 139; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1481


May 31, 1977, Argued  
July 1, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: William C. Sachtjen, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), that granted motion of respondents, the city and others (the city), for summary judgment in the citizen's action challenging the appropriation of funds for certain programs in the city.


OVERVIEW: The citizen challenged the appropriation of funds by the city for services provided by a tenant union, an Hispanic organization, and for a day care program as expenditures of public funds for other than a public purpose. The lower court disagreed and found in favor of the city. The citizen appealed. The court affirmed. As a procedural matter, the court found that none of the affidavits in support of the citizen's motion for summary judgment met the statutory requirement that they contain evidentiary facts within the affiant's own knowledge. With respect to the appropriations, the court noted that public funds may be expended for only public purposes. An expenditure of public funds for other than a public purpose would have been abhorrent to the state constitution. The rule also applied to expenditure of public funds by municipalities. The court concluded that the challenged appropriations were not made contrary to the law. They constituted expenditure of funds for public purposes by promoting the health and general welfare of the public. The trial court correctly granted the city's motion for summary judgment dismissing the citizen's action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the city's motion for summary judgment dismissing the citizen's action challenging the appropriation of funds by the city.

 

396 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Tisdale v. Hasslinger


No. 75-616


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


79 Wis. 2d 194; 255 N.W.2d 314; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1485


June 2, 1977, Submitted on Briefs  
July 1, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dodge County: Henry G. Gergen, Jr., Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin), which granted respondent insurance company's motion for summary judgment in respondent minor employee's action against the employer for injuries sustained by the employee while working on the employer's farm.


OVERVIEW: The employee was 11 years old and working on the employer's farm for one day when he was injured. The company refused to cover the injury, claiming that it fell within an exclusion in the employer's policy for any farm employee employed in violation of the law as to age. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the company. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the minor's injury was not one of the risks the company undertook to insure. The court noted that at the time the insurance policy was issued, there was no minimum age for farm employment. The court further noted that Wis. Stat. § 103.67(2), which set a minimum age for employment, and Wis. Adm. Code § Ind 70.06(22), which prohibited a child under 16 from assisting in the operation of a tractor, became effective prior to the date on which the employee was hired. The court concluded that the exclusion in the policy looked to the date of employment of the minor to determine whether his employment was in violation of the law. The court found that, on the date he was hired, the employee's employment was in violation of § 103.67(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting summary judgment in favor of the insurance company.

 

397 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Terry v. Kolski


No. 75-249


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


78 Wis. 2d 475; 254 N.W.2d 704; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1260


March 2, 1977, Argued  
June 14, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: John A. Decker, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed, and cause remanded to the circuit court, with directions to remand to the county court for further proceedings on the complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision that dismissed his small claims court action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against respondent sheriff.


OVERVIEW: The inmate brought a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action in small claims court when copies of adult magazines were seized from his prison cell and destroyed. The inmate alleged that the acts deprived him of his First Amendment rights. The county court's dismissal of the action for failure to state a cause of action under state law was affirmed on appeal to the circuit court, which upon rehearing concluded that a § 1983 action would be cognizable in a state court only where it was pendent to a state action. On appeal, the court reversed. The small claims court had jurisdiction over the action. U.S. Const. art. VI, para. 2 not only permitted state courts to exercise jurisdiction in enforcement of federal laws to the extent permitted by Congress but mandated that federal causes of action and federal rights, unless exclusively reserved to the federal courts, were required to be enforced by state courts. The provision in 28 U.S.C.S. § 1343(3) for "original jurisdiction" in the district courts was not to be equated with exclusive jurisdiction. It was in fact a statement of congressional intent that exclusive jurisdiction was not intended.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that affirmed a decision that dismissed his small claims court § 1983 action against the sheriff. The matter was remanded with directions to remand to the county court for further proceedings on the complaint.

 

398 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Harrison v. State


No. 75-763-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


78 Wis. 2d 189; 254 N.W.2d 220; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1239


March 30, 1977, Submitted on Briefs  
June 1, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Writs of Error to review a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Adams County: Lowell D. Schoengarth, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the Circuit Court for Adams County (Wisconsin) for endangering the safety of another by conduct regardless of life in contravention of Wis. Stat. § 941.30 and attempted first degree murder in contravention of Wis. Stat. §§ 939.32, 940.01. He was sentenced to 3 years on the first count and 15 years on the second, with the sentences to be served concurrently.


OVERVIEW: After an altercation with the victims earlier in the day, defendant and an cohort found the victims at a bar, and another altercation ensued, ending in one victim being shot in the leg and the other being shot in the back. The cohort pled guilty and received a suspended sentence. On the assurance that he would face no further charges, the cohort gave testimony at defendant's trial that inculpated himself and fully exculpated defendant. The jury obviously did not believe his testimony because it found defendant guilty. The trial court then denied defendant's post-conviction motion alleging ineffective assistance of counsel because his trial attorney had also represented the cohort prior in his plea. The trial court made specific findings that trial counsel had meticulously and capably tried the case and thus fully discharged his duty to defendant. The court affirmed, finding that defendant had not met his burden of proving by clear and convincing evidence that there was either dual representation or a conflict of interest between the cohort and defendant. The mere potentiality for conflict or prejudice was insufficient, and an actual conflict was not shown.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's convictions of defendant for endangering the safety of another by conduct regardless of life and attempted first degree murder.

 

399 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Harris v. State


No. 75-893-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


78 Wis. 2d 357; 254 N.W.2d 291; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1253


February 2, 1977, Argued  
June 1, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Rehearing Denied, without Costs, on July 19, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Error to review a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Victor Manian, Acting Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order modified and as modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of one count of abduction, two counts of sexual perversion, and one count of obstructing an officer.


OVERVIEW: According to the State defendant and a co-defendant forced the victim in the car where she was beaten, forcibly detained, and forced to commit acts of oral sodomy on each man. Defendant and co-defendant contended that the victim was a willing occupant, and that no sexual activity occurred. The court held the crimes of abduction and sexual perversion constituted different crimes with similar acts, but not identical elements thus defendant's charge and convictions for both crimes was proper. The court further held that the abduction statute was not unconstitutionally vague because men of common intelligence did not necessarily have to guess as to the meaning of "detain" under Wis. Stat. § 940.32. Although the court held that it was improper to have allowed co-defendant's counsel to testify it was not prejudicial because it was brief and collateral. Finally, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in failing to order a presentence investigation, However, the court held that trial court failed to credit defendant with 112 days of pre-conviction jail time on three of the fours counts.


OUTCOME: The court modified the sentence crediting each count defendant was convicted of with 112 days of pre-conviction jail time. The court affirmed the judgment as modified.

 

400 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Nodell Inv. Corp. v. Glendale


No. 75-506


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


78 Wis. 2d 416; 254 N.W.2d 310; 1977 Wisc. LEXIS 1256


May 3, 1977, Argued  
June 1, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Harvey Neelen, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which held that because the property owners had failed to exhaust administrative remedies under Wis. Stat. § 62.23(7)(e), the court did not possess subject matter jurisdiction. The property owners wished to challenge the administration of respondent city's zoning ordinance without first appealing to the zoning board of appeals.


OVERVIEW: The property owners brought a declaratory judgment action in 1975 seeking to have their 1956 and 1966 deeds to the city declared null and void. They alleged that the plan commission's administration of the city building permit ordinance violated the constitutional guarantees of equal protection of the laws and just compensation for private property taken for public use. The trial court sustained demurrers to the complaint, and the property owners appealed. The court held that the property owners, having failed to utilize available administrative remedies provided by law, were precluded from judicial relief. The city's board of appeals had the power to invalidate the conditions imposed by the plan commission and to afford relief to the property owners without invalidating the ordinance itself. The property owners did not challenge the validity of the plan commission's conditional building permits issued to them before the board of appeals. The court held that because the property owners failed to follow the required statutory procedure, the court below had no jurisdiction, and should have dismissed the action on that ground.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court, which held that the property owners were precluded from judicial relief, was affirmed.
